Ruling on Wages for Hijamah and Stud Fee
States ruling on hijamah and 'asb al-tays with proofs and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for hijamah and 'asb al-tays, explain the proof and the abrogation argument against the Zahiri position, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference on mahr al-bagh.

Core Idea
Cupping wages permissible by prophetic practice and ijma; stud fee prohibited because the service cannot be garantied and the consideration is impure.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses two controversial earnings: wages for cupping (hijamah) and the stud fee of a ram ('asb al-tays). The Hanafi school permits the former based on the Prophet's own practice and consensus, while prohibiting the latter due to the impossibility of guaranteeing the service. The passage also discusses an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the 'dower of a prostitute' (mahr al-bagh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings and their hukm levels
First, note that the passage gives a ruling for cupping wages (permissible, mubah) and for stud fee (prohibited, haram).
2
Locate the Hanafi proof for cupping wages
The author cites the Prophet's own practice of being cupped and paying wages, plus continuous custom forming ijma. The Zahiri objection is based on a hadith that seems to prohibit earnings of cupper.
3
Analyze the abrogation (naskh) argument
The Hanafi response is that the prohibiting hadith is abrogated by a later hadith where the Prophet permits feeding one's family from a cupper's earnings. Understand why naskh applies.
The abrogating hadith is considered later in time.
4
Examine the proof for prohibition of stud fee
The Prophet called the stud fee 'usury' (suh't). Additionally, the service (impregnation) cannot be garantied, and the payment is for an impure substance (semen).
The impossibility of garantying makes the contract void.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on mahr al-bagh
The passage reports that Abu Hanifa allows taking money from a corrupt hire for fornication, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad forbid it. Understand the basis: Hanafi view focuses on the contract rather than the cause.
This is a subsidiary point within the discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجام أي جاز أخذ أجرة الحجام لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام احتجم وأعطى أجرته وبه جرى التعارف بين الناس من لدن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى يومنا هذا فانعقد إجماعاً. وقالت الظاهرية : لا يجوز لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن عسب التيس وكسب الحجام وقفيز الطحان قلنا هذا الحديث منسوخ لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال له رجل: إن لي عيالاً وغلاماً حجاماً أفأطعم عيالي من كسبه؟ قال: نعم. وإنما فسرنا الصحة بالجواز لأن العادة جارية هنا وفيما بعده لعدم جريان عقد فيه . قال لا أجرة عسب التيس يعني لا يجوز أخذ أجرة عسب التيس لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام إن السحت عسب التيس مهر البغي ولأنه عمل لا يقدر عليه وهو الإحبال فلا يجوز أخذ الأجرة عليه ولا أخذ المال بمقابلة الماء وهو نجس لا قيمة له فلا يجوز . والمراد هنا استئجار التيس لينزو على الغنم ويحبلها بأجر، أما لو فعل ذلك من غير لا بأس به لأن به يبقى النسل. وفي المحيط : ومهر البغي في الحديث وهو أن يؤاجر أمته على الزنا وما أخذه من المهر فهو حرام عندهما، وعند الإمام إن أخذه بغير عقد بأن زنى بأمته ثم أعطاها شيئاً فهو حرام لأنه أخذه بغير حق، وإن استأجرها ليزني بها ثم أعطاها مهرها أو ما شرط لها لا بأس بأخذه لأنه في إجارة فاسدة فيطيب له وإن كان السبب حراماً
And [the ruling on] the cupper: it is permissible to take wages for cupping because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was cupped and gave his wage, and custom has continued among people from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to this day, so consensus has formed. The Zahiris said: it is not permissible because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the stud fee of the ram, the earnings of the cupper, and the measure of the miller. We say this hadith is abrogated because it is narrated that a man said to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I have dependents and a slave who is a cupper; may I feed my family from his earnings?' He said: 'Yes.' And we interpret validity as permissibility because custom is current here and hereafter due to the absence of a contract in it. He said: (no wage for the stud fee of the ram) i.e., it is not permissible to take wages for the stud fee of the ram due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'The usury is the stud fee of the ram, the dower of the prostitute,' and because it is an action that cannot be performed, namely impregnation, so it is not permissible to take wages for it, nor is it permissible to take money in exchange for water which is impure and has no value. What is meant here is hiring the ram to mount sheep and impregnate them for a wage; as for doing it without [a wage], there is no harm because through it progeny remains. In al-Muhit: The dower of the prostitute in the hadith is that he hires out his slave woman for fornication, and what he takes as dower is forbidden according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), if he takes it without a contract, i.e., he fornicates with his slave woman and then gives her something, it is forbidden because he took it without right; but if he hires her to fornicate with her and then gives her her dower or what he stipulated, there is no harm in taking it because it is a corrupt hire, so it is permissible for him even though the cause is forbidden.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of taking wages for cupping (hijamah) and the prohibition of taking wages for the stud fee of a ram ('asb al-tays). The author begins by stating that taking wages for cupping is permissible, citing the Prophet's own practice and the continuous custom from his time until today, which constitutes consensus (ijma). The Zahiri school objects using a hadith prohibiting earnings from cupping, but the Hanafi response is that the hadith is abrogated by another hadith where the Prophet permits feeding one's family from a cupper's earnings. The term 'validity' is interpreted as 'permissibility' because cupping usually involves no explicit contract but follows custom. Then the author addresses the stud fee: it is prohibited because the Prophet called it 'usury' (suh't), and because the action (impregnation) is not a service that can be guaranteed, and the payment is in exchange for water (semen) which is impure and valueless. However, if the ram is used without a wage, it is permissible. The passage also discusses the 'dower of a prostitute' (mahr al-bagh), with a intra-Hanafi difference: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, taking money for hiring out a slave woman for fornication is forbidden; according to Abu Hanifa, if done through a corrupt contract, the money is permissible (tayyib) to the taker, though the act is sinful. This shows the Hanafi focus on the contract rather than the cause.

Key Terms
الحجام (al-hajjam): The cupper, one who performs hijamah (cupping therapy).
عسب التيس (asb al-tays): The stud fee of a ram, i.e., wage paid for allowing a ram to mate.
مهر البغي (mahr al-bagh): The dower of a prostitute, i.e., wage for fornication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on taking wages for cupping (hijamah)?
A) It is prohibited because of the hadith forbidding earnings of the cupper.
B) It is permissible based on the Prophet's own practice and ijma.
C) It is permissible only if the cupper is a slave.
D) It is makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
Cupping wages are halal by consensus and prophetic practice; stud fees are haram by clear prohibition and contractual impossibility.

Hiring for Acts of Worship: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on hiring for devotional acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits hiring for acts of worship and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
You cannot sell an act of worship — its reward belongs to the doer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the Hanafi position on hiring for acts of worship (adhan, Hajj, imamah, teaching Quran/fiqh) and engages with the Shafi'i school's opposing view. The dispute hinges on whether devotional acts are delegable and whether the service can be guaranteed. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: acts of worship are not commodities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its scope
State which acts are prohibited for hiring according to the Hanafi school: adhan, Hajj, leading prayer, teaching Quran, and teaching fiqh. Note that the prohibition is restricted to 'acts of worship' (af'al al-ṭa'ah).
Teaching worldly subjects like writing, grammar, or medicine is permissible by consensus.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Locate the two hadiths cited: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat by it' and 'Do not take wages for the adhan.' Also understand the rational argument: the reward of a devotional act goes to the doer, so taking wages would be akin to selling the reward.
Hanafi usul considers these hadiths as strong evidence against hiring for worship.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes to permissible hiring for building mosques, paying zakat, writing the Quran, and teaching fiqh. He argues that being a devotional act does not preclude hiring, as seen in those examples.
The Shafi'i position relies on qiyas and a broader view of what can be contracted.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish: building a mosque and writing the Quran are not purely devotional or are delegable; acts like prayer and fasting are not delegable. Teaching Quran and fiqh involve an uncertain outcome (learning depends on the student), so the contract is void due to gharar.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says contract fasid (corrupt), Shafi'i says valid and wages due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والأذان والحج والإمامة وتعليم القرآن والفقه) يعني لا يجوز استئجار هذه الأشياء. وقال الإمام الشافعي : يجوز لأنه استئجار على عمل غير متعين عليه وكونه عبارة لا ينافي ذلك ألا ترى أنه يجوز الاستئجار على بناء المسجد وأداء الزكاة وكتابة المصحف والفقه ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام أقرؤوا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لعثمان بن أبي وقاص : لا تأخذ على الأذان أجراً. ولأن القربة تقع للعامل فلا يجوز أخذ الأجر على عمل وقع له كما في الصوم والصلاة، ولأن التعليم مما لا يقدر عليه المعلم إلا بمعنى من جهة المتعلم فيكون ملتزماً ما لا يقدر على تسليمه فلا يجوز بخلاف بناء المسجد وأداء الزكاة وكتابة المصحح والفقه فإنه يقدر عليها الأجير وكذا الأجير يكون للآمر لوقوع الفعل عنه نيابة، ولهذا لا تشترط أهلية المأمور فيهما بل أهلية الأمر حتى جاز أن يستأجر الكافي فيهما ولا يجوز فيما نحن فيه؛ كذا قالوا . وينتقض هذا بما ذكروا في باب الحج عن الغير أن الحج يقع عن الأمر وأن للإنسان أن يجعل ثواب عمله لغيره. قيد بأفعال الطاعة لأنه لو استأجره ليعلم ولده الكتابة أو النحو أو الطب أو التعبير يجوز بالاتفاق؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وفي الكبرى : تعليم الفرائض والحساب والوصايا بأجر يجوز. وفي الذخيرة لو استأجره ليعلم ولده الشعر والأدب إذا بين له مدة جاز ويستحق المسمى إذا سلم نفسه تعلم أو لم يتعلم، وإذا لم يذكر له مدة فالعقد فاسد ويستحق أجرة المثل إذا تعلم .اهـ. وفيها أيضاً : ويجوز الاستئجار على تعليم الصنعة والتجارة والهدم والبناء والحفر وأشباه ذلك، فإذا أجره عبده ليعلمه كذا على إعطاء المولى شيئاً معيناً فهو جائز، وإن شرط المعلم على المولى أن يعطيه في كل شهر كذا ويقوم على غلامه في تعليم كذا فهو جائز، وإذا لم يشترط كل واحد منهما شيئاً فلما فرغ وتعلم قال المعلم لي الأجرة على رب العبد كذا وقال سيد العبد لي الأجرة على المعلم ينظر في ذلك إلى عرف تلك البلدة؛ فإن كان سيد العبد هو الذي يعطي فالأجرة عليه، وإن كان المعلم هو الذي يعطي فالأجرة على المعلم اهـ.
He (the author) said: (And the call to prayer, and Hajj, and leading the prayer, and teaching the Quran and jurisprudence) meaning it is not permissible to hire for these things. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible because it is hiring for an action that is not individually obligatory, and being a devotional act does not negate that; do you not see that hiring for building a mosque, performing zakat, writing the Quran, and jurisprudence is permissible? And we have his saying (peace be upon him): 'Recite the Quran and do not eat by it,' and he said (peace be upon him) to Uthman ibn Abi Qas: 'Do not take wages for the call to prayer.' And because the reward goes to the doer, so it is not permissible to take wages for an action that accrues to him, as in fasting and prayer. And because teaching is something the teacher cannot perform except with a meaning from the student, so he is committing to something he cannot deliver, so it is not permissible, unlike building a mosque, performing zakat, writing the Quran and jurisprudence, for the hireling is able to do them, and similarly the hireling acts on behalf of the employer by proxy, and for this reason the qualification of the subordinate is not required, only that of the employer, so much so that it is permissible to hire an unbeliever for them, and it is not permissible in what we are discussing; so they said. And this is contradicted by what they mentioned in the chapter on Hajj on behalf of another: that Hajj occurs on behalf of the one for whom it is performed, and that a person can give the reward of his action to another. It is restricted to acts of worship because if he hires him to teach his child writing, grammar, medicine, or dream interpretation, it is permissible by agreement; thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And in al-Kubra: Teaching farai'd, calculation, and bequests for wages is permissible. And in al-Dhakhira: If he hires him to teach his child poetry and literature, if he specifies a duration, it is permissible and he is entitled to the named wage if he makes himself available whether the child learns or not; if he does not specify a duration, the contract is corrupt and he is entitled to the counterpart wage if there is learning. And in it also: Hiring for teaching a craft, trade, demolition, construction, digging, and the like is permissible. So if he hires out his slave to teach him for a specified payment from the master, it is permissible; and if the teacher stipulates on the master to give him something each month and to take care of his servant in teaching, it is permissible; and if none of them stipulates anything, then when the slave finishes and learns, if the teacher says 'the wage is due from the master' and the slave's master says 'the wage is due from the teacher,' then the custom of that town is looked to: if it is the master who gives, the wage is on him; if it is the teacher who gives, the wage is on the teacher.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding hiring for acts of worship. The author states the Hanafi ruling: it is not permissible to hire for adhan, Hajj, leading prayer, teaching Quran, and teaching fiqh, because these are purely devotional acts (qurbat) where the reward goes to the doer, and teaching Quran and fiqh cannot be guaranteed since learning depends on the student. The Shafi'i school permits such hiring by analogy to permissible hiring for building mosques, paying zakat, writing Quran, and teaching fiqh. The Hanafi response provides proofs: the hadith 'Recite Quran and do not eat by it' and the Prophet's instruction to Uthman not to take wages for adhan. The Hanafis argue that the examples given by Shafi'i are different because those actions (building, writing) are not purely devotional and can be delegated, whereas acts of worship are not delegable in the same way. A potential objection regarding Hajj on behalf of another is answered: Hajj by proxy is a separate issue. The passage then clarifies that the prohibition is restricted to acts of worship; teaching worldly subjects like writing, grammar, medicine, crafts, etc. is permissible by consensus. The text also addresses practical scenarios, such as hiring a slave to teach, with detailed rulings on when the wage is due based on custom and stipulation.

Key Terms
أفعال الطاعة (af'al al-ṭa'ah): Acts of obedience/worship; the context restricts the prohibition to these.
الاستئجار (al-isti'jar): Hiring for a service; the legal discussion is about the validity of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hiring for teaching the Quran not permissible?
A) Because the Quran is too sacred to be exchanged for money.
B) Because teaching is a devotional act and the reward goes to the teacher, and the service cannot be guaranteed.
C) Because the Prophet forbade any payment for religious knowledge.
D) Because the teacher must do it for free to gain reward.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits hiring for acts of worship due to the non-delegable nature of devotional acts and uncertainty in teaching, while permitting hiring for worldly services.

The Contemporary Fatwa on Hiring for Quran Teaching
Contemporary fatwa allowing wages for Quran teaching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why later Hanafi scholars permitted hiring for Quran teaching and identify the role of istihsan in changing rulings.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa can change with time; istihsan allowed wages for Quran teaching to preserve the Quran.

This lesson examines a pivotal shift in Hanafi fiqh: the permissibility of hiring teachers for Quran instruction. The author presents the fatwa of later scholars from Balkh who used istihsan to overrule the earlier prohibition, basing their decision on changed social and economic circumstances. You will see how rulings adapt to preserve religious practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (permissible/impermissible)? The act is hiring a teacher to teach the Quran. The ruling is permissibility (mubah) according to the contemporary fatwa.
The ruling is from the later scholars, not the early ones.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited for this permissibility? The text says 'istihsan' (juristic preference) based on the principle that rulings change with time (taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman) and the necessity to preserve the Quran.
Istihsan is a subsidiary source in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof lead to the ruling? Earlier, teachers received stipends from the treasury and gifts from students; now they lack such support. If wages were not allowed, Quran teaching would cease, leading to loss of the Quran. Istihsan overrides the original analogy that teaching is a non-compensable act.
The key link is changed custom and necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Who disagreed? The earlier Hanafi scholars (and some later individuals like Muhammad ibn al-Fadl who made wages obligatory) held different views. The text presents the earlier position as prohibition and the later as permissibility.
Muhammad ibn al-Fadl's view is stricter: wages are obligatory, not just permissible.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Which position is relied upon for fatwa today? The author sides with the later scholars' fatwa, making the mufta bihi permissibility. This is based on the consensus of the later Balkh scholars and the underlying necessity.
The tarjih authority is the author's own choice, supported by the principle of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن) وهذا مذهب المتأخرين من مشايخ بلخ، استحسنوا ذلك وقالوا بنى أصحابنا المتقدمون الجواب على ما قلة الحفاظ ورغبة الناس فيهم ولأن الحفاظ والمعلمين كان لهم عطايا في بيت المال وافتقادات من المتعلمين في مجازات التعليم من غير شرط وهذا الزمان قل ذلك واشتغل الحفاظ بمعائشهم فلو لم يفتح لهم باب التعليم بالأجر لذهب القرآن فأفتوا بالجواز، والأحكام تختلف باختلاف الزمان، وكان محمد بن الفضل يفتي بأن الأجرة تجب ويحبس عليها. وفي الخلاصة : إذا أخذ المعلم من الصبي شيئاً من المأكول أو دفع الصبي ذلك إلى ولد المعلم لا يحل له بخلاف ثمن الحصر لأن ذلك تمليك من أب الصغير اهـ. وفي الحاوي للكرابيسي: إذا استأجره ليختم عنده القرآن ولم يسم له أجراً ليس له أن يأخذ أقل خمسة وأربعين درهماً شرعاً، أما إذا سمى أجراً لزم ما سمى لكن يأثم المستأجر إذا عقد على أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً إلا أن المستأجر ما بقي من تمام القدر أو يشترط أن يكون ثواب ما فوقه لنفسه فلا يأثم وكذا إذا قال اقرأ بقدر ما قدرت عليه فله بقدر ما قرأ وهذا يجب حفظه كما في المبسوط أقول: وهذا في عرفهم، أما في عرفنا فيجوز ذلك. وفي الخلاصة : رجل استأجر قوماً يحملون جنازة ويغسلون ميتاً إن كان في موضع لا يجد من يغسله غيرهم ولا من يحمله فلا أجر لهم، وإن كان هناك غيرهم فلهم الأجر اهـ. وفي المحيط : استأجر الإمام رجلاً ليقتل مرتداً أو أسيراً أو لاستيفاء القصاص في النفس لم يجز عندهما، ولو استأجره لاستيفاء القصاص فيما دون النفس يجوز، ولو استأجر من الأجر
He (the author) said: And the fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran. And this is the madhhab of the later scholars from the scholars of Balkh; they deemed it good (istihsan) and said: Our earlier scholars based the answer on the scarcity of memorizers and the people's desire for them, and because the memorizers and teachers used to receive gifts from the treasury and offerings from students without stipulation, and in this time the situation has decreased and the memorizers are occupied with their livelihoods, so if the door of teaching for wages were not opened for them, the Quran would be lost. So they gave a fatwa of permissibility, and rulings differ with the difference of time. And Muhammad ibn al-Fadl used to give fatwa that wages are owed and are enforceable. In al-Khulasa: If the teacher takes from the child some food, or the child gives it to the teacher's child, it is not permissible for him, unlike the price of a mat, because that is a transfer of ownership from the father of the minor. In al-Hawi al-Karabisi: If he hires him to complete the Quran before him without naming a wage, he is not entitled to take less than forty-five dirhams by sacred law; but if he names a wage, what he names is binding, but the hirer sins if he contracts for less than forty-five dirhams, unless the hirer deducts some of the full amount or stipulates that the reward for the excess be for himself, then he does not sin; similarly if he says 'recite as much as you can,' then he gets what he recited, and this must be memorized as in al-Mabsut. I say: This is according to their custom; as for our custom, that is permissible. And in al-Khulasa: A man hired a group to carry a corpse and wash the dead; if it is a place where no one else is found to wash or carry, there is no wage for them; but if others are there, they have a wage. And in al-Muhit: If the imam hires a man to kill an apostate or a prisoner, or to carry out retaliation in homicide, it is not permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); but if he hires him to carry out retaliation for injury less than homicide, it is permissible; and if he hires [from the wage?]...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents a contemporary fatwa that permits hiring for teaching the Quran, a departure from the earlier ruling. The later Hanafi scholars of Balkh used istihsan (juristic preference) based on changed circumstances: in earlier times, Quran teachers received stipends from the treasury and gifts from students, so there was no need to hire them. But in later times, such support diminished, and teachers needed to earn a living; without allowing wages, the teaching of the Quran might cease, leading to its loss. Hence the ruling was relaxed. The author also cites Muhammad ibn al-Fadl who held that such wages are obligatory and enforceable. Additional rulings include: a teacher cannot accept food from a student without permission from the father; a minimum wage of 45 dirhams is recommended for completing a Quran recitation, though one can stipulate otherwise; hiring for carrying funeral bier and washing the dead is only compensable if other laborers are available; and hiring an imam to execute a criminal is invalid for capital punishment but valid for lesser injuries. This shows that even within the Hanafi school, later jurists adapted rulings to social needs.

Key Terms
الفتوى اليوم (al-fatwa al-yawm): The authoritative opinion in the present time, indicating a shift from earlier rulings.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; the method used by later scholars to permit hiring for Quran teaching despite earlier prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the later Hanafi scholars of Balkh issue a fatwa allowing wages for teaching the Quran?
A) Because they disagreed with the earlier prohibition entirely.
B) Because teachers were no longer supported by the treasury and needed wages to survive, otherwise Quran would be lost.
C) Because the Prophet had told Uthman to take wages for adhan.
D) Because the Shafi'i school convinced them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to adapt rulings to changing circumstances, as shown by the contemporary fatwa permitting wages for Quran teaching.

Additional Ijara Rulings: Teacher's Perks, Minimum Wage, Funeral Services, and Execution Contract
Collection of ijara rulings with custom and necessity considerations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi principles of custom (urf) and necessity to various hire (ijara) scenarios, such as teacher acceptance of gifts, minimum wage for Quran completion, hiring for funeral services, and contracting an executioner.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, permissibility of hire contracts often depends on local custom and the availability of alternatives.

This lesson expands on the theme of ijara by presenting several practical rulings from the same source. You will see how the author applies the maxims of custom and necessity to distinct cases: what a teacher may accept from a student, the minimum customary wage for completing a Quran recitation, the entitlement of funeral workers, and the validity of hiring a person to execute a legal punishment. These cases illustrate the principle that rulings are not absolute but contextual.

Guided Path
1
List the scenarios presented
There are four distinct scenarios: (1) teacher taking food from student, (2) hiring to complete Quran without stipulating wage, (3) hiring to carry funeral and wash the dead, (4) imam hiring someone to kill an apostate/prisoner or carry out qisas.
Each scenario has its own ruling and rationale.
2
For each case, identify the ruling
Determine whether the action is permissible, prohibited, or conditional. For example, taking food from the student is impermissible unless it is from the father's property; the minimum wage for Quran completion is 45 dirhams by custom; funeral workers get no wage if no other workers exist; execution contract is invalid for capital cases but valid for lesser injuries.
Some rulings are from earlier authorities (Karabisi, Khulasa, etc.).
3
Identify the underlying legal reason (illa/urf)
For each case, ask: what custom or principle drives the ruling? The teacher's food is impermissible because it is not a proper wage; the 45 dirhams is based on the custom of Basra; funeral workers get no wage because the duty is communal (fard kifaya); execution contract is invalid because it resembles hiring for something that is not a service.
The author also notes that rulings differ with custom: 'this is according to their custom; as for our custom, that is permissible.'
4
Apply the principle of taghayyur al-ahkam
Notice that the author explicitly distinguishes between the custom of earlier times and his own time. The ruling on minimum wage, for example, may change if the custom changes. This reinforces the lesson from the main fatwa.
The principle of changing rulings with changing times applies to all these cases.

قال رحمه الله : والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن) وهذا مذهب المتأخرين من مشايخ بلخ، استحسنوا ذلك وقالوا بنى أصحابنا المتقدمون الجواب على ما قلة الحفاظ ورغبة الناس فيهم ولأن الحفاظ والمعلمين كان لهم عطايا في بيت المال وافتقادات من المتعلمين في مجازات التعليم من غير شرط وهذا الزمان قل ذلك واشتغل الحفاظ بمعائشهم فلو لم يفتح لهم باب التعليم بالأجر لذهب القرآن فأفتوا بالجواز، والأحكام تختلف باختلاف الزمان، وكان محمد بن الفضل يفتي بأن الأجرة تجب ويحبس عليها. وفي الخلاصة : إذا أخذ المعلم من الصبي شيئاً من المأكول أو دفع الصبي ذلك إلى ولد المعلم لا يحل له بخلاف ثمن الحصر لأن ذلك تمليك من أب الصغير اهـ. وفي الحاوي للكرابيسي: إذا استأجره ليختم عنده القرآن ولم يسم له أجراً ليس له أن يأخذ أقل خمسة وأربعين درهماً شرعاً، أما إذا سمى أجراً لزم ما سمى لكن يأثم المستأجر إذا عقد على أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً إلا أن المستأجر ما بقي من تمام القدر أو يشترط أن يكون ثواب ما فوقه لنفسه فلا يأثم وكذا إذا قال اقرأ بقدر ما قدرت عليه فله بقدر ما قرأ وهذا يجب حفظه كما في المبسوط أقول: وهذا في عرفهم، أما في عرفنا فيجوز ذلك. وفي الخلاصة : رجل استأجر قوماً يحملون جنازة ويغسلون ميتاً إن كان في موضع لا يجد من يغسله غيرهم ولا من يحمله فلا أجر لهم، وإن كان هناك غيرهم فلهم الأجر اهـ. وفي المحيط : استأجر الإمام رجلاً ليقتل مرتداً أو أسيراً أو لاستيفاء القصاص في النفس لم يجز عندهما، ولو استأجره لاستيفاء القصاص فيما دون النفس يجوز، ولو استأجر من الأجر
He (the author) said: And the fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran. And this is the madhhab of the later scholars from the scholars of Balkh; they deemed it good (istihsan) and said: Our earlier scholars based the answer on the scarcity of memorizers and the people's desire for them, and because the memorizers and teachers used to receive gifts from the treasury and offerings from students without stipulation, and in this time the situation has decreased and the memorizers are occupied with their livelihoods, so if the door of teaching for wages were not opened for them, the Quran would be lost. So they gave a fatwa of permissibility, and rulings differ with the difference of time. And Muhammad ibn al-Fadl used to give fatwa that wages are owed and are enforceable. In al-Khulasa: If the teacher takes from the child some food, or the child gives it to the teacher's child, it is not permissible for him, unlike the price of a mat, because that is a transfer of ownership from the father of the minor. In al-Hawi al-Karabisi: If he hires him to complete the Quran before him without naming a wage, he is not entitled to take less than forty-five dirhams by sacred law; but if he names a wage, what he names is binding, but the hirer sins if he contracts for less than forty-five dirhams, unless the hirer deducts some of the full amount or stipulates that the reward for the excess be for himself, then he does not sin; similarly if he says 'recite as much as you can,' then he gets what he recited, and this must be memorized as in al-Mabsut. I say: This is according to their custom; as for our custom, that is permissible. And in al-Khulasa: A man hired a group to carry a corpse and wash the dead; if it is a place where no one else is found to wash or carry, there is no wage for them; but if others are there, they have a wage. And in al-Muhit: If the imam hires a man to kill an apostate or a prisoner, or to carry out retaliation in homicide, it is not permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); but if he hires him to carry out retaliation for injury less than homicide, it is permissible; and if he hires [from the wage?]...

Commentary
This passage presents a contemporary fatwa that permits hiring for teaching the Quran, a departure from the earlier ruling. The later Hanafi scholars of Balkh used istihsan (juristic preference) based on changed circumstances: in earlier times, Quran teachers received stipends from the treasury and gifts from students, so there was no need to hire them. But in later times, such support diminished, and teachers needed to earn a living; without allowing wages, the teaching of the Quran might cease, leading to its loss. Hence the ruling was relaxed. The author also cites Muhammad ibn al-Fadl who held that such wages are obligatory and enforceable. Additional rulings include: a teacher cannot accept food from a student without permission from the father; a minimum wage of 45 dirhams is recommended for completing a Quran recitation, though one can stipulate otherwise; hiring for carrying funeral bier and washing the dead is only compensable if other laborers are available; and hiring an imam to execute a criminal is invalid for capital punishment but valid for lesser injuries. This shows that even within the Hanafi school, later jurists adapted rulings to social needs.

Key Terms
الخلاصة (al-Khulasa): A Hanafi fiqh text used as a source for the rulings on teacher's gifts and funeral hire.
الحاوي (al-Hawi): A work by al-Karabisi, cited for the ruling on minimum wage for Quran completion.
المحيط (al-Muhit): A Hanafi reference cited for rulings on hiring an executioner.

Hiring for Teaching the Quran: From Prohibition to Permissibility
Commentary on the permissibility and conditions of hiring for teaching

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the shift in the Hanafi position on hiring for teaching the Quran and apply the concept of istihsan to similar evolving cases.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa on hiring for teaching the Quran changed from prohibition to permissibility via istihsan, preserving the Quran in changing times.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq illustrates a classic evolution in Hanafi fiqh: the ruling on hiring for teaching the Quran. Early Hanafis deemed it invalid because the benefit of teaching is intangible and cannot be delivered in a single instant. Later scholars, observing that state support for Quran memorizers had dried up and the Quran was at risk of being lost, used istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it. This lesson unpacks that legal reasoning and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
Determine what early Hanafis ruled regarding hiring for teaching the Quran and their basis (qiyas on intangible benefits).
The original Zahir al-Riwayah position is invalidity.
2
Understand the objection and response
Examine the objection that teaching cannot be hired because the benefit is not deliverable, and the response that the actual benefit is the teaching act (talqin), not the learning.
This response reframes the benefit as deliverable.
3
Recognize the role of istihsan
Analyze how later Hanafis used istihsan to override qiyas, citing changed circumstances (loss of stipends, need to preserve Quran).
Istihsan is a source of law in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Use the same framework (qiyas vs. istihsan) to evaluate other modern scenarios, such as hiring for online Quran teaching.
The principles of necessity and custom can update rulings.

كتاب الإجارة باب الإجارة الفاسدة
لتعليم القرآن ولا يجوز على الغناء والنوح والملاهي وفسد إجارة المشاع إلا من الشريك
نحن فيه؛ كذا قالوا . وينتقض هذا بما ذكروا في باب الحج عن الغير أن الحج يقع عن الأمر وأن للإنسان أن يجعل ثواب عمله لغيره. قيد بأفعال الطاعة لأنه لو استأجره ليعلم ولده الكتابة أو النحو أو الطب أو التعبير يجوز بالاتفاق ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وفي الكبرى : تعليم الفرائض والحساب والوصايا بأجر يجوز. وفي الذخيرة لو استأجره ليعلم ولده الشعر والأدب إذا بين له مدة جاز ويستحق المسمى إذا سلم نفسه تعلم أو لم يتعلم، وإذا لم يذكر له مدة فالعقد فاسد ويستحق أجرة المثل إذا تعلم .اهـ. وفيها أيضاً : ويجوز الاستئجار على تعليم الصنعة والتجارة والهدم والبناء والحفر وأشباه ذلك، فإذا أجره عبده ليعلمه كذا على إعطاء المولى شيئاً معيناً فهو جائز، وإن شرط المعلم على المولى أن يعطيه في كل شهر كذا ويقوم على غلامه في تعليم كذا فهو جائز، وإذا لم يشترط كل واحد منهما شيئاً فلما فرغ وتعلم قال المعلم لي الأجرة على رب العبد كذا وقال سيد العبد لي الأجرة على المعلم ينظر في ذلك إلى عرف تلك البلدة؛ فإن كان سيد العبد هو الذي يعطي فالأجرة عليه، وإن كان المعلم هو الذي يعطي فالأجرة على المعلم اهـ.
شاهدوا من
قال رحمه الله : والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن) وهذا مذهب المتأخرين من مشايخ بلخ، استحسنوا ذلك وقالوا بنى أصحابنا المتقدمون الجواب على ما قلة الحفاظ ورغبة الناس فيهم ولأن الحفاظ والمعلمين كان لهم عطايا في بيت المال وافتقادات من المتعلمين في مجازات التعليم من غير شرط وهذا الزمان قل ذلك واشتغل والحفاظ بمعائشهم فلو لم يفتح لهم باب التعليم وبالأجر لذهب القرآن فأفتوا بالجواز، والأحكام تختلف باختلاف الزمان، وكان محمد بن الفضل يفتي بأن الأجرة تجب ويحبس عليها. وفي الخلاصة : إذا أخذ المعلم من الصبي شيئاً من المأكول أو دفع الصبي ذلك إلى ولد المعلم لا يحل له بخلاف ثمن الحصر لأن ذلك تمليك من أب الصغير اهـ. وفي الحاوي للكرابيسي: إذا استأجره ليختم عنده القرآن ولم يسم له أجراً ليس له أن يأخذ أقل خمسة وأربعين درهماً شرعاً، أما إذا سمى أجراً لزم ما سمى لكن يأثم المستأجر إذا عقد على أقل من خمسة وأربعين درهماً إلا أن المستأجر ما بقي من تمام القدر أو يشترط أن يكون ثواب ما فوقه لنفسه فلا يأثم وكذا إذا قال اقرأ بقدر ما قدرت عليه فله بقدر ما قرأ وهذا يجب حفظه كما في المبسوط أقول: وهذا في عرفهم، أما في عرفنا فيجوز ذلك.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter of Invalid Ijarah. For teaching the Quran, and it is not permissible for singing, wailing, and musical instruments, and the lease of shared property is invalid except from the partner. We are in it; thus they said. And this is contradicted by what they mentioned in the chapter of hajj on behalf of another, that hajj occurs on behalf of the one commanded, and that a person can gift the reward of his deeds to others. It is restricted to acts of obedience, because if he hired him to teach his child writing, grammar, medicine, or interpretation, it is permissible by agreement; thus in al-Tatarakhaniyya. In al-Kubra: teaching inheritance shares, arithmetic, and wills for a fee is permissible. In al-Dhakhira: If he hired him to teach his child poetry and literature, if he specified a period, it is valid and the named fee is due if he made himself available whether or not the child learned; if he did not specify a period, the contract is invalid and the equivalent fee is due if the child learned. It also says: It is permissible to hire for teaching a craft, trade, demolition, construction, digging, and similar things. If he hired his slave to teach something in exchange for the master giving something specific, it is valid. If the teacher stipulated that the master give him a monthly amount and take care of his child in teaching, it is valid. If neither stipulated anything, and after finishing the teacher said 'the fee is upon the child's master' and the master said 'the fee is upon the teacher', then the custom of that town is looked to; if the master is the one who gives, the fee is upon him; if the teacher is the one who gives, the fee is upon the teacher. (They witnessed from) He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: The fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran. This is the school of the later scholars of the masters of Balkh; they deemed it good (istihsan) and said: Our earlier masters based the answer on the abundance of memorizers and the people's desire for them, and because the memorizers and teachers received stipends from the treasury and gifts from students during teaching arrangements without condition. In this time, that has decreased and the memorizers are occupied with their livelihoods, so if the door of teaching with a fee were not opened for them, the Quran would be lost. So they gave a fatwa of permissibility. Rulings differ with difference of time. Muhammad ibn al-Fadl used to give fatwa that the fee is obligatory and he would imprison for it. In al-Khulasa: If the teacher takes from the child something edible, or the child gives that to the teacher's child, it is not permissible for him, unlike the price of mats because that is a transfer of ownership from the minor's father. In al-Hawi al-Karabisi: If he hired him to complete the recitation of the Quran with him and did not name a fee, he is not entitled to take less than forty-five dirhams by law; but if he named a fee, what he named is binding, but the lessee sins if he contracted for less than forty-five dirhams, unless the lessee has left some of the full amount or stipulates that the reward for what is above goes to himself, then he does not sin. Similarly, if he said 'recite as much as you are able,' then he gets according to what he recited, and this must be memorized. I say: This is in their custom, but in our custom it is permissible.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains rulings on hiring for teaching. The matn states that teaching the Quran is permissible (since the statement 'for teaching the Quran' is not prohibited), while singing, wailing, and musical instruments are prohibited. The commentary expands on the permissibility of hiring for teaching various subjects. It begins by addressing a potential objection: if hiring for teaching is considered invalid because the benefit is not measurable, then what about hiring for Hajj on behalf of another, which is allowed? The response is that teaching is restricted to acts of obedience. Teaching writing, grammar, medicine, and interpretation is unanimously allowed. Teaching inheritance, arithmetic, and wills is also permissible. For teaching poetry and literature, the rule depends on whether a duration is specified; if so, the contract is valid and the named fee is due once the teacher makes himself available, regardless of learning. If no duration is specified, the contract is invalid, and the teacher gets the equivalent fee only if learning occurs. Similarly, teaching crafts and trades is valid, with detailed rules about who pays the fee based on custom. The commentator then presents the fatwa of later Hanafi scholars from Balkh, who permitted hiring for teaching the Quran due to the decline of state support for memorizers. They applied istihsan (juristic preference) overriding the earlier analogy. The earlier scholars had forbidden it because the benefit of teaching is intangible and cannot be delivered in a single instant, making the contract akin to hiring for something impossible. The later scholars argued that the actual benefit is the act of teaching (talqin), which is deliverable, and the learning is incidental. This is a classic case of qiyas vs. istihsan. The passage also discusses the details of what fee is due, including a minimum of 45 dirhams in their custom, and the ruling on teachers accepting gifts from students.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijarah): A contract hiring a person for a specific benefit in exchange for a known wage.
تعليم (ta'lim): Teaching, which includes both talqin (imparting) and tafhim (making understand).
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides analogy in view of necessity or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Quran was being neglected by the people.
B) The teachers had lost their state stipends and would not teach without pay, risking the loss of the Quran.
C) Teaching the Quran is an act of worship and cannot be paid.
D) The earlier scholars were mistaken in their qiyas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa on hiring for teaching the Quran evolved from prohibition to permissibility via istihsan, reflecting the principle that rulings can change with time and necessity.

Hiring for Teaching Quran: Qiyas vs. Istihsan and Related Cases
Listing rulings on invalid ijarah, with focus on teaching Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fatwa permits hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh by istihsan, distinguish between talaqqin and ta'lim, and apply the ruling to other similar cases (Mushaf, qisas, etc.).

Core Idea
Hiring to teach Quran is valid by istihsan because the benefit of talaqqin is deliverable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classical Hanafi dispute: is it permissible to hire someone to teach the Quran? While qiyas (analogy) suggests it is invalid because teaching is an intangible benefit, istihsan (juristic preference) permits it, especially when a fixed term is agreed. The key legal distinction is between talaqqin (direct instruction) and ta'lim (teaching as an abstract benefit). The passage also addresses other invalid hire cases, such as hiring a Mushaf, hiring for retaliation (qisas), and hiring by dhimmis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core act and its ruling
What is the main action being ruled upon? The passage focuses on hiring (isti'jar) for teaching Quran and Fiqh. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is permissibility (jawaz) by istihsan.
This is a developed ruling from later Hanafi scholarship.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogical reasoning) argument
What is the qiyas position? The passage states that in qiyas, hiring for teaching is invalid because the benefit (ta'lim) is not a known, deliverable commodity. The asl (original case) is general ijarah, which requires a known, deliverable benefit. The far' (new case) is teaching, and the illa (effective cause) is the inability to guarantee the benefit.
Qiyas is a deductive method; Hanafis use it but allow istihsan to override.
3
Analyze the istihsan (juristic preference) argument
What is the istihsan position? The passage explains that istihsan focuses on talaqqin (direct instruction), which is a physical, deliverable act. Making talaqqin the primary benefit and ta'lim subsidiary allows the contract to be valid. This is the preferred view of later scholars like those of Balkh.
Istihsan is a distinct Hanafi methodology.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on other cases
The passage records a disagreement on hiring for qisas: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say invalid, Muhammad says valid. Also, hiring a Mushaf is universally invalid; hiring for adhan/imamah is permissible by analogy to teaching.
The fatwa on teaching is clear; the qisas dispute is recognized but less impactful.
5
Apply the principles to similar scenarios
The passage gives other rulings: dhimmis cannot hire for sinful acts (prayer, bell-ringing), but Magian can hire a Muslim to kindle fire. The general principle is that any hire for a permissible act with a known benefit is valid, provided no prohibition via qiyas or istihsan.
The key is the nature of the benefit and customary practice.

هو أن مصحفاً ليقرأ فيه لم يجز، وإن قرى فيه فلا أجر عليه، والقاضي كالإمام. لو استأجر القاضي رجلاً ليقوم عليه في مجلس القضاء شهراً جاز، ولو استأجر من له القصاص رجلاً ليقتص له فلا أجر له لا يجوز هذا العقد عند الأول والثاني ويجوز عند الثالث. وفي قاضيخان: أهل الذمة إذا استأجروا ذمياً ليصلي بهم أو ليضرب الناقوس لهم لا يجوز، ولو استأجر المجوسي مسلماً ليقيم له النار لا بأس به لأن الانتفاع بالنار مباح .اهـ. وفي النهاية يعني يجوز الاستئجار على تعلم الفقه. وفي الروضة: وفي زماننا يجوز للإمام والمؤذن والمعلم أخذ الأجرة. ومثله في الذخيرة. ولا يجوز استئجار كتب الفقه والتفسير والحديث لعدم التعارف . قال ابن قاضي زاده: أقول وفيما ذكروا من وجه الاستحسان نظر قوي بيان ذلك مقتضى الدليل الأول أنه لا يمكن تحقيق ماهية الإجارة وهي تمليك المنافع بعوض في الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن ونظائره بناء على عدم القدرة على تسليم ما التزمه المؤجر من استحساناً والاستحسان فرع تحقق ماهية الإجارة كما لا يخفى، وهذا محل تسكب فيه العبرات. أقول : والجواب أن الإجارة في تعلم القرآن والفقه على أمرين، على التلقين والتعليم. ففي القياس نظروا إلى التعليم وجعلوا التلقين تابعاً له فقالوا : لا يمكن . وفي الاستحسان نظروا إلى التلقين وجعلوا التعليم تابعاً له فقالوا بالجواز فاختلفت الجهة . والأذان والإمامة دخلاً تبعاً فتدبره فإنه جيد. وفي الظهيرية ومشايخ بلخ أفتوا بجواز ذلك إذا ضرب له مدة وعند عدم الاستئجار أصلاً يجب أجر المثل .اهـ. وفي الملتقط : ولو امتنع أبو الصبي من دفع الوظيفة جبر عليه وحبس عليه اهـ.
It is that [if one hires] a Mushaf to read in it, it is not permissible, and if it is read in it, there is no wage for him. And the judge is like the Imam. If the judge hires a man to stand over him in the court for a month, it is permissible. And if the one who has the right of retaliation hires a man to execute retaliation for him, there is no wage for him; this contract is not permissible according to the first and second [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf] and is permissible according to the third [Muhammad]. And in Qadikhan: dhimmis if they hire a dhimmi to lead them in prayer or to ring the bell for them, it is not permissible. And if a Magian hires a Muslim to kindle fire for him, there is no harm because benefiting from fire is permissible. In al-Nihaya: it means it is permissible to hire for learning fiqh. In al-Rawda: in our time, it is permissible for the imam, muadhdhin, and teacher to take wages. Similar in al-Dhakhira. And it is not permissible to hire books of fiqh, tafsir, and hadith due to lack of customary practice. Ibn Qadi Zada said: I say: in what they mentioned from the aspect of istihsan, there is strong consideration. Explanation: the requirement of the first evidence is that the reality of ijarah (leasing) cannot be realized, which is the transfer of benefits in exchange, in hiring for teaching Quran and its likes, based on the inability to deliver what the lessor has committed. And istihsan is a branch of the realization of the reality of ijarah, as is not hidden, and this is a place where tears are shed. I say: The answer is that ijarah in learning Quran and fiqh is upon two things: talaqqin (dictation/instruction) and ta'lim (teaching). In qiyas, they looked at teaching and made talaqqin subsidiary to it, so they said it is not possible. In istihsan, they looked at talaqqin and made teaching subsidiary to it, so they said it is permissible. So the perspective differs. And adhan and imamah entered as subsidiary, so reflect on it, for it is good. In al-Zahiriya: the scholars of Balkh gave fatwa on its permissibility if a term is stipulated. And without hiring at all, the fair wage is obligatory. In al-Multaqat: if the father of a boy refuses to pay the stipend, he is compelled and imprisoned.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses several rulings regarding invalid idarah contracts. The passage begins with the ruling that hiring a Mushaf to read from it is invalid because the Mushaf itself is not something that can be rented for recitation; recitation is an act of the servant, not a property right that can be transferred. Similarly, if a judge hires a person to stand over him in court, it is permissible because the benefit is lawful and deliverable. However, hiring someone to execute retaliation (qisas) is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, but permissible according to Imam Muhammad. The passage then moves to dhimmis: they cannot hire a dhimmi to lead them in prayer or ring bells, as these acts are sinful in Islam. But a Magian may hire a Muslim to kindle fire, as benefiting from fire is permissible. The central discussion is about hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh. The author notes that in qiyas, such hiring is invalid because the benefit (teaching) is not precisely definable or because the teacher cannot guarantee delivery of knowledge. However, by istihsan, the scholars permitted it, especially in later times when it became customary for imams, muadhdhins, and teachers to take wages. The key is distinguishing between talaqqin (direct instruction, which is a physical act) and ta'lim (teaching as an abstract benefit). In istihsan, the focus is on talaqqin, which can be delivered, so the contract is valid. The adhan and imamah are also permissible as subsidiary. The fatwa of the scholars of Balkh is that if a term is fixed, it is permissible, otherwise the fair wage is due. The passage ends with a ruling that if the father of a boy refuses to pay the teacher's stipend, he is compelled and imprisoned.

Key Terms
مصحف (mushaf): Physical copy of the Quran
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case to a new case
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a more appropriate ruling
تلقين (talaqqin): Direct instruction, oral teaching
تعليم (ta'lim): Teaching, education
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Fair market wage
وظيفة (wazifa): Stipend, fixed periodic payment
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, retributive justice

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon fatwa on hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh?
A) It is invalid by qiyas and no alternative is given.
B) It is permissible by istihsan, especially if a fixed term is stipulated.
C) It is valid only if the teacher is also an imam.
D) It is invalid unless the teacher is a dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
Hiring for teaching Quran and Fiqh is permissible by istihsan, provided a fixed term is stipulated, and the teacher is entitled to a fair wage otherwise.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Invalid Ijarah: Hiring for Singing, Wailing, and Musical Instruments
Core ruling on invalid ijarah for sinful acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that hiring for singing, wailing, and musical instruments is invalid and explain why any wage paid must be returned.

Core Idea
Hiring for sinful acts is invalid because the benefit is unrecognized—any wage paid must be returned.

This lesson examines the core rule on invalid ijarah (hire) for acts that are sinful in themselves. The passage establishes that singing, wailing, and musical instruments produce a benefit that cannot be rightfully claimed in a contract. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing valid from invalid hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter
The passage lists singing, wailing, and musical instruments as examples of prohibited subject matter for ijarah.
These are considered sinful benefits (manfa'ah muharramah).
2
Determine the basis for invalidity
The text states the benefit is not conceivable to be established by the contract (laysat mutasawwarat al-istihqaq). In Hanafi law, a valid ijarah requires the benefit to be permissible and capable of being owned.
If the benefit is inherently sinful, it cannot be a valid consideration.
3
Apply the consequence
Since the contract is invalid (fasid), the wage is not owed. If already paid, it must be returned. If taken without condition, it may be permissible as a gift.
The distinction between 'taking with condition' and 'without condition' is important for determining obligation to return.
4
Note the exception for unconditional taking
The passage mentions from al-Muhit: if the money is taken without a stipulation that it is a wage, it becomes permissible for the recipient.
This is a form of istihsan (juristic preference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ولا يجوز على الغناء والنوح والملاهي لأن المنفعة لا تتصور استحقاقها بالعقد فلا يجب عليه الأجر من غير أن يستحق عليه لأن لا تكون إلا عند الاستحقاق، وإن أعطاه الأجر وقبضه لا يحل له ويجب عليه رده على صاحبه. وفي المحيط من كتاب الاستحسان : إذا أخذ المال من غير شرط يباح له. وفي المحيط : ذمي استأجر من مسلم أو ذمي بيعة يصلي فيها لم يجز لأن صلاة الذمي معصية وإن كانت طاعة في زعمه، ولو استأجر المسلم من المسلم مسجداً ليصلي فيه لم يجز لأن المسجد لا يملك، ولو استأجر ذمي داراً من مسلم فاتخذ فيها مصلى لنفسه لم يمنع فإن جمع الجماعة وضرب الناقوس فلصاحبها منعه، ولو أراد . الخمر فيها فإن كان في السواد لا يمنع وأما في سواد خراسان، فإنهم بيع يمنعون من ذلك لأن الغالب فيها المسلمون مسلم يشرب الخمر في داره ويجمع القوم يمنع ذلك ولا يخرج من داره، وكذا الذمي لو استأجر مسلماً ليرعى له الخنازير ويجوز عند من الإمام. خلافاً لهما. استأجر ذمي مسلماً ليحمل له ميتاً أو دماً يجوز لأن نقل الميت والدم لإماطة الأذى عن الناس مباح مات ميت من المشركين فاستأجروا مسلماً ليحمله إلى بلدة أخرى قال أبو يوسف : لا أجر له. وقال محمد: إن علم الأجير أنها جيفة لا أجر له لأنه نقل ما لا يجوز له، وإن لم يعلم فله الأجر. وفي الخانية: الفتوى على قول محمد اهـ. ولو استأجره لينقل الميت المشرك إلى المقبرة يجوز ؛ كذا في المحيط. وفي المضمرات: الغناء حارم الأديان، وكذا إذا أوصى بما هو معصية عندنا وعند أهل الكتاب لا يجوز وذكر في جميع منها الوصية للمغنيين والمغنيات. وقال ظهير الدين من قال لمقرئي زماننا أحسنت عند قراءته يكفر. وفي الكبرى : رجل جمع المال وهو كان مطرباً مغنياً هل يباح له ذلك؟ إن كان من غير شرط يباح له. وإن كان بالشرط يرده على أصحابه. وإن لم يعرف يتصدق به. وفي العتابية : وأما المعصية نحو أن يستأجر نائحة أو مغنية أو لتعليم الغناء وفي فتاوى أهل سمرقند : استأجر رجلاً لينحت له مزماراً أو طنبوراً أو بربطاً ففعل يطيب له الأجر إلا أنه يأثم. وفي الإعانة على المعصية، ولو استأجر المسلم ليبني له بيعة أو كنيسة جاز ويطيب له الأجر. ولو استأجر امرأة ليكتب لها قرآناً أو غيره جاز ويطيب له الأجر إذا بين الشرط وهو إعداد الخط وقدره، ولو استأجر مسلماً ليحمل له خمراً ولم يقل لأشربه جازت الإجارة على قول الإمام خلافاً لهما. وفي المحيط السارق أو الغاصب لو استأجر رجلاً يحمل المغصوب أو المسروق لم يجز لأن نقل مال الغير معصية .اهـ. وفي شرح الكافي ولا يجوز الإجارة على شيء من الغناء واللهو والنوح والمزامير والطبل ولا على الحداء وقراءة الشعر ولا غيره ولا أجر في ذلك. هذا في الطبل إذا كان للهو، أما إذا كان لغيره فلا بأس به كطبل القراءة وطبل العرس. وفي الأجناس ولا بأس أن يكون ليلة العرس دف يضرب به لشهرة العرس. وفي الولوالجية: رجل استأجر رجلاً ليضرب الطبل إن كان للهو لا يجوز. وإن كان للغزو والقافلة يجوز .
He said: And it is not permissible [to hire] for singing, wailing, and musical instruments, because the benefit is not conceivable to be established by the contract, so the wage is not obligatory upon him without being due upon him, because it is only when it is due. And if he gave the wage and received it, it is not lawful for him and he must return it to its owner. In al-Muhit from the book of Istihsan: if he took the money without a condition, it is permissible for him. In al-Muhit: a dhimmi hiring from a Muslim or dhimmi a church to pray in it is not permissible, because the prayer of a dhimmi is disobedience even if it is obedience in his belief. And if a Muslim hires from a Muslim a mosque to pray in it, it is not permissible because the mosque is not owned. And if a dhimmi hires a house from a Muslim and takes it as a place of prayer for himself, it is not prevented. If he gathers a congregation and rings the bell, the owner may prevent him. And if he wants [to drink] wine in it, if it is in the countryside (sawad), he is not prevented, but in the countryside of Khurasan, they prevent him because the majority there are Muslims. A Muslim drinking wine in his house and gathering people is prevented but not evicted from his house. Likewise, a dhimmi if he hires a Muslim to tend his pigs, it is permissible according to the Imam, contrary to the two. A dhimmi hires a Muslim to carry a dead body or blood: permissible because transferring the dead body and blood to remove harm from people is permissible. If a dead person from the polytheists dies and they hire a Muslim to carry him to another town, Abu Yusuf said: no wage for him. Muhammad said: if the hired knows it is a carcass, no wage for him because he carried what is not permissible. If he does not know, he has the wage. In al-Khaniya: the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. And if he hires him to carry the dead polytheist to the cemetery, it is permissible. In al-Mudmarat: singing is forbidden in all religions. Likewise, if one bequeaths what is sinful in our view and in the view of the People of the Book, it is not permissible. And he mentioned that the bequest to male and female singers is included. And Zahir al-Din said: whoever says to our latter-day reciters 'you did well' at his recitation becomes a disbeliever. In al-Kubra: a man collected wealth while he was a musician singer; is it permissible for him? If without condition, permissible. If with condition, he returns it to its owners. If he does not know, he gives it in charity. In al-Utabiya: as for sin, such as hiring a wailer or singer or to teach singing, it is not permissible. In the fatwas of the people of Samarkand: if a man hires a man to carve a flute or lute or lyre for him and he does it, his wage is good but he sins because he assisted in sin. And if a Muslim hires to build a church or synagogue for him, it is permissible and his wage is good. And if a man hires a woman to write a Quran or other for him, it is permissible and his wage is good if the condition is clarified, which is the preparation of the line and its amount. And if a Muslim hires a Muslim to carry wine for him and he did not say 'I will drink it', the ijarah is permissible according to the Imam, contrary to the two. In al-Muhit: a thief or usurper if he hires a man to carry the usurped or stolen property, it is not permissible because transferring another's property is disobedience. In Sharh al-Kafi: it is not permissible to hire for any singing, amusement, wailing, flutes, and drum, nor for leading camels in travel (hida'), and reading poetry, nor other, and there is no wage for that. This regarding the drum when it is for amusement. If for other, there is no harm, such as the drum of recitation and the drum of wedding. In al-Ajnas: there is no harm in the wedding night to have a duff (frame drum) beaten to announce the wedding. In al-Walwalijiya: a man hires a man to beat the drum if for amusement, not permissible. If for war or caravan, permissible.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This lengthy passage continues the chapter on invalid ijarah, focusing on hire contracts whose subject matter is sinful (ma'siya). The opening rule: hiring for singing, wailing, and musical instruments is invalid because the benefit is not recognized by the Shari'ah and thus cannot be a valid consideration in a contract. Any wage paid must be returned. However, if money is taken without explicit condition, it may be permissible (as a gift). The passage then covers various scenarios: a dhimmi hiring a place of worship; a Muslim hiring a mosque (invalid because mosque cannot be owned); a dhimmi hiring a house to pray (permissible but can be prevented if he rings bells); drinking wine in rented house in rural vs urban areas; a Muslim tending pigs for a dhimmi (permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, against the two disciples); carrying dead bodies of disbelievers (valid if for sanitation, with a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); building churches (valid); writing Quran (valid with proper conditions); carrying wine (valid if the carrier knows it's for permissible use? actually text says if not stated to drink, contract is valid per Abu Hanifa); carrying stolen goods (invalid). The passage also addresses the permissibility of earning from singing/music if without prior agreement, and the ruling on drums for war and weddings.

Key Terms
الغناء (al-ghina'): Singing, especially for entertainment
النوح (al-nawh): Wailing, lamentation for the dead
الملاهي (al-malahi): Musical instruments

According to the passage, if a Muslim hires a singer without specifying a wage, and later gives the singer a gift, what is the ruling?
A) The gift is permissible and the singer may keep it.
B) The gift must be returned because the hiring is invalid.
C) The contract is valid and the gift is considered wage.
D) It is makruh to accept the gift.

Key Takeaway
Hiring for any act that is inherently sinful (singing, wailing, musical instruments) results in an invalid contract; wages must be returned unless taken without condition.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Intra-Hanafi Disputes: Ijarah for Pigs, Dead Bodies, and Wine
Intra-Hanafi disputes on ijarah for assistance in sin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on hiring for tending pigs, carrying dead polytheists, and carrying wine, and identify the mufta bihi for each.

Core Idea
Imams differ on whether assisting in sin through ijarah is invalid—fatwa favors Muhammad on dead body, Imam's view on other cases.

While the general rule prohibits hiring for sinful acts, the Hanafi school has internal disagreements on borderline cases where the worker's act is not itself sinful but assists another's sin. This lesson examines three classic disputes: tending pigs, carrying dead polytheists, and carrying wine. Understanding these disputes sharpens your ability to apply the principle that the benefit must be permissible in itself.

Guided Path
1
Examine the case of tending pigs
A dhimmi hires a Muslim to tend his pigs. Imam Abu Hanifa permits the ijarah because tending is not inherently sinful; the sin is on the owner. The Sahibayn prohibit it as assisting in sin.
The thamarah: if the contract is made, wage is due per Imam, not per Sahibayn.
2
Examine the case of carrying dead polytheist
If hired to carry a dead body to another town, Abu Yusuf says no wage at all. Muhammad says if the hired knows it is a carcass, no wage; if unaware, wage is due. Fatwa is on Muhammad's view.
The distinction between knowing and not knowing is crucial.
3
Examine the case of carrying wine
If a Muslim hires a Muslim to carry wine without stating he will drink it, Imam permits the ijarah. The Sahibayn invalidate it because carrying wine is assisting in sin.
The condition of not stating the purpose makes the benefit ambiguous.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
For the dead body, the text explicitly says fatwa is on Muhammad's view. For the other two, the text does not specify, but later Hanafi practice tends to follow the Imam's view.
The authority_weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin for the dead body case.

Source Text

وفي المضمرات: الغناء حارم الأديان، وكذا إذا أوصى بما هو معصية عندنا وعند أهل الكتاب لا يجوز وذكر في جميع منها الوصية للمغنيين والمغنيات. وقال ظهير الدين من قال لمقرئي زماننا أحسنت عند قراءته يكفر. وفي الكبرى : رجل جمع المال وهو كان مطرباً مغنياً هل يباح له ذلك؟ إن كان من غير شرط يباح له. وإن كان بالشرط يرده على أصحابه. وإن لم يعرف يتصدق به. وفي العتابية : وأما المعصية نحو أن يستأجر نائحة أو مغنية أو لتعليم الغناء وفي فتاوى أهل سمرقند : استأجر رجلاً لينحت له مزماراً أو طنبوراً أو بربطاً ففعل يطيب له الأجر إلا أنه يأثم. وفي الإعانة على المعصية، ولو استأجر المسلم ليبني له بيعة أو كنيسة جاز ويطيب له الأجر. ولو استأجر امرأة ليكتب لها قرآناً أو غيره جاز ويطيب له الأجر إذا بين الشرط وهو إعداد الخط وقدره، ولو استأجر مسلماً ليحمل له خمراً ولم يقل لأشربه جازت الإجارة على قول الإمام خلافاً لهما. وفي المحيط السارق أو الغاصب لو استأجر رجلاً يحمل المغصوب أو المسروق لم يجز لأن نقل مال الغير معصية .اهـ. وفي شرح الكافي ولا يجوز الإجارة على شيء من الغناء واللهو والنوح والمزامير والطبل ولا على الحداء وقراءة الشعر ولا غيره ولا أجر في ذلك. هذا في الطبل إذا كان للهو، أما إذا كان لغيره فلا بأس به كطبل القراءة وطبل العرس. وفي الأجناس ولا بأس أن يكون ليلة العرس دف يضرب به لشهرة العرس. وفي الولوالجية: رجل استأجر رجلاً ليضرب الطبل إن كان للهو لا يجوز. وإن كان للغزو والقافلة يجوز .
He said: And it is not permissible [to hire] for singing, wailing, and musical instruments, because the benefit is not conceivable to be established by the contract, so the wage is not obligatory upon him without being due upon him, because it is only when it is due. And if he gave the wage and received it, it is not lawful for him and he must return it to its owner. In al-Muhit from the book of Istihsan: if he took the money without a condition, it is permissible for him. In al-Muhit: a dhimmi hiring from a Muslim or dhimmi a church to pray in it is not permissible, because the prayer of a dhimmi is disobedience even if it is obedience in his belief. And if a Muslim hires from a Muslim a mosque to pray in it, it is not permissible because the mosque is not owned. And if a dhimmi hires a house from a Muslim and takes it as a place of prayer for himself, it is not prevented. If he gathers a congregation and rings the bell, the owner may prevent him. And if he wants [to drink] wine in it, if it is in the countryside (sawad), he is not prevented, but in the countryside of Khurasan, they prevent him because the majority there are Muslims. A Muslim drinking wine in his house and gathering people is prevented but not evicted from his house. Likewise, a dhimmi if he hires a Muslim to tend his pigs, it is permissible according to the Imam, contrary to the two. A dhimmi hires a Muslim to carry a dead body or blood: permissible because transferring the dead body and blood to remove harm from people is permissible. If a dead person from the polytheists dies and they hire a Muslim to carry him to another town, Abu Yusuf said: no wage for him. Muhammad said: if the hired knows it is a carcass, no wage for him because he carried what is not permissible. If he does not know, he has the wage. In al-Khaniya: the fatwa is on Muhammad's view. And if he hires him to carry the dead polytheist to the cemetery, it is permissible. In al-Mudmarat: singing is forbidden in all religions. Likewise, if one bequeaths what is sinful in our view and in the view of the People of the Book, it is not permissible. And he mentioned that the bequest to male and female singers is included. And Zahir al-Din said: whoever says to our latter-day reciters 'you did well' at his recitation becomes a disbeliever. In al-Kubra: a man collected wealth while he was a musician singer; is it permissible for him? If without condition, permissible. If with condition, he returns it to its owners. If he does not know, he gives it in charity. In al-Utabiya: as for sin, such as hiring a wailer or singer or to teach singing, it is not permissible. In the fatwas of the people of Samarkand: if a man hires a man to carve a flute or lute or lyre for him and he does it, his wage is good but he sins because he assisted in sin. And if a Muslim hires to build a church or synagogue for him, it is permissible and his wage is good. And if a man hires a woman to write a Quran or other for him, it is permissible and his wage is good if the condition is clarified, which is the preparation of the line and its amount. And if a Muslim hires a Muslim to carry wine for him and he did not say 'I will drink it', the ijarah is permissible according to the Imam, contrary to the two. In al-Muhit: a thief or usurper if he hires a man to carry the usurped or stolen property, it is not permissible because transferring another's property is disobedience. In Sharh al-Kafi: it is not permissible to hire for any singing, amusement, wailing, flutes, and drum, nor for leading camels in travel (hida'), and reading poetry, nor other, and there is no wage for that. This regarding the drum when it is for amusement. If for other, there is no harm, such as the drum of recitation and the drum of wedding. In al-Ajnas: there is no harm in the wedding night to have a duff (frame drum) beaten to announce the wedding. In al-Walwalijiya: a man hires a man to beat the drum if for amusement, not permissible. If for war or caravan, permissible.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This lengthy passage continues the chapter on invalid ijarah, focusing on hire contracts whose subject matter is sinful (ma'siya). The opening rule: hiring for singing, wailing, and musical instruments is invalid because the benefit is not recognized by the Shari'ah and thus cannot be a valid consideration in a contract. Any wage paid must be returned. However, if money is taken without explicit condition, it may be permissible (as a gift). The passage then covers various scenarios: a dhimmi hiring a place of worship; a Muslim hiring a mosque (invalid because mosque cannot be owned); a dhimmi hiring a house to pray (permissible but can be prevented if he rings bells); drinking wine in rented house in rural vs urban areas; a Muslim tending pigs for a dhimmi (permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, against the two disciples); carrying dead bodies of disbelievers (valid if for sanitation, with a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); building churches (valid); writing Quran (valid with proper conditions); carrying wine (valid if the carrier knows it's for permissible use? actually text says if not stated to drink, contract is valid per Abu Hanifa); carrying stolen goods (invalid). The passage also addresses the permissibility of earning from singing/music if without prior agreement, and the ruling on drums for war and weddings.

Key Terms
الخنازير (al-khanazir): Pigs
الجيفة (al-jifa): Carcass, dead body
الخمر (al-khamr): Wine, intoxicant

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fatwa (relied-upon ruling) regarding a Muslim hired to carry a dead polytheist to another town, if he does not know it is a corpse?
A) He has no wage according to both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
B) He has a wage according to Muhammad
C) He has no wage according to Muhammad, and a wage according to Abu Yusuf
D) The contract is invalid altogether

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi disputes on ijarah for acts that assist sin demonstrate that the permissibility depends on whether the worker's direct benefit is itself sinful, with the mufta bihi often following the Imam's view.
