Hiring a Wet Nurse with Food and Clothing: The Role of Custom in Contractual Certainty
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hiring a wet nurse with unspecified wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on hiring a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing, identify the role of custom ('urf) in overriding qiyas, and apply the principle that jahalah only invalidates a contract if it leads to dispute.

Core Idea
Custom can override the general rule that uncertain wages invalidate a contract when it prevents dispute.

The Hanafi school generally requires that the wage in an ijarah contract be known to avoid disputes. However, there is an exception: hiring a wet nurse (zair) with food and clothing as payment. In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether the uncertainty in the wage is permissible. The dispute hinges on the role of custom ('urf) and the definition of harmful ignorance (jahalah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the contract? Hiring a wet nurse (zair) with her food and clothing (ta'amiha wa kiswatiha) as the wage. The point of disagreement: is such a contract valid when the wage is unspecified?
The wage is completely unspecified in quantity and type.
2
State the positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is valid. The two companions (Sahibayn) hold it is not permissible, considering it analogous to hiring a cook with an unspecified wage.
The matn says 'This is with Imam' indicating the relied-upon position.
3
Examine each proof
Abu Hanifa relies on custom ('urf) and istihsan: people are generous with wet nurses due to compassion for children, so no dispute arises. The Sahibayn rely on qiyas: the wage is unknown (majhul), which invalidates the contract by analogy to other hiring contracts.
The Sahibayn's view is 'the qiyas' – the default ruling by analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Why does custom override qiyas here? Because jahalah (ignorance) only invalidates a contract if it typically leads to litigation (tazara'). In this case, the customary practice of generosity prevents dispute, so uncertainty is not harmful.
This is a direct application of the usul principle that custom ('urf) can specify the general or restrict the absolute.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the contract is valid. If the food and clothing are not described, the wet nurse is entitled to the average (al-mutawassit) from the custom of the locality.
Al-Haddadi is cited for the 'average' rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبطعامها وكسوتها وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يجوز وهو القياس . وجه قولهما أن الأجرة مجهولة فصار كما إذا استأجرها للطبخ والخبز والجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لأن العادة جرت بالتوسعة عليها شفقة على الأولاد بل يعطيها ما طلبت ويوافقها على مرادها، والجهالة إنما تمنع إذا أفضت إلى المنازعة . أطلق في طعامها أو كسوتها فشمل ما إذا بين جنسها أو لم يبين . قال الحدادي : إذا لم يوصف ذلك فلها المتوسط. وفي الخلاصة: وإذا
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And with her food and clothing, and this is with Imam Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not permissible, and that is the qiyas. The point of their statement is that the wage is unknown, so it becomes like hiring her for cooking and baking, and ignorance does not lead to dispute because custom has run on giving generously out of compassion for children; rather he gives her what she asks and agrees to her desire, and ignorance only prevents when it leads to dispute. He used general wording in her food or clothing, so it includes whether its type is specified or not. Al-Haddadi said: if it is not described, then she gets the average. And in al-Khulasa: and if...
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the second part of the matn regarding hiring a wet nurse with her food and clothing (bi ta'amiha wa kiswatiha) as payment. The matn states it is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) reject this based on qiyas: the wage (food and clothing) is unknown (majhul), leading to dispute. However, Abu Hanifa's view is based on custom (urf): people are generous with wet nurses out of compassion, so there is no dispute. Ignorance (jahl) only nullifies a contract if it leads to litigation. The commentary notes that the matn's wording is general: even if the type of food or clothing is unspecified, it is valid. If not described, the wet nurse gets the average (al-mutawassit). The text from al-Khulasa is incomplete here.

Key Terms
طعامها وكسوتها (ṭa'āmuhā wa kiswatuhā): Her food and clothing, unspecified, as payment for wet nursing.
جهالة (jahālah): Uncertainty or ignorance about the wage, which normally invalidates a contract.
عرف (‘urf): Custom or common practice, used here to justify the validity despite uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa allow hiring a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing while the Sahibayn disallow it?
A) Abu Hanifa considers the contract as a gift, not an ijarah.
B) Custom shows that families are generous with wet nurses, so uncertainty does not lead to dispute.
C) Abu Hanifa requires the wage to be estimated by experts.
D) The Sahibayn hold that all ijarah contracts require known wages without exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, custom ('urf) can override the general rule that uncertain wages invalidate a contract when the custom prevents dispute, as in hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing.

The Object of the Wet Nurse Contract: Milk or Service?
Explains the nature of the wet nurse contract and the scholarly disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on the object of the wet nurse contract and explain how the chosen view affects the wet nurse's liability.

Core Idea
The contract is on the milk; the wet nurse is a specialized hire, not liable for loss without negligence.

This lesson examines the fundamental nature of the wet nurse (istijar al-zhi'r) contract. Hanafi scholars disagree whether the contract is on the milk or on both milk and service. The resolution determines whether the wet nurse is a specialized or common hire, affecting her liability for the child. The passage begins with this dispute and concludes with the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the two opinions
Identify the two views on the object of the contract: one says it is on the milk (with service subsidiary), the other says it is on both milk and service.
2
Identify the preferred view
Note that Shams al-A'imma and the author of al-Kafi deem the first view as more correct and more akin to fiqh.
3
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that if the wet nurse is a specialized hire, she is not liable for loss of the child without negligence. If she were a common hire, she would be liable.
4
Confirm the classification
Al-Mabsut explicitly states she is a specialized hire. Al-Dhakhira mentions she can be both, but the relied-upon view is specialized.
The passage also mentions that if she works for multiple families, she may be treated as common for wage but sins as specialized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لها. وقال بعضهم: العقد يرد على اللبن والتربية والخدمة تابعة لها وإليه مال شمس الأئمة. وقال : هو الأصح والأول أشبه بالفقه وأقرب إليه. وقال في الكافي : وهو الصحيح. والظئر المرأة ذات اللبن سواء كانت مسلمة أو كافرة حرة أو أمة أو مدبرة أو أم ولد أو مكاتبة؛ كذا في قاضيخان. وفي ابن فرشته فلو عجزت المكاتبة وردت في الرق يحكم أبو يوسف ببقاء العقد، وأبطله محمد وفي المحيط وأجرت الأمة الفاجرة أو الكافرة نفسها ظئراً جاز لأن الإجارة من التجارة، ولو رضع الصبي جارية الظئر أو خدمها فلها الأجر كاملاً لأن الظئر بمنزلة الأجير المشترك، ولو استأجرت الظئر ظئراً فارضعته فلها الأجر استحساناً، ولو شرط عليها أن ترضع الصبي بنفسها فأرضعته بمن ذكر فلها الأجر لأن اشتراط الرضاع عليها بنفسها لا يفيد . ولو اختلفا فقال أهل الصغير أرضعتيه بلبن شاة فلا أجز لك وقالت أرضعته بلبن آدمية فلي الأجر فالقول قولها مع يمينها لأن الظاهر يشهد لها، وإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينتها لأنها مثبتة. وإن شرطوا عليها ارضاع الصبي في منزل الأب فليس للظئر أن تخرج به منه لأن الإرضاع في منزل الأب أجود للصبي، وليس لهم أن يحبسوا الظئر في منزلهم إن لم يشترطوا ذلك اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه لا بد من أن تكون المدة معلومة ولهذا قال في التجريد : ولا بد أن تكون المدة معلومة وما جاز في استئجار العبد للخدمة جاز في الظئر، وما بطل هناك بطل هنا. وفي الأصل : وإذا جازت هذه الإجارة ينظر بعد ذلك إن شرط في عقد الإجارة أنها ترضع الصبي في منزل الأب اعتبر ، ولو لم يكن هناك شرط ينظر للعرف؛ إن كانت ترضع في منزل الأب اعتبر، ولو لم يكن هناك شرط ينظر للعرف؛ إن كانت ترضع في منزل الأب أو في منزلها يعمل به وإلا فلها الخيار إن شاءت أرضعت الصبي في منزل الأب أو في منزلها اهـ . قال الأكمل : فإن قلت الطئر أجير خاص أو مشترك؟ قلت: هو أجير خاص يدل عليه لفظ المبسوط قال : لو ضاع الصبي من يدها أو وقع فمات أو سرق من حلي الصبي أو ثيابه شيء لم تضمن الظئر لأنها بمنزلة الأجير الخاص. وذكر في الذخيرة ما يدل على أنه كما يكون مشتركاً يجوز أن يكون خاصاً قال : لو أجرت نفسها لقوم غير الأول ولو لم يعلم الأول فأرضعت كلاً منهما صح وتصير المرضعة أمينة وهذه خيانة منها ولها الأجر كاملاً في الفريقين، وهذا يدل على أنها تحتملهما معاً فقلنا تجب الأجرة كاملاً نظراً إلى أنها مشترك ويأثم نظراً إلى أنها خاص.
It is for her. Some said: The contract is on the milk, and upbringing and service are subsidiary to it, and Shams al-A'imma inclined to this. He said: It is the most correct, and the first is more akin to fiqh and closer to it. It is said in al-Kafi: It is the correct view. The wet nurse is a woman having milk, whether she is Muslim or non-Muslim, free or slave, mudabbara, umm walad, or mukataba; as in Qadi Khan. In Ibn Farishta: If the mukataba becomes unable and is returned to slavery, Abu Yusuf rules that the contract remains, and Muhammad invalidates it. In al-Muhit: A sinful or non-Muslim slave woman hiring herself as a wet nurse is valid because hiring is from trade. If the boy suckles the wet nurse's slave girl or serves her, she gets the full wage because the wet nurse is like a common hire. If the wet nurse hires another wet nurse and she suckles him, she gets the wage by istihsan. If she stipulates that she herself suckle the boy, then she suckles him with someone else, she gets the wage because stipulating suckling by herself is useless. If they dispute: the boy's family say, 'You suckled him with sheep's milk, so no wage for you,' and she says, 'I suckled him with human milk, so I deserve the wage,' then her word is taken with her oath because the apparent circumstance witnesses for her. If they both bring evidence, the evidence of the woman is preferred because it is affirmative. If they stipulate that she suckle the boy in the father's house, then the wet nurse may not take him out because suckling in the father's house is better for the boy. They may not detain the wet nurse in their house if they did not stipulate that. It is not hidden that the term must be known; hence it is said in al-Tajrid: The term must be known, and what is valid in hiring a slave for service is valid in the wet nurse, and what is invalid there is invalid here. In al-Asl: When this hiring is valid, then if they stipulate in the contract that she suckle the boy in the father's house, it is considered; if there is no stipulation, custom is considered: if she habitually suckles in the father's house, it is considered; if in her house, it is considered; otherwise she has the choice: if she wishes, she may suckle in the father's house or in her house. Al-Akmal said: If you ask, is the wet nurse a specialized or common hire? I say: She is a specialized hire; the wording of al-Mabsut indicates this: he said: If the boy is lost from her hand, or falls and dies, or something of his jewelry or clothes is stolen, the wet nurse is not liable because she is like a specialized hire. In al-Dhakhira, something is mentioned indicating that just as she can be common, she can also be specialized: He said: If she hires herself to other people without the knowledge of the first, and suckles each, it is valid, and she becomes a trustee, and this is treachery from her, and she gets the full wage from both parties. This indicates that she admits both possibilities; so we say the wage is due in full because she is common, but she sins because she is specialized.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the contract of hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-zhi'r). The commentator begins by noting a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: some say the contract is primarily on the milk, with upbringing and service being subsidiary; Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani favored this, and it is deemed more correct by many. The passage then clarifies who can be a wet nurse: any lactating woman, regardless of religion, status (free or slave), including mukataba (a slave who has contracted manumission). It then addresses a specific case: if a mukataba becomes unable to pay and returns to slavery, Abu Yusuf holds the contract remains valid, while Muhammad invalidates it. The ruling that a sinful or non-Muslim slave woman may be hired as a wet nurse is justified because hiring is a form of commerce, and it is valid. The text then discusses various scenarios: if the boy suckles the wet nurse's own slave girl, she still gets the full wage because the wet nurse is considered a common hire (ajir mushtarak) for that moment. If she hires another wet nurse to suckle the boy, that second wet nurse gets her wage by istihsan because the first wet nurse is like an intermediary. Stipulating that she herself must suckle is not effective; if she delegates to another, she still gets the wage. Regarding disputes about the type of milk (human vs. animal), the woman's statement is trusted with her oath because the apparent circumstance (normal practice) supports her. If both bring evidence, the woman's evidence is preferred as it affirms her claim. The place of feeding: if stipulated in the father's home, she must comply; if not, custom determines; otherwise she has a choice. The term of the contract must be known. Finally, the classification of the wet nurse: according to al-Mabsut, she is a specialized hire (ajir khas) because she is not liable for loss of the child. However, al-Dhakhira suggests she can be either specialized or common; if she simultaneously works for others without informing the first, she gets the full wage from both (as a common hire) but sins due to the breach of trust (as a specialized hire).

Key Terms
ظئر (zhi'r): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specialized hiree (employee) who works exclusively for one employer during the term
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hiree who offers services to the public and is liable for loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the wet nurse's liability if the child is lost without negligence?
A) She is liable because she is a common hire.
B) She is not liable because she is a specialized hire.
C) She is liable only if she used animal milk.
D) She is liable if the contract is on both milk and service.

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse is a specialized hire; the contract is on the milk, and she is not liable for loss without negligence.

Practical Rulings for the Wet Nurse Contract
Provides detailed rulings for common issues in wet nurse contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi rulings to various scenarios involving the wet nurse contract, such as disputes over milk type, subcontracting, and stipulations.

Core Idea
The wet nurse contract is flexible: she can be any lactating woman, and many disputes are resolved by custom and circumstantial evidence.

This lesson covers the practical rulings derived from the wet nurse contract passage. It addresses who can be hired, what happens when a mukataba returns to slavery, how disputes about milk type are resolved, the validity of subcontracting, and the place of feeding. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan, custom, and the principle that the apparent circumstance (zahir) supports the wet nurse's claim in many cases.

Guided Path
1
List permissible hirees
Identify from the passage that the wet nurse can be any lactating woman: Muslim or non-Muslim, free or slave, including mukataba, mudabbara, and umm walad.
The passage explicitly says 'والظئر المرأة ذات اللبن سواء كانت مسلمة أو كافرة حرة أو أمة أو مدبرة أو أم ولد أو مكاتبة'.
2
Analyze the mukataba case
Understand that if a mukataba (slave with contract of manumission) becomes unable to pay and returns to slavery, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf holds the contract remains, Muhammad invalidates it.
This shows that the validity of the contract depends on her status at the time of hiring.
3
Resolve disputes over milk type
If the family claims she used animal milk, her word with oath is taken because the apparent circumstance (normally she would use human milk) supports her. If both bring evidence, her evidence is preferred because it affirms her claim.
The principle is 'القول قولها مع يمينها لأن الظاهر يشهد لها'.
4
Understand subcontracting and stipulations
If the wet nurse hires another woman to suckle, the second woman gets her wage by istihsan. Stipulating that she must suckle personally is ineffective; if she uses another, she still gets the wage.
The passage says 'لو اشتراط الرضاع عليها بنفسها لا يفيد'.
5
Determine the place of feeding
If stipulated in the father's house, she must comply; otherwise custom dictates; if no custom, she has the choice to feed in the father's house or her own.
Custom ('urf) is given weight in the absence of stipulation.

Source Text

مسلمة أو كافرة حرة أو أمة أو مدبرة أو أم ولد أو مكاتبة؛ كذا في قاضيخان. وفي ابن فرشته فلو عجزت المكاتبة وردت في الرق يحكم أبو يوسف ببقاء العقد، وأبطله محمد وفي المحيط وأجرت الأمة الفاجرة أو الكافرة نفسها ظئراً جاز لأن الإجارة من التجارة، ولو رضع الصبي جارية الظئر أو خدمها فلها الأجر كاملاً لأن الظئر بمنزلة الأجير المشترك، ولو استأجرت الظئر ظئراً فارضعته فلها الأجر استحساناً، ولو شرط عليها أن ترضع الصبي بنفسها فأرضعته بمن ذكر فلها الأجر لأن اشتراط الرضاع عليها بنفسها لا يفيد . ولو اختلفا فقال أهل الصغير أرضعتيه بلبن شاة فلا أجز لك وقالت أرضعته بلبن آدمية فلي الأجر فالقول قولها مع يمينها لأن الظاهر يشهد لها، وإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينتها لأنها مثبتة. وإن شرطوا عليها ارضاع الصبي في منزل الأب فليس للظئر أن تخرج به منه لأن الإرضاع في منزل الأب أجود للصبي، وليس لهم أن يحبسوا الظئر في منزلهم إن لم يشترطوا ذلك اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه لا بد من أن تكون المدة معلومة ولهذا قال في التجريد : ولا بد أن تكون المدة معلومة وما جاز في استئجار العبد للخدمة جاز في الظئر، وما بطل هناك بطل هنا. وفي الأصل : وإذا جازت هذه الإجارة ينظر بعد ذلك إن شرط في عقد الإجارة أنها ترضع الصبي في منزل الأب اعتبر ، ولو لم يكن هناك شرط ينظر للعرف؛ إن كانت ترضع في منزل الأب اعتبر، ولو لم يكن هناك شرط ينظر للعرف؛ إن كانت ترضع في منزل الأب أو في منزلها يعمل به وإلا فلها الخيار إن شاءت أرضعت الصبي في منزل الأب أو في منزلها اهـ . قال الأكمل : فإن قلت الطئر أجير خاص أو مشترك؟ قلت: هو أجير خاص يدل عليه لفظ المبسوط قال : لو ضاع الصبي من يدها أو وقع فمات أو سرق من حلي الصبي أو ثيابه شيء لم تضمن الظئر لأنها بمنزلة الأجير الخاص. وذكر في الذخيرة ما يدل على أنه كما يكون مشتركاً يجوز أن يكون خاصاً قال : لو أجرت نفسها لقوم غير الأول ولو لم يعلم الأول فأرضعت كلاً منهما صح وتصير المرضعة أمينة وهذه خيانة منها ولها الأجر كاملاً في الفريقين، وهذا يدل على أنها تحتملهما معاً فقلنا تجب الأجرة كاملاً نظراً إلى أنها مشترك ويأثم نظراً إلى أنها خاص.
It is for her. Some said: The contract is on the milk, and upbringing and service are subsidiary to it, and Shams al-A'imma inclined to this. He said: It is the most correct, and the first is more akin to fiqh and closer to it. It is said in al-Kafi: It is the correct view. The wet nurse is a woman having milk, whether she is Muslim or non-Muslim, free or slave, mudabbara, umm walad, or mukataba; as in Qadi Khan. In Ibn Farishta: If the mukataba becomes unable and is returned to slavery, Abu Yusuf rules that the contract remains, and Muhammad invalidates it. In al-Muhit: A sinful or non-Muslim slave woman hiring herself as a wet nurse is valid because hiring is from trade. If the boy suckles the wet nurse's slave girl or serves her, she gets the full wage because the wet nurse is like a common hire. If the wet nurse hires another wet nurse and she suckles him, she gets the wage by istihsan. If she stipulates that she herself suckle the boy, then she suckles him with someone else, she gets the wage because stipulating suckling by herself is useless. If they dispute: the boy's family say, 'You suckled him with sheep's milk, so no wage for you,' and she says, 'I suckled him with human milk, so I deserve the wage,' then her word is taken with her oath because the apparent circumstance witnesses for her. If they both bring evidence, the evidence of the woman is preferred because it is affirmative. If they stipulate that she suckle the boy in the father's house, then the wet nurse may not take him out because suckling in the father's house is better for the boy. They may not detain the wet nurse in their house if they did not stipulate that. It is not hidden that the term must be known; hence it is said in al-Tajrid: The term must be known, and what is valid in hiring a slave for service is valid in the wet nurse, and what is invalid there is invalid here. In al-Asl: When this hiring is valid, then if they stipulate in the contract that she suckle the boy in the father's house, it is considered; if there is no stipulation, custom is considered: if she habitually suckles in the father's house, it is considered; if in her house, it is considered; otherwise she has the choice: if she wishes, she may suckle in the father's house or in her house. Al-Akmal said: If you ask, is the wet nurse a specialized or common hire? I say: She is a specialized hire; the wording of al-Mabsut indicates this: he said: If the boy is lost from her hand, or falls and dies, or something of his jewelry or clothes is stolen, the wet nurse is not liable because she is like a specialized hire. In al-Dhakhira, something is mentioned indicating that just as she can be common, she can also be specialized: He said: If she hires herself to other people without the knowledge of the first, and suckles each, it is valid, and she becomes a trustee, and this is treachery from her, and she gets the full wage from both parties. This indicates that she admits both possibilities; so we say the wage is due in full because she is common, but she sins because she is specialized.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the contract of hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-zhi'r). The commentator begins by noting a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: some say the contract is primarily on the milk, with upbringing and service being subsidiary; Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani favored this, and it is deemed more correct by many. The passage then clarifies who can be a wet nurse: any lactating woman, regardless of religion, status (free or slave), including mukataba (a slave who has contracted manumission). It then addresses a specific case: if a mukataba becomes unable to pay and returns to slavery, Abu Yusuf holds the contract remains valid, while Muhammad invalidates it. The ruling that a sinful or non-Muslim slave woman may be hired as a wet nurse is justified because hiring is a form of commerce, and it is valid. The text then discusses various scenarios: if the boy suckles the wet nurse's own slave girl, she still gets the full wage because the wet nurse is considered a common hire (ajir mushtarak) for that moment. If she hires another wet nurse to suckle the boy, that second wet nurse gets her wage by istihsan because the first wet nurse is like an intermediary. Stipulating that she herself must suckle is not effective; if she delegates to another, she still gets the wage. Regarding disputes about the type of milk (human vs. animal), the woman's statement is trusted with her oath because the apparent circumstance (normal practice) supports her. If both bring evidence, the woman's evidence is preferred as it affirms her claim. The place of feeding: if stipulated in the father's home, she must comply; if not, custom determines; otherwise she has a choice. The term of the contract must be known. Finally, the classification of the wet nurse: according to al-Mabsut, she is a specialized hire (ajir khas) because she is not liable for loss of the child. However, al-Dhakhira suggests she can be either specialized or common; if she simultaneously works for others without informing the first, she gets the full wage from both (as a common hire) but sins due to the breach of trust (as a specialized hire).

Key Terms
ظئر (zhi'r): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specialized hiree (employee) who works exclusively for one employer during the term
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hiree who offers services to the public and is liable for loss

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the family claims the wet nurse used sheep's milk and she denies it, how is the dispute resolved?
A) The family must provide two male witnesses.
B) The wet nurse's word is taken with her oath.
C) The wet nurse must pay back any wage received.
D) The contract is voided.

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse's word is taken in disputes about milk type, and she may subcontract by istihsan; custom governs the place of feeding.

The Wet Nurse's Payment: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas in Specifying Wages
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijara with unspecified wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa allows hiring a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing by istihsan, and identify the conditions under which the contract is valid.

Core Idea
Custom overrides analogy when unknown wages do not lead to dispute.

In Hanafi fiqh, hiring a wet nurse (ijara) normally requires a known wage. However, Imam Abu Hanifa makes an exception based on custom: paying the wet nurse with food and clothing without specification is valid by istihsan. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue by qiyas that the unknown wage invalidates the contract. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling per each Imam
The act is hiring a wet nurse with her food and clothing as payment. Imam Abu Hanifa says it is valid (sahih); the Sahibayn say it is invalid (batil) by qiyas.
2
State the qiyas argument of the Sahibayn
They analogize to hiring a woman for cooking with unspecified food: the wage is unknown (jahalah), which leads to invalidity. Here too, the food and clothing are unspecified.
The illa is 'unknown wage that may cause dispute'.
3
Explain the istihsan objection of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam says that the illa (dispute) is absent because custom (urf) ensures generosity and compassion for the child. Disputes rarely arise, so the unknown wage does not invalidate.
Istihsan is used to avoid harshness of qiyas.
4
Note the conditions for validity from the commentary
If the type and quantity are specified, all agree it is valid. If unspecified, she gets the medium quality. For clothing, a term must be stated because it cannot be owed as a description except deferred.
These conditions come from al-Haddadi and al-Khulasa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Imam Abu Hanifa's view – the contract is valid by istihsan. This is supported by custom and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
Zahir al-riwayah records this as the school's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وبطعامها وكسوتها وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : لا يجوز وهو القياس . وجه قولهما أن الأجرة مجهولة فصار كما إذا استأجرها للطبخ والخبز والجهالة لا تفضي إلى المنازعة لأن العادة جرت بالتوسعة عليها شفقة على الأولاد بل يعطيها ما طلبت ويوافقها على مرادها، والجهالة إنما تمنع إذا أفضت إلى المنازعة . أطلق في طعامها أو كسوتها فشمل ما إذا بين جنسها أو لم يبين . قال الحدادي : إذا لم يوصف ذلك فلها المتوسط. وفي الخلاصة: وإذا بين جنس الثياب أو صفتها وعرضها وبين كيل الطعام وصفته جاز بالاتفاق اهـ. وفي المحيط : لو اشترطت طعامها وكسوتها عند ستة أشهر وسمت دراهم مسماة عند الفطام ولم تضف شيئاً . ذلك جاز استحساناً عند الإمام. وقالوا : معنى تسميته الدراهم أن يجعل الأجرة دراهم ثم يدفع الطعام مكان الدراهم فيكون معناه على التقدير سما بدل الدراهم طعاماً، وإذا بين كيل الطعام وصفته جاز بالاتفاق، سواء كان حالاً أو مؤجلاً. ولا يشترط أن يذكر أجلاً، وفي الكسوة يشترط بيان الأجل لأنها لا تثبت يوصوفة في الذمة إلا مؤجلاً؛ كذا في الشارح وغيره.
The author said: (And with her food and clothing). This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two said: It is not permissible, and that is the qiyas. The face of their argument is that the wage is unknown, so it becomes like hiring her for cooking and baking. But ignorance does not lead to dispute because custom has made it generous out of compassion for children; rather, he gives what she asks and agrees to her wish. Ignorance only prevents when it leads to dispute. He made it absolute in her food or clothing, so it includes whether its type is specified or not. Al-Haddadi said: If it is not described, she gets the middle. In al-Khulasa: If the type or quality and width of clothes, and the measure and description of food are specified, it is permissible by agreement. In al-Muhit: If she stipulates her food and clothing after six months and specifies named dirhams at weaning without adding anything, that is permissible by istihsan according to Imam. They said: The meaning of naming dirhams is that he makes the wage dirhams, then gives food in place of dirhams, so it means nominally he substituted food for dirhams. If the measure and description of food are specified, it is permissible by agreement, whether immediate or deferred. It is not required to mention a term, but in clothing, specifying the term is required because it cannot be established as described in the liability except as deferred.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage presents the matn statement 'وبطعامها وكسوتها' (and with her food and clothing) and the surrounding commentary. The matn indicates that hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing is valid, but this is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa only. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not valid, and that is the qiyas (analogical reasoning). Their reasoning: the wage (food and clothing) is unspecified and thus unknown, which should invalidate the contract by analogy to hiring for cooking where unspecified food leads to invalidity. However, Imam Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: custom allows this because the employer is generous for the child's sake, and disputes rarely arise. If no description is given, the wet nurse gets the medium quality. If the type and quantity are specified, all agree it is valid. The commentary further explains that if the parties agree on a certain amount of dirhams at weaning but instead give food, it is valid by istihsan. For clothing, since it cannot be owed as a described obligation except deferred, a term must be specified. The key takeaway: the Hanafi school follows Imam Abu Hanifa's view here, allowing payment with unspecified food and clothing due to custom and necessity.

Key Terms
طعامها وكسوتها (ta'amiha wa kiswatiha): The wet nurse's food and clothing as payment for her services
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to custom, necessity, or equity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa allow hiring a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing, while the Sahibayn disallow it?
A) Imam uses qiyas, while the Sahibayn use istihsan.
B) The Sahibayn consider the wage unknown, Imam says custom prevents dispute.
C) Imam relies on the hadith of the wet nurse, the Sahibayn on the Quran.
D) Both agree it is valid if the term is specified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, paying a wet nurse with unspecified food and clothing is valid by istihsan because custom ensures fairness and prevents disputes.

Husband's Right to Rescind the Wet Nurse Contract
States the husband's right to rescind the wet nurse contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a husband can rescind a wet nurse hire contract and apply them to a scenario.

Core Idea
Husband's right to intercourse cannot be overridden by a hire contract; he can rescind if not informed.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the husband's marital rights take precedence over a hire contract for nursing. The key is whether the husband knew and consented; if not, he may rescind, even if the contract was made without his knowledge. The ruling protects the husband's dignity and marital privacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband’s right
Recognize that the husband has a right to intercourse with his wife, which the hirer cannot invalidate.
2
Determine when rescission is allowed
The husband can rescind the contract if he did not know about it. The text says: 'إذا لم يعلم به'.
This is the primary condition.
3
Consider the dishonor factor
According to the preferred view, dishonor is irrelevant; the husband can rescind whether it dishonors him or not. The text says 'وهو الأصح'.
There is a contrary view from al-Asl that only dishonor triggers rescission.
4
Apply to noble women
If the woman is from nobility, her guardians can rescind to remove disgrace, even without the husband's objection.
This is an additional right for guardians.
5
Note the guardian's power over relatives
The guardian of the child can prevent the wet nurse's relatives from staying, and can restrict visiting if it harms the child's care.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يمنع الزوج من وطئها لأنه حقه فلا يمكن المستأجر من إبطاله ولهذا كان للزوج أن يفسخ هذا العقد إذا لم يعلم به سواء كان يشينه إجارتها بأن كان وجيهاً بين الناس أو لم يشنه وهو الأصح، كما له أن يمنعها من الخروج وأن يمنع الصبي من الدخول عليها لأن الإرضاع والسهر يذهب جمالها فكان له أن يمنعها من ذلك كما يمنعها من الصيام تطوعاً لكن إذا ثبتت الزوجية بإقرارهما ليس لها أن تفسخ لأنهما لا يصدقان في حق المستأجر كما إذا أقرت المنكوحة بالرق لا تصدق في حق بطلان النكاح وللمستأجر أن يمنع زوجها من دخول بيته. وفي الأصل : إذا عقدت بغير إذن الزوج والزوج لا يشينه ذلك فليس له حق الفسخ في الصحيح، والمرأة إذا كانت من الاشراف وأجرت نفسها ظئراً فللأولياء حق الفسخ لدفع العار عنهم. وفي الظهيرية ولولي الصبي أن يمنع أقارب الظئر من المكث في منزله، وأما الزيارة إذا كان يؤدي ذلك إلى الإخلال بالقيام بمصالح الصغير له حق المنع وإلا فلا. قال رحمه الله : (فإن مرضت أو حبلت فسخت) يعني إذا حبلت المرضعة أو مرضت فتفسخ الإجارة لأن لبن الحبلى والمريضة يضر الصغير وهي أيضاً يضرها الإرضاع فكان لها ولهم الخيار. ولو تقايأ الصبي لبنها لأهله الفسخ، وكذا إذا كانت سارقة، وكذا إذا كانت فاجرة ظاهر فجورها بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة. قال في النهاية ولا يبعد أن يقال عيب الفجور
The author said: (And the husband is not to be prevented from intercourse with her) because it is his right, so the hirer cannot annul it. Hence, the husband has the right to rescind this contract if he did not know about it, whether it dishonors him (if he is a notable among people) or not — this is the most correct view. Just as he may prevent her from going out and prevent the boy from entering upon her, because nursing and staying up take away her beauty, so he may prevent her from that, just as he prevents her from voluntary fasting. But if the marriage is established by their admission, she may not rescind because they are not believed against the hirer, just as if a married woman admits to being a slave, she is not believed for annulment of the marriage. And the hirer may prevent her husband from entering his house. In al-Asl: If she contracted without the husband's permission and it does not dishonor him, he does not have the right to rescind in the correct view. If the woman is from nobility and hires herself as a wet nurse, the guardians have the right to rescind to remove disgrace from them. In al-Zahiriyyah: The guardian of the small child may prevent the relatives of the wet nurse from staying in his house. As for visiting, if it leads to neglect of the child's welfare, he has the right to prevent; otherwise not. The author said: (So if she becomes ill or pregnant, it is rescinded), meaning if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, the hire is rescinded because the milk of a pregnant or sick woman harms the child, and nursing also harms her, so they both have the option. If the boy vomits her milk, her family has the right to rescind. Likewise if she is a thief, and likewise if she is openly sinful, unlike if she is a disbeliever. It is said in al-Nihaya: It is not far that the defect of sinfulness... (text incomplete).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers two matn statements. First: 'ولا يمنع الزوج من وطئها' — the husband of the wet nurse cannot be prevented from having intercourse with her, as that is his right. The hirer cannot annul this right. Hence, the husband has the right to rescind the hire contract if he did not consent, regardless of whether it dishonors him. He may also prevent her from going out and prevent the boy from entering upon her, because nursing affects her beauty, similar to preventing voluntary fasting. However, if the marriage is established by their own admission, the wife cannot rescind unilaterally. The hirer can prevent the husband from entering his house. If the contract was made without the husband's permission and it does not dishonor him, he has no right to rescind. If the woman is from a noble family, her guardians may rescind to avoid disgrace. The guardian of the child may prevent the wet nurse's relatives from staying. Second matn: 'فإن مرضت أو حبلت فسخت' — if the wet nurse becomes ill or pregnant, the contract is rescinded because her milk becomes harmful to the child and nursing harms her. Both parties have the option to terminate. Other defects like thievery or open sin also give the right to rescind, but not merely being a disbeliever. The passage emphasizes the rights of the husband and the protection of the child's welfare.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or termination of the contract unilaterally due to a right or defect
وجيهاً (wajihan): A person of high standing, notable in the community
أصح (asahh): Most correct; the preferred view in the school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does the husband have the right to rescind the wet nurse contract according to the preferred view?
A) If he is a notable and it dishonors him.
B) If he did not know about the contract.
C) If the wet nurse is a sinner.
D) If the wet nurse becomes ill.

Key Takeaway
A husband can rescind a wet nurse hire contract if he did not know about it, regardless of whether it dishonors him.

Rescission Due to Illness, Pregnancy, or Other Defects
States when a wet nurse contract is rescinded due to defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defects that give the right to rescind a wet nurse hire contract and explain why.

Core Idea
Illness or pregnancy of the wet nurse harms the child and her, thus both parties may rescind the hire.

The second matn in the passage addresses situations where the wet nurse becomes unfit due to illness or pregnancy. The goal is to protect the child's health and the wet nurse's wellbeing. The ruling also extends to other defects such as thievery or open sin. This lesson explains the rationale and scope of these rescissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defects mentioned
The text lists: illness (مرضت), pregnancy (حبلت), theft (سارقة), open sin (فاجرة ظاهر فجورها). Also, the child vomiting her milk (تقيأ اللبن).
Note that disbelief is not a defect.
2
Understand the rationale
Illness and pregnancy harm both the child (bad milk) and the wet nurse (nursing harmful). Theft and open sin affect trust.
3
Identify who has the option to rescind
For illness/pregnancy: the wet nurse and the hirer both have the option (خيار). For theft/sin: the hirer can rescind? The text says 'فسخت' implying rescission occurs; al-Nihaya considers sin as a defect.
The text is clear that for vomiting, the child's family has the right.
4
Apply the rule to new cases
Any defect that harms the child or makes the wet nurse unfit gives the right to rescind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يمنع الزوج من وطئها لأنه حقه فلا يمكن المستأجر من إبطاله ولهذا كان للزوج أن يفسخ هذا العقد إذا لم يعلم به سواء كان يشينه إجارتها بأن كان وجيهاً بين الناس أو لم يشنه وهو الأصح، كما له أن يمنعها من الخروج وأن يمنع الصبي من الدخول عليها لأن الإرضاع والسهر يذهب جمالها فكان له أن يمنعها من ذلك كما يمنعها من الصيام تطوعاً لكن إذا ثبتت الزوجية بإقرارهما ليس لها أن تفسخ لأنهما لا يصدقان في حق المستأجر كما إذا أقرت المنكوحة بالرق لا تصدق في حق بطلان النكاح وللمستأجر أن يمنع زوجها من دخول بيته. وفي الأصل : إذا عقدت بغير إذن الزوج والزوج لا يشينه ذلك فليس له حق الفسخ في الصحيح، والمرأة إذا كانت من الاشراف وأجرت نفسها ظئراً فللأولياء حق الفسخ لدفع العار عنهم. وفي الظهيرية ولولي الصبي أن يمنع أقارب الظئر من المكث في منزله، وأما الزيارة إذا كان يؤدي ذلك إلى الإخلال بالقيام بمصالح الصغير له حق المنع وإلا فلا. قال رحمه الله : (فإن مرضت أو حبلت فسخت) يعني إذا حبلت المرضعة أو مرضت فتفسخ الإجارة لأن لبن الحبلى والمريضة يضر الصغير وهي أيضاً يضرها الإرضاع فكان لها ولهم الخيار. ولو تقايأ الصبي لبنها لأهله الفسخ، وكذا إذا كانت سارقة، وكذا إذا كانت فاجرة ظاهر فجورها بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة. قال في النهاية ولا يبعد أن يقال عيب الفجور
The author said: (And the husband is not to be prevented from intercourse with her) because it is his right, so the hirer cannot annul it. Hence, the husband has the right to rescind this contract if he did not know about it, whether it dishonors him (if he is a notable among people) or not — this is the most correct view. Just as he may prevent her from going out and prevent the boy from entering upon her, because nursing and staying up take away her beauty, so he may prevent her from that, just as he prevents her from voluntary fasting. But if the marriage is established by their admission, she may not rescind because they are not believed against the hirer, just as if a married woman admits to being a slave, she is not believed for annulment of the marriage. And the hirer may prevent her husband from entering his house. In al-Asl: If she contracted without the husband's permission and it does not dishonor him, he does not have the right to rescind in the correct view. If the woman is from nobility and hires herself as a wet nurse, the guardians have the right to rescind to remove disgrace from them. In al-Zahiriyyah: The guardian of the small child may prevent the relatives of the wet nurse from staying in his house. As for visiting, if it leads to neglect of the child's welfare, he has the right to prevent; otherwise not. The author said: (So if she becomes ill or pregnant, it is rescinded), meaning if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, the hire is rescinded because the milk of a pregnant or sick woman harms the child, and nursing also harms her, so they both have the option. If the boy vomits her milk, her family has the right to rescind. Likewise if she is a thief, and likewise if she is openly sinful, unlike if she is a disbeliever. It is said in al-Nihaya: It is not far that the defect of sinfulness... (text incomplete).
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage covers two matn statements. First: 'ولا يمنع الزوج من وطئها' — the husband of the wet nurse cannot be prevented from having intercourse with her, as that is his right. The hirer cannot annul this right. Hence, the husband has the right to rescind the hire contract if he did not consent, regardless of whether it dishonors him. He may also prevent her from going out and prevent the boy from entering upon her, because nursing affects her beauty, similar to preventing voluntary fasting. However, if the marriage is established by their own admission, the wife cannot rescind unilaterally. The hirer can prevent the husband from entering his house. If the contract was made without the husband's permission and it does not dishonor him, he has no right to rescind. If the woman is from a noble family, her guardians may rescind to avoid disgrace. The guardian of the child may prevent the wet nurse's relatives from staying. Second matn: 'فإن مرضت أو حبلت فسخت' — if the wet nurse becomes ill or pregnant, the contract is rescinded because her milk becomes harmful to the child and nursing harms her. Both parties have the option to terminate. Other defects like thievery or open sin also give the right to rescind, but not merely being a disbeliever. The passage emphasizes the rights of the husband and the protection of the child's welfare.

Key Terms
فاجرة (fajira): A woman who is openly sinful (e.g., prostitute or flagrant sinner)
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind a contract
تقايأ (taqayya'a): Vomited (referring to the child vomiting the wet nurse's milk)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a defect that gives the right to rescind a wet nurse contract?
A) Illness of the wet nurse
B) Pregnancy of the wet nurse
C) The wet nurse being a disbeliever
D) Open sin of the wet nurse

Key Takeaway
Illness, pregnancy, theft, and open sin are defects that allow rescission of the wet nurse hire contract to protect the child and the wet nurse.

Conditions of Wet Nurse Hire and Wage Liability
Explains validity conditions and wage responsibility in wet nurse hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid wet nurse hire contract and apply the Hanafi rulings on wage liability when the father dies or the infant has no wealth.

Core Idea
A wet nurse contract requires clear specification of compensation; wage liability depends on the infant's wealth and guardianship after the father's death.

This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses two key issues in hiring a wet nurse: what must be specified in the contract to make it valid, and who is liable for the wage in various scenarios. The author explains the conditions for specifying food and clothing, then clarifies that the wage obligation shifts based on whether the infant had wealth at the time of hiring and whether a guardian assumes responsibility. Understanding these rules is essential for ensuring the contract is enforceable and just.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Conditions for Validity
Read the first part regarding specification of clothing and food. Note that for clothing, both description and term are required; for food, only measure and description are sufficient, and no term is needed.
Clothing cannot be a deferred debt without a term; food can be immediate or deferred.
2
Analyze the Istihsan Ruling
The passage cites al-Muhit: if the wet nurse stipulates food and clothing at six months and names dirhams at weaning, it is valid by istihsan. Understand that this is a departure from strict qiyas, allowed because the compensation is effectively specified.
Istihsan here validates a contract where payment is partly in kind and partly deferred.
3
Trace Wage Liability After Father's Death
There are two sub-scenarios: (a) infant had no wealth at hiring → wage was from father, contract voids on death; (b) infant had wealth → contract continues. If uncle offers to pay, it is valid only if he is a guardian.
If uncle is not a guardian, his promise is not binding; it is a matter of knowledge (i.e., his honor).
4
Examine Wet Nurse's Refusal and Husband's Permission
If the wet nurse refuses and the child accepts no other, she is given a choice to continue for like-wage. If she contracted without husband's permission, he may prevent her.
Husband's right to prevent is based on his authority over his wife's time.
5
Identify Residual Rules: Judge Hiring and Relatives' Liability
The judge may hire for an orphan. If the infant has a mother but no wealth, the wage is on relatives according to inheritance shares. The father may hire his own mother (grandmother) for his child.
Relatives' liability is proportional to their potential inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بين جنس الثياب أو صفتها وعرضها وبين كيل الطعام وصفته جاز بالاتفاق اهـ. وفي المحيط : لو اشترطت طعامها وكسوتها عند ستة أشهر وسمت دراهم مسماة عند الفطام ولم تضف شيئاً . ذلك جاز استحساناً عند الإمام. وقالوا : معنى تسميته الدراهم أن يجعل الأجرة دراهم ثم يدفع الطعام مكان الدراهم فيكون معناه على التقدير سما بدل الدراهم طعاماً، وإذا بين كيل الطعام وصفته جاز بالاتفاق، سواء كان حالاً أو مؤجلاً. ولا يشترط أن يذكر أجلاً، وفي الكسوة يشترط بيان الأجل لأنها لا تثبت يوصوفة في الذمة إلا مؤجلاً؛ كذا في الشارح وغيره. ولم يذكر المؤلف لمن تجب عليه أجرة الظئر ونحن نبين ذلك قال في قاضيخان: استأجر ظئراً لترضع ولده شهوراً فمات الأب فقال عم الصغير أرضعيه وأنا أعطيك الأجر فأرضعته شهراً مع ذلك قالوا: إن لم يكن للصغير مال حين استأجرها كانت الأجرة عليه من ماله وإذا مات بطلت، فإذا قال العم ذلك بعد موته ولم يكن وصياً كان ذلك على العلم ولو كان للصغير مال حين استأجرها الأب لا تبطل الإجارة بموت الأب، وإذا امتنع الظئر من الرضاع والصغير لا يأخذ ثدي غيرها تخير على أن ترضعه بأجرة مثلها . قالوا: هذا إذا عقدت بإذن الزوج، وإذا عقدت بغير إذنه فللزوج منعها. وإذا استأجر القاضي ظئراً لليتيم كان حسناً، وإذا كان للرضيع أم وليس له مال فأجرة أرضاعه على أقاربه بقدر ميراثهم منه ، ويجوز للأب أن يستأجر أمه لترضع ولده وبنته وأخته اهـ.
If the type of garments or its description and width are specified, and the measure and description of the food are specified, it is valid by consensus. It is in al-Muhit: If she stipulated her food and clothing at six months and specified named dirhams at weaning without adding anything, that is valid by istihsan according to the Imam. They said: The meaning of specifying the dirhams is that he makes the wage dirhams then pays food in place of dirhams, so its meaning is based on the estimation that he specified food as a substitute for dirhams. And if the measure of food and its description are specified, it is valid by consensus, whether it is immediate or deferred. It is not required to mention a term, but in clothing, specifying a term is required because it is not established as described in the debt except deferred; likewise in al-Sharh and others. And the author did not mention on whom the wage of the wet nurse is obligatory, and we will explain that. He said in Qadikhan: He hired a wet nurse to breastfeed his child for months, then the father died. The child's uncle said: 'Breastfeed him and I will give you the wage.' She breastfed him for a month with that. They said: If the child had no wealth at the time of hiring, the wage was due from his wealth, and when he died, it becomes void. And if the uncle said that after his death and was not a guardian, it is upon knowledge. And if the child had wealth at the time the father hired her, the hiring is not void by the father's death. And if the wet nurse refuses to breastfeed and the child does not accept the breast of another, she is given the choice to breastfeed him for her like-wage. They said: This is if she contracted with the husband's permission; if she contracted without his permission, the husband has the right to prevent her. And if the judge hires a wet nurse for the orphan, it is good. And if the infant has a mother and has no wealth, the wage for his breastfeeding is upon his relatives according to their inheritance share from him. And it is permissible for the father to hire his mother to breastfeed his child, his daughter, and his sister.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqaiq discusses the validity conditions of hiring a wet nurse and the obligation of her wage. First, it states that specifying the type, description, and width of clothing, as well as the measure and description of food in the contract, makes it valid by consensus of the Hanafi school. The commentary from al-Muhit adds that if a woman stipulates her food and clothing at six months and names specific dirhams at weaning, this is valid by istihsan according to Imam Abu Hanifa. This is interpreted as making the wage in dirhams but then substituting food for dirhams, so it is effectively a valid specification. For food, specifying the measure and description is sufficient, whether the wage is immediate or deferred, and no term is required. For clothing, a term must be mentioned because clothing cannot be established as a described debt without deferment. The author then notes that the original text (Kanz) did not specify who is liable for the wet nurse's wage, so he explains from Qadikhan: If the father hires a wet nurse and then dies, the ruling depends on whether the infant had wealth at the time of hiring. If the infant had no wealth, the wage was due from the father, and upon his death the contract becomes void. If the uncle then offers to pay and she nurses, it is valid if the uncle is a guardian; otherwise, it is based on knowledge. If the infant had wealth, the contract does not void upon the father's death. If the wet nurse refuses to nurse and the infant will not accept another, she is given the option to nurse for the like wage. The passage also notes that if the wet nurse contracted with the husband's permission, the husband cannot prevent her; otherwise he may. If the judge hires for an orphan, it is good. If the infant has a mother but no wealth, the relatives must pay the wage according to their inheritance shares. Finally, the father may hire his own mother (the grandmother) to breastfeed his children.

Key Terms
ظئر (z'ir): A woman hired to breastfeed a child who is not her own.
إجارة (ijarah): A contract for hire or service, where compensation is paid for benefit or work.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that allows departure from analogical reasoning for a more suitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a father hires a wet nurse and later dies, and the infant had no wealth at the time of hiring, what becomes of the hire contract?
A) It remains valid and the wage is due from the uncle.
B) It becomes void upon the father's death.
C) The judge becomes liable for the wage.
D) The wet nurse must continue for free.

Key Takeaway
A wet nurse contract is valid only when compensation is clearly specified; wage liability after the father's death hinges on whether the infant possessed wealth at contract formation.

Grounds for Rescinding a Wet Nurse Contract
Defines defects in wet nurse that allow rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the defects that allow rescission of a wet nurse contract and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wet nurse's right to rescind when taunted.

Core Idea
A wet nurse contract is voidable upon certain defects; her right to rescind when taunted is disputed within the Hanafi school.

When hiring a wet nurse, certain defects in her person or conduct may allow the guardians to terminate the contract. Conversely, the wet nurse herself may have grounds to rescind under specific circumstances. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates these defects and presents a notable disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on one particular scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage deals with rescission (faskh) of a wet nurse contract. Determine what defects give the guardians the right to rescind, and what gives the wet nurse the right.
2
List the defects from the text
Read the text carefully and compile all defects mentioned for each party. Guardians: infant does not take milk, wet nurse is a disbeliever, adulteress, insane, foolish, refuses to travel, foul-mouthed. Wet nurse: verbal abuse from household, taunting due to infant's attachment.
The passage also notes that the wet nurse's disbelief is not an automatic voidance; a proof is given.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites that prophets had disbelieving wives but never married prostitutes. This illustrates that internal belief does not necessarily invalidate a contract. Understand how this proof relates to the wet nurse's defect.
The proof is a hadith: 'ما بعت امرأة نبي قط' (no prophet married a prostitute).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the infant becomes attached only to the wet nurse and she is taunted, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say she has the right to rescind. Abu Yusuf says she does not. Identify the differing views.
Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani favors Abu Yusuf's view as the relied-upon position.
5
Determine the operative ruling
The mufta bihi for the dispute is that the wet nurse cannot rescind in that case. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: if she rescinds, she may leave; otherwise, she must continue nursing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في هذا فوق عيب الكفر لأن كفرها في اعتقادها ألا ترى أنه كان في نساء بعض الرسل كامرأتي نوح ولوط عليهما الصلاة والسلام وما بعت امرأة نبي قط؛ هكذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام. ولم يتزوج نبي فاجرة وكذا إذا كان الصبي لا يأخذ لبنها كان لهم أن يفسخوا ولها ذلك أيضاً، وكذا إذا عيرت به ولو مات الصبي أو الظئر انقضت الإجارة. وفي الخانية : إذا ظهر الظئر كافرة أو زانية أو مجنونة أو حمقاء كان لهم الفسخ . وفي الأصل: أرادوا سفراً وأبت الخروج فلهم الفسخ، وكذا إذا كانت سيئة بذية اللسان، وكذا إذا أذاها أهله باللسان كان لها الفسخ، وكذا إذا كان ألفها الصبي ولم يأخذ لبن غيرها وهي تعير بذلك كان لها الفسخ في ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي يوسف ليس لها الفسخ قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : الاعتماد على رواية أبي يوسف. وفي المحيط : انتهت مدة إرضاع الظئر والصغير لا يأخذ إلا ثديها تبقى الإجارة بأجرة المثل جبراً عليها لأن الإجارة كما لا تفسخ بالأعذار تبقى بالأعذار.
This is above the defect of disbelief because her disbelief is in her belief. Do you not see that among the wives of some messengers were the two wives of Nuh and Lut, peace be upon them, and he never married a prostitute; thus said the Prophet, peace be upon him. And no prophet married a prostitute. Likewise, if the infant does not take her milk, they may rescind, and she also has that right. Likewise, if she is taunted because of it. And if the infant or the wet nurse dies, the hire contract is terminated. And in al-Khaniyya: If the wet nurse appears to be a disbeliever, adulteress, insane, or foolish, they have the right to rescind. And in al-Asl: If they intend to travel and she refuses to go out, they have the right to rescind. Likewise, if she is ill-tongued and foul-mouthed. Likewise, if her household verbally abuses her, she has the right to rescind. Likewise, if the infant becomes attached to her and does not take any other milk and she is taunted because of that, she has the right to rescind in the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf: she does not have the right to rescind. Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani said: The reliance is on the narration of Abu Yusuf. And in al-Muhit: If the term of the wet nurse's nursing ends and the infant takes only her breast, the contract remains with the wages of the like, coerced upon her, because just as a hire contract is not rescinded due to excuses, it remains due to excuses.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the grounds for rescinding a wet nurse (ẓi'r) contract. It begins by stating that the defect of disbelief is above other defects because her disbelief is an internal belief, yet prophets had disbelieving wives (e.g., Nuh and Lut). However, no prophet married a prostitute. The text then lists various defects that give the infant's guardians the right to rescind: if the infant does not take her milk (i.e., she is unable to nurse), if she is found to be a disbeliever, adulteress, insane, foolish, if she refuses to travel with them, if she is foul-mouthed. Conversely, the wet nurse herself may also rescind if her household verbally abuses her, or if the infant becomes excessively attached to her to the point that she is taunted. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that she cannot rescind in the latter case, and Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani says the relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf. Al-Muhit adds that if the nursing period ends but the infant still only takes her milk, the contract continues with her forced to accept wages of the like, because a hire contract is not terminated by excuses.

Key Terms
ظئر (ẓi'r): A wet nurse hired to nurse an infant.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or termination of a contract due to a defect or excuse.
تعيير (ta'yir): Taunting or reproaching; a ground for the wet nurse to rescind in some narrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wet nurse being beautiful
B) The wet nurse being insane
C) The wet nurse being wealthy
D) The wet nurse being tall

Key Takeaway
Defects such as disbelief, adultery, insanity, foolishness, refusal to travel, and foul language give the guardians the right to rescind; the wet nurse's right when taunted is disputed and the relied-upon view denies it.

Death of a Party in a Wet Nurse Contract
States consequences of death of either party in a wet nurse contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the termination of a wet nurse contract when the infant, wet nurse, or father dies, and explain why the father's death does not terminate it.

Core Idea
Death of the infant or the wet nurse ends the contract; the father's death does not.

This lesson covers a specific ruling within the Hanafi school regarding hire contracts (ijara) for wet nurses. The death of the person being nursed (the infant) or the nurse herself terminates the agreement because the service becomes impossible. However, the death of the father who hired the nurse does not affect the contract; the obligation to pay wages continues from the infant's estate or other guardians.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three parties
The infant (mahall), the wet nurse (ajir), and the father (musta'jir). The father is the one who contracts and pays wages.
2
Apply the general rule for death in personal service contracts
In Hanafi fiqh, death of either party to a personal service contract typically terminates it. But note the exception here.
3
Apply to the infant's death
Since the infant is the subject of the service, his death makes performance impossible → contract ends.
4
Apply to the wet nurse's death
Since she is the service provider, her death makes performance impossible → contract ends.
5
Apply to the father's death
The father is not the direct service provider or receiver; he is a third-party hirer. His death does not affect the need for or possibility of the service. Therefore the contract continues. The father's obligation to pay may shift to the infant's estate.
This is the exception to the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات الصبي أو الظئر انقضت الإجارة. ولو مات أبو الصغير لم تنقض الإجارة سواء كان للصغير مال أو لم يكن له مال.
And if the infant or the wet nurse dies, the hire contract is terminated. And if the infant's father dies, the contract is not terminated, whether the infant has wealth or not.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This brief ruling addresses the effect of death on a wet nurse (ẓi'r) contract. If the infant dies, the contract ends because the purpose of the contract (nursing the infant) is impossible. Similarly, if the wet nurse dies, she is no longer able to perform the service. However, the death of the infant's father does not terminate the contract. The father is the one who contracts with the wet nurse and pays the wages; his death does not affect the need for nursing. The infant may have wealth from which wages can be paid, or if not, the responsibility may shift to the mother or other relatives, but the contract remains valid and continues.

Key Terms
انقضت الإجارة (inqaḍat al-ijārah): The hire contract is terminated automatically upon the death of one of the parties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Does the death of the infant's father terminate the wet nurse contract?
A) Yes, because the father pays
B) No, the contract continues
C) Yes, if the infant has no wealth
D) No, but only if the infant has wealth

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse contract ends upon death of the infant or wet nurse, but continues after the father's death.

Partial Termination of a Nursing Contract When One of Two Infants or Wet Nurses Dies
Explains effect of death of one of two nursed infants on wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios of death of a subject in a nursing contract and apply the correct wage division.

Core Idea
Death of one subject splits the wage equally for equal subjects (infants), proportionally for unequal subjects (wet nurses).

This lesson delves into the partial termination of a nursing contract. When one of the two nursed infants dies, the contract is partially void, and half the wage is forfeited. But if one of the two wet nurses dies, the contract continues for the surviving nurse with a proportional wage adjustment. The key distinction lies in whether the subjects are equal (infants) or unequal (wet nurses) in their claim to the wage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize the two cases: (1) a single wet nurse hired for two infants, and (2) two wet nurses hired for an infant or infants. Note the different outcomes when one subject dies.
2
Understand the reasoning for infants
When one infant dies, the other infant's entitlement to the wet nurse's milk is a full half of the compensation (the milk). Since the contract was for both, each infant gets an equal share, so half the wage is forfeited.
The infants are considered equal in entitlement.
3
Understand the reasoning for wet nurses
When one wet nurse dies, the surviving wet nurse continues the contract. The wage is divided between them based on their individual nursing value (value of their milk), which may differ. Hence, the wage split is proportional to their worth.
Wet nurses vary in ability, so the wage is not equal.
4
Contrast the two reasonings
The difference hinges on the nature of the subjects: infants are equal in their need for milk, so their shares are equal. Wet nurses provide service of different value, so their compensation is proportional.
This distinction is the key legal point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استأجرها لترضع صبيين كل شهر بكذا فمات أحدهما سقط نصف الأجرة لأنها لا يمكنها الوفاء بهذا فانفسخت الإجارة ولو استأجر ظئرين فمات أحدهما بقي العقد في وانفسخ في الأخرى بحصتها والفرق بين هذا وبين ما إذا مات أحد الصبيين أن في الظئر يقسم الأجر عليهما باعتبار قيمته لأنهما متفاوتان في الارضاع وفي الصبي الإيجار وقع لهما واستحق كل واحد منهما نصف البدل وهو لبن الظئر فيجب المبدل عليهما نصفان اهـ.
And if he hired her to nurse two infants each month for a certain amount, and one of the two died, half the wages are forfeited because she cannot fulfill this, so the contract is terminated. And if he hired two wet nurses and one of them died, the contract remains in effect regarding one and is terminated regarding the other for its share. The difference between this and when one of the two infants dies is that in the case of the wet nurses, the wage is divided between them based on their value because they differ in nursing ability. In the case of the infants, the hire contract was made for both, and each is entitled to half of the compensation, which is the wet nurse's milk, so the compensation is divided equally between them.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage examines two scenarios. First, if a single wet nurse is hired to nurse two infants for a fixed monthly wage, and one infant dies, she cannot provide full nursing for the remaining infant because the contract was for both. Hence, the contract is partially void and the wage is reduced by half. Second, if two wet nurses are hired and one dies, the contract continues for the surviving wet nurse and terminates for the deceased one, with the wage divided proportionally based on their respective nursing value. The key difference is that when the infants are the subjects, they are considered equal in entitlement to the milk (each gets half), so the wage splits equally upon death of one. But wet nurses have different values, so the wage split is proportional to their value, not equal.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Compensation or consideration in a contract; here, the wage for nursing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where two wet nurses are hired and one dies, how is the wage divided?
A) Equally between the two
B) According to their value in nursing
C) The contract is entirely void
D) The wage goes entirely to the surviving nurse

Key Takeaway
The death of one subject in a joint nursing contract triggers partial termination; wage division depends on the equality or inequality of the subjects.

Hiring One's Wife or a Sheep to Nurse
Rulings on validity of hiring wife or animal to nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three nursing contract scenarios and explain the legal distinction between human milk and animal milk.

Core Idea
Wife's milk is a service, sheep's milk is a commodity—uncertainty in commodity invalidates the lease.

In this passage from al-Muntaqa, the Hanafi jurist discusses three cases involving the leasing of nursing services. The first case, hiring one's wife to nurse, is valid because her milk is considered a service, not a saleable item. The second case, hiring a sheep, is invalid because animal milk has market value and the amount is unknown, creating gharar (uncertainty). The third case, hiring a wet nurse for a foundling, places the financial burden on the finder, who acts voluntarily. We will examine the reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Distinguish between hiring one's wife, hiring a sheep, and hiring a wet nurse for a foundling. Note the subject and the context of each.
The passage uses the term 'istājara' for 'hire'.
2
Determine the ruling for each
State the legal outcome: valid (jā’iz), invalid (lā yajūz), or voluntary (mutṭawwi‘).
The wife case is permissible; the sheep case is not permissible; the foundling case places wages on the finder.
3
Analyze the rationale for wife vs. sheep
The key distinction is whether the milk has market value. A wife's milk has no value in this context; it is part of her service. A sheep's milk is a valuable commodity, and the contract would be for an unknown quantity, which is gharar.
Gharar (uncertainty) invalidates contracts in Islamic law.
4
Understand the foundling case
The finder has no legal guardianship over the foundling, so he acts voluntarily. He cannot claim reimbursement from the foundling's wealth unless authorized by a judge.
The term 'mutṭawwi‘' means volunteer, acting without compensation claim.
5
Summarize the underlying rule
For an ijara (hire) contract to be valid, the subject matter must be known (ma‘lūm) and deliverable. The sheep's milk is unknown in amount, violating this condition.
This principle is derived from the general prohibition of gharar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المنتقى : استأجر مرأته لترضع ابنه من مال الصغير فهو جائز، ولو استأجر شاة لترضع ولده لا يجوز لأن لبن البهائم له قيمة فوقعت الإجارة عليه وهو مجهول فلا يجوز بخلاف لبن المرأة لأنه لا قيمة له والإجارة على الخدمة ولو التقط صبياً فاستأجر له ظئراً حالاً فالأجرة عليه وهو متطوع لأنه لا ولاية له على الصبي اهـ.
And in al-Muntaqa: If he hires his wife to nurse his son from the child's wealth, it is permissible. And if he hires a sheep to nurse his child, it is not permissible because the milk of animals has value, so the hire contract falls upon it and it is unknown, so it is not permissible, unlike the milk of a woman because it has no value and the hire is for service. And if he picks up a foundling and hires a wet nurse for him immediately, the wages are upon him, and he is a volunteer because he has no guardianship over the foundling.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage from al-Muntaqa discusses three scenarios. First, a man may hire his own wife to nurse his child, paying from the child's own wealth (if the child has wealth). This is valid because the wife's milk is considered a service, not a commodity. Second, hiring a sheep to nurse a child is invalid because animal milk has a known market value, so the contract would be for an unknown quantity of milk (gharar), which is prohibited. A woman's milk, by contrast, is not sold on the market; the contract is for her service of nursing, not for her milk as a commodity. Third, if someone finds a foundling (laqīṭ) and hires a wet nurse on the spot, the wages are on the finder, but he is a volunteer (mutṭawwi‘) since he has no legal guardianship over the foundling; he acts out of charity.

Key Terms
الصبي اللقيط (al-ṣabiyy al-laqīṭ): A foundling, an abandoned infant of unknown parentage.
ظئر (ẓa’ir): A wet nurse.
متطوع (muṭṭawi‘): One who acts voluntarily, without legal entitlement to compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hiring a sheep to nurse a child invalid according to the passage?
A) Because sheep are impure animals
B) Because animal milk has value and the amount is unknown
C) Because sheep cannot be trusted
D) Because it is forbidden to milk sheep

Key Takeaway
The validity of a nursing hire contract depends on whether the milk is considered a service (wife) or a commodity (sheep); animal milk creates uncertainty and invalidates the contract.
