Obligations of Wet Nurse and Forfeiture of Wages for Substituting Milk
Specifies wet nurse's duties and ruling on nursing with sheep's milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the contractual obligations of a wet nurse under Hanafi fiqh and explain why substituting sheep's milk for her own milk results in forfeiture of wages.

Core Idea
A wet nurse must nurse from her own breast; using animal milk is not nursing and voids her wage.

In an ijara (hire) contract for a wet nurse, her primary duty is to nurse the infant from her own breast. However, she also has ancillary duties defined by custom, such as preparing food and washing clothes. This lesson examines these obligations and the critical ruling that if she substitutes her milk with animal milk, she forfeits her wage because the act is considered 'ijar' (medicinal feeding) rather than nursing. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
The wet nurse's core duty is to nurse the infant from her own breast. This is the essence of the contract and the basis for wage entitlement.
2
List ancillary duties based on custom
Beyond nursing, she must prepare food, wash clothes, cook and chew food for the infant, and avoid foods that spoil her milk. These are wajib if custom so dictates.
The father provides food and clothes; oil and perfume are disputed.
3
Analyze the role of custom (urf)
Custom determines duties in matters lacking explicit textual ruling. Note the difference between Kufan custom and the relied-upon fatwa regarding oil and perfume.
Al-Mudmarat and the fatwa state oil and perfume are not on the wet nurse.
4
Evaluate the substitution case
If the wet nurse uses sheep's milk, she is not performing the contracted service. The act becomes ijar (pouring medicine) not rida' (nursing).
The source cites al-Sihah for the definition of ijar.
5
Draw the legal consequence
Since she failed to perform the wajib service (nursing), she receives no wage (fala ajr). The wage is conditioned on actual nursing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وعليها إصلاح طعام الصبي لأن خدمة الصبي واجبة عليها وهذا منه عرفا وهو معتبر فيما لا نص فيه وغسل ثيابه منه والطعام والثياب على الوالد والدهن والريحان على الظئر كما هو عادة أهل الكوفة، وفي عرف ديارنا ما يعالج به الصبي على أهل. وفي المضمرات والفتوى على أنه ليس على الظئر الدهن والريحان وطعام الصبي على أهله إذا كان الصبي يأكل الطعام وعلى الظئر أن تهيئه له. وفي الينابيع : وعليها طبخه وعليها أن تمضغ الطعام للصبي ولا تأكل شيئاً يفسد لبنها وتضمن به. قال رحمه الله : (فإن أرضعته بلبن شاة فلا أجر) لأنها لم تأت بالواجب عليها من العمل وهو الإرضاع وهذا إيجار وليس بإرضاع. قال في الصحاح : الوجور الدواء يؤجر في وسط الفم أي يصب يقال له منه وجرت الصبي وأوجر بمعنى واحد.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And upon her is preparing the infant's food because the service of the infant is obligatory upon her, and this is considered customary, and custom is considered in matters where there is no text. And washing his clothes from it. And food and clothes are upon the father, and oil and perfume are upon the wet nurse as is the custom of the people of Kufa. In the custom of our lands, what is used to treat the infant is upon his family. In al-Mudmarat and the fatwa: it is not upon the wet nurse to provide oil and perfume. The infant's food is upon his family if the infant eats food, and upon the wet nurse is to prepare it for him. In al-Yanabi‘: Upon her is cooking it and she must chew the food for the infant, and she must not eat anything that spoils her milk, and she is liable for it. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (If she nurses him with the milk of a sheep, she receives no wage) because she did not fulfill the obligatory work upon her, which is nursing, and this is pouring medicine (ijār) and not nursing. In al-Sihah: al-wujūr is medicine that is poured into the middle of the mouth. It is said: wajartu al-ṣabiyya and awjartu meaning the same.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage outlines the duties of a wet nurse beyond just breastfeeding. According to the author (presumably the commentator), she is responsible for preparing the infant's food (once the infant starts eating solids) and washing his clothes. These duties are considered part of the service contract based on custom. Food and clothes are provided by the father, while oil and perfume for the infant are on the wet nurse according to Kufan custom. However, al-Mudmarat and the relied-upon fatwa state that oil and perfume are not on the wet nurse; rather, the infant's family provides them. If the infant eats food, the family provides it, and the wet nurse only prepares it. She must cook and even chew food for the infant. She must also avoid foods that spoil her milk; if she eats such and harms the milk, she is liable. Finally, if the wet nurse nurses the infant with sheep's milk (i.e., she substitutes her own milk with animal milk), she forfeits her entire wage because she did not perform the contracted service—actual breastfeeding from her own breast. Pouring sheep's milk into the infant's mouth is not considered nursing but rather 'ījār (medicinal feeding), which is a different act.

Key Terms
إيجار (ījār): Pouring medicine or liquid into the mouth of an infant, as opposed to breastfeeding.
الأجرة (al-ujra): The wage or compensation for the wet nurse's services.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She receives full wages
B) She receives half wages because the infant is fed
C) She receives no wages because it is not considered nursing
D) She receives wages of the like for the milk

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse's duty is to personally nurse the infant; substituting any other milk forfeits her wages because it changes the nature of the service.

Hire for a Share of the Output is Invalid (Fasid)
Ruling on invalid hire with share of output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a hire contract paying a share of the output is fasid in the Hanafi school, apply the rule to determine the worker's entitlement to ujrat al-mithl, and evaluate the Balkh scholars' exception based on custom.

Core Idea
Paying wages from the output creates uncertainty and impossibility of delivery, rendering the hire fasid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key ruling in Hanafi ijara law: a contract where the worker is paid from the very thing he produces is invalid (fasid). The text presents the ruling, explains the reasoning via qiyas to the miller's qafiz, addresses objections, and discusses an intra-Hanafi difference with Balkh scholars. We will walk through the legal analysis step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is hiring someone to weave cloth for a share of the cloth, or to carry food for a share of the food. The ruling is that such a contract is not permissible (lam yajuz) – i.e., fasid.
The text gives three examples: weaving for half, carrying for a qafiz, and baking for a dirham. The last is straightforward fixed wage; the first two are the problematic ones.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text uses qiyas to the miller's qafiz (qafiz al-tahhan), a well-known prohibited contract where the miller takes a portion of the flour as wage. The 'illa is that the wages are part of the output, making delivery impossible at the time of contract.
The ability to deliver the wages is a condition for validity of the hire contract. Since the wages do not yet exist, the hirer cannot deliver them.
3
Understand the legal consequence
Even though the contract is fasid, if the work is performed, the worker is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (fair wages) not exceeding the named amount. This is because the work itself is not prohibited.
This distinguishes fasid from batil: in fasid contracts, some legal effects remain, such as the right to fair wages.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Scholars of Balkh permitted such contracts based on custom ('urf) and local practice, setting aside qiyas as in istisna'. However, the majority Hanafi position (including al-Sarakhsi and al-Sayyid al-Shahid) rejects this as a limited custom that does not override general principles.
The mufta bihi is the prohibition; the Balkh view is considered an exception.
5
Know the hila (legal trick)
To avoid the prohibition, they can stipulate an unqualified qafiz (absolute measure) as wages, so that the wages are known and deliverable. Once the work is done, the worker earns that wage.
This hila is mentioned in the text and is a common technique in Hanafi fiqh to achieve a permissible result.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب الإجارة الفاسدة
ولو دفع غزلاً لينسجه بنصفه أو استأجره ليحمل طعامه بقفيز منه أو ليخبز له كذا اليوم بدرهم لم يجز وإن استأجر أرضاً على أن يكر بها ويزرعها أو يسقيها ويزرعها صح وإن |

من باب المشاكلة وهو ذكر الشيء
قلت اطبخوا لي جبة وقميصاً

فذكر المؤلف الإيجار بلفظ الإرضاع لوقوعه في صحبته قيد بلبن الشاة لأنها لو أرضعته بلبن خادمها أو جاريتها أو بلبن ظئر استأجرتها بلا عقد فلها الأجرة كما تقدم . رحمه الله : (ولو دفع غزلاً لينسجه بنصفه أو استأجره ليحمل طعامه بقفيز منه أو ليخبز له كذا اليوم بدرهم لم يجز) لأنه في المسألة الأولى والثانية جعل الأجرة بعض ما يخرج من فيصير في معنى قفيز الطحان ولأن المستأجر عاجز عن تسليم الأجرة لأنه بعض ما يخرج والقدرة على التسليم شرط لصحة العقد وهو لا يقدر على ذلك بنفسه وإنما يقدر بغيره فلا يعد قادراً، فإذا نسج أو عمل فله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى بخلاف ما لو استأجره ليحمل له نصف هذا الطعام بنفصه الآخر حيث لا يجب له شيء من الأجر لأن الأجير ملك فيه النصف في الحال بالتعجيل فصار الطعام مشتركاً بينهما في الحال. ومن حمل طعاماً مشتركاً بينه وبين غيره لا يستحق الأجر. هذا لأنه لا يعمل شيئاً لشريكه عما لا يقع بعضه لنفسه فلا الأجر ؛ هكذا قالوا قال الشارح وفيه إشكالان: أحدهما أن الإجارة فاسدة والأجرة لا تملك إلا في الصحيحة منها بالعقد، سواء كانت عيناً أو ديناً على ما بينا، فكيف تملك هنا من غير تسليم ومن غير شرط التعجيل الثاني أنه قال ملكه في الحال وقوله لا الأجر ينافي الملك لأنه لا يملك إذا ملك بطريق الإجارة فإذا لم يستحق فكيف يملك يستحق يستحق يستحق :
·
وبأي سبب يملك؟ والجواب عن الأول أنه ملك هنا بالتعجيل والتسليم كما صرح هو به في تقریره وصرح به صاحب النهاية ومعراج الدراية حيث قالا دفع إليه. والجواب عن الثاني أنه لا منافاة بين قوله ملكه في الحال وبين قوله ومعنى لا يستحق الأجرة ولا يجب لأن معنى ملكه في الحال يعني ابتداء بموجب العقد وتسليم الأجر إلى الأجير بالتعجيل، ومعنى لا الأجر لبطلان العقد قبل العمل بعد أن ملك الأجر بالتسليم بسبب أنه صار شريكاً في الطعام. قال في النهاية : لو قال احمل لي هذا الكر إلى بغداد بنصفه فإنه لا يكون شريكاً وتفسد الإجارة لأنه في معنى قفيز الطحان وللأجير أجر مثله إن وصل إلى بغداد لا يتجاوز المسمى، ومشايخ بلخ والنسفي جوزوا حمل الطعام ببعض المحمول ونسج الثوب ببعض المنسوج لتعامل أهل بلادهم بذلك، والقياس يترك بالتعامل كما في الاستصناع، ومشايخنا الله لم يجوزوا ذلك وقالوا : هذا التخصيص تعامل أهل بلدة واحدة وبه لا يخص الأثر . والحيلة في جوازه أن يشترطا قفيزاً مطلقاً فإذا عمل استحق الأجرة. وفي الغياثية: دفع إلى حائك ثوباً لينسجه بنصفه أو بثلثه أو ربعه فالإجارة فاسدة عند علمائنا وبه أفتى الإمام السرخسي والسيد الإمام الشهيد ومشايخ بلخ يفتون بالجواز لعرف بلادهم. وفي الظهيرية : أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث وشمس الأئمة الحلواني والقاضي أبو علي النسفي اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : لو استأجر ثوراً ليطحن له أردباً ببعض منه أو حماراً ليحمل له أردباً ببعض منه فالإجارة فاسدة ولو استأجر حانوتاً بنصف ما فيه فالإجارة فاسدة. وفي المحيط : ولو استأجر حائكاً لينسج هذا الثوب بنصفه على أن يزيد رطلاً . من عند فنسج وزاد فله أجر مثل عمله ويضمن صاحب الثوب للحياك رطلاً من الغزل.
Book of Hire, Chapter of Corrupt Hire. And if he gave yarn to weave for half of it, or hired him to carry his food for a qafiz of it, or to bake for him such-and-such a day for a dirham, it is not permissible. And if he hired land that he plow and sow it, or irrigate and sow it, it is valid. Then how does the commentator say: this is hire, not breastfeeding? The answer is that this is by way of using the word for something else due to its occurrence in his company, like his saying: from the category of rhetorical style (mushakala) and it is mentioning the thing. I said: cook a cloak and a shirt for me. He said: its work. So the author mentioned hiring by the word breastfeeding due to its occurrence in his company, restricted by the milk of a ewe, because if she breastfed him with the milk of her servant or her handmaiden or the milk of a wet nurse she hired without a contract, she gets the wages as previously mentioned. May Allah have mercy on him: (And if he gave yarn to weave for half of it, or hired him to carry his food for a qafiz of it, or to bake for him such-and-such a day for a dirham, it is not permissible) because in the first and second issues, he made the wages some of what comes out, so it becomes like the miller's qafiz, and because the hirer is incapable of delivering the wages because it is part of what comes out, and ability to deliver is a condition for the validity of the contract, and he is not able to do that by himself, but only through others, so he is not considered able. So if he wove or worked, he gets wages equal to his work without exceeding the named [amount]. Contrary to if he hired him to carry half of this food with the other half, where nothing of wages is obligatory for him, because the hired person owns the half immediately by advance payment, so the food becomes shared between them immediately. And whoever carries food shared between himself and others does not deserve wages. This is because he does nothing for his partner about what some of it is for himself, so no wages. Thus they said. The commentator said: In it there are two difficulties: one, that the hire is corrupt and wages are only owned in a sound one by contract, whether specific or debt as we explained, so how is it owned here without delivery and without a condition of advance? Second, he said he owns it immediately, and his saying 'no wages' contradicts ownership because he does not own if he owns by way of hire, so if he does not deserve, how does he own? And by what cause does he own? The answer to the first: that he owns here by advance and delivery as he himself clarified in his exposition, and as stated by the author of al-Nihaya and Mi'raj al-Diraya where they said: he paid to him. And the answer to the second: that there is no contradiction between his saying 'he owns it immediately' and his saying and meaning 'he does not deserve wages and it is not obligatory', because the meaning of 'he owns it immediately' is that it begins by virtue of the contract and delivery of wages to the hire by advance, and the meaning of 'no wages' is due to the invalidity of the contract before work after he owned the wages by delivery because he became a partner in the food. He said in al-Nihaya: if he said 'carry this kurr to Baghdad for half of it', then he is not a partner and the hire is corrupt because it is like the miller's qafiz, and the hire has wages equal to his work if he reaches Baghdad, not exceeding the named. And the scholars of Balkh and al-Nasafi permitted carrying food for some of the carried load and weaving cloth for some of the woven due to the practice of the people of their land, and qiyas is abandoned due to practice as in istisna', and our scholars did not permit that and said: this specification is the practice of one town and by it the precedent is not specified. The trick for its validity is that they stipulate an absolute qafiz, then when he works he deserves wages. And in al-Ghiyathiyya: he gave to a weaver a cloth to weave for half of it, or a third, or a fourth, then the hire is corrupt according to our scholars, and by it gave fatwa al-Imam al-Sarakhsi and al-Sayyid al-Imam al-Shahid, and the scholars of Balkh give fatwa of its permissibility due to the custom of their land. And in al-Zahiriyya: taken by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth and Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani and al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi, end. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: if he hired an ox to grind an ardebb for some of it, or a donkey to carry an ardebb for some of it, the hire is corrupt. And if he hired a shop for half of what is in it, the hire is corrupt. And in al-Muhit: and if he hired a weaver to weave this cloth for half of it on condition that he add a ratl from himself, and he wove and added, then he gets wages equal to his work and the owner of the cloth guarantees to the weaver a ratl of yarn.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: hiring for a share of the output is invalid (fāsid). The text first states the ruling: if someone gives yarn to be woven for half the cloth, or hires a person to carry food for a qafīz of that food, or to bake for a day for a dirham, it is not permissible. The commentary then digresses to explain why the author earlier used the term 'hire' in a context of breastfeeding, but that is a side note. The main analysis: in the first two cases, the wages are part of the item produced, making it similar to the miller's qafīz (an established invalid contract). The hirer cannot deliver the wages because they do not yet exist, and ability to deliver is a condition. If the work is done, the worker gets fair wages (ujrat al-mithl) not exceeding the named amount. In contrast, if the hire is to carry half of the food in exchange for the other half, the hired person owns half immediately, so he is carrying his own share and owes nothing. The commentator raises two objections: (1) how can the hired person own the wages when the contract is invalid? (2) how can he own and yet not deserve wages? The answers: (1) he owns through advance delivery, not through the invalid contract; (2) he owns initially by delivery, but the contract is voided before work, so he becomes a partner and thus gets no wage for carrying his own share. Later authorities (al-Nihaya, etc.) affirm the prohibition. However, scholars of Balkh allowed such contracts due to custom, setting aside qiyās, just as istisnā' is permitted. The relied-upon Hanafi position rejects this, considering it a limited custom. A legal trick (hīla) is to stipulate an unqualified qafīz, making the wage a known liability. Various citations (al-Ghiyāthiyya, al-Zāhiriyya, al-Tātārkhāniyya, al-Muhīt) confirm the prohibition and provide additional cases.

Key Terms
الإجارة الفاسدة (al-ijāra al-fāsida): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect in the subject matter or compensation, but not wholly void (bātil). The worker still deserves fair wages for the work done.
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): The miller's qafīz: a prohibited arrangement where the miller takes a portion of the flour as his wage, leading to uncertainty.
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): Fair wages equivalent to what a similar worker would receive for similar work, without exceeding the named amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid hire contract where the wages are part of the output, what does the worker receive?
A) Nothing, because the contract is invalid.
B) The named amount exactly.
C) Ujrat al-mithl not exceeding the named amount.
D) Double the fair wage.

Key Takeaway
Hiring for a share of the output is fasid because the wages are uncertain and undeliverable; the worker still gets fair wages limited to the named amount.

Baking for a Day for a Dirham: Dispute on Combining Time and Work
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hire when both timeframe and specific work are mentioned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the validity of a hire contract that mentions both a timeframe and specific work, and state the practical consequences of each position.

Core Idea
When a hire mentions both time and work, ambiguity arises—Imam says corrupt, Sahibayn say valid if time is merely for urgency.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a hire contract where the employer says 'bake for the day for a dirham.' Does mentioning both the timeframe (the day) and the specific work (baking) render the contract invalid due to uncertainty? Imam Abu Hanifa holds it corrupt (fasid), while his two companions Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider it valid. Let's unpack their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting elements
Notice that the contract contains both a duration ('the day') and a specific task ('baking'). Each points to a different possible object: the benefit of time or the work itself.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Imam says the contract is fasid because the object is ambiguous—no priority can be given to time or work. This uncertainty invalidates the contract.
Imam's ruling leads to fasid, and the worker gets ujrat al-mithl.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
They say the contract is valid and the object is the work; the time is mentioned only for urgency (al-ta'jil). They analogize to hiring to finish by a deadline, which is valid by consensus.
Under the Sahibayn, the contract is valid and the named wage is due upon completion of work.
4
Analyze Imam's distinction
Imam distinguishes that in the matn's case the day is intended as an end (qasād), not merely a description. In the sewing example from al-Ghiyāthiyya, if time is a condition for completion, it may invalidate.
This shows Imam is concerned about whether time is an integral part of the object.
5
Determine the practical difference
Under Imam, contract is fasid, worker gets ujrat al-mithl; under Sahibayn, contract valid, named wage due. Later Hanafi fatwas often adopt Sahibayn's view.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects the amount and enforceability of the wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثالث وهو ما إذا استأجره ليخبز له طول النهار بدرهم فلأن ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المعقود هو المنفعة، وذكر العمل يوجب كون العمل هو المعقود عليه ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر، فإن وقع على المنفعة استحق الأجر بمضي الوقت عمل أو لم يعمل، وإن وقع على العمل لا يستحق إلا بالعمل فيفسد العقد وهو قول الإمام. وقالا : العقد جائز ويكون العقد على العلم دون اليوم حتى إذا فرغ منه نصف النهار فله الأجر، وإن لم يعمل في اليوم فعليه أن يعلم في الغد وذكر اليوم للتعجيل فصار كما إذا استأجره على أن يفرغ منه في هذا اليوم يجوز بالإجماع والفرق للإمام هنا أن اليوم لم يذكر هنا إلا لإثبات صفة في العمل والصفة تابعة للموصوف غير مقصودة بالذات، وفي مسألة الكتاب ذكر اليوم قصاداً. وفي الغياثية : لو استأجره ليخيط له هذا الثوب قميصاً اليوم بدرهم لم يجز عند الإمام. ولو قال ليخيط ولم يذكر الوقت يجوز، ولو قال ليخيطه قميصاً ويفرغ في اليوم جاز، ولو قال بشرط أن يفرغ أو على أن يفرغ في اليوم لم يجز .
As for the third, which is if he hired him to bake for him the entire day for a dirham, because mentioning the time makes the contracted thing the benefit (manfa'a), and mentioning the work makes the work the contracted object, and there is no preponderance of one over the other. If it is contracted for the benefit, he deserves wages with the passage of time whether he worked or not. If it is contracted for the work, he only deserves by work. So the contract becomes corrupt, and this is the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the contract is valid, and the contract is on the work (al-'ilm?) not on the day, such that if he finished half of the day he gets the wages, and if he did not work on that day, he must work the next day. Mentioning the day is for urgency, so it becomes like if he hired him to finish in this day, which is valid by consensus. The difference for the Imam here is that the day is not mentioned except to establish a description in the work, and the description is subsidiary to the described, not intended in itself. But in the book's issue, the day is mentioned intentionally. And in al-Ghiyathiyya: if he hired him to sew this cloth as a shirt today for a dirham, it is not valid according to Imam. And if he said 'to sew' without mentioning time, it is valid. And if he said 'to sew it as a shirt and finish in the day', it is valid. And if he said 'on condition that he finish' or 'on condition that he finish in the day', it is not valid.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage deals with the third case from the initial matn: hiring someone to bake for the entire day for a dirham. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract corrupt (fāsid) because the contract mentions both a timeframe (the day) and a specific work (baking). Since the contracted object is ambiguous (is it the benefit of the worker's time or the specific work of baking?), there is no basis to prefer one, leading to uncertainty. If it were for the benefit, wages are due at the end of the day regardless; if for the work, only upon completion. Because both are equally possible, the contract is fāsid. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the contract is valid, and it is for the work, not the day. So if he finishes baking halfway through the day, he gets the full wages; if he doesn't complete that day, he must finish the next day. The mention of 'day' is only for urgency, not as a condition for the work. They analogize it to hiring to finish by a certain day, which is valid by consensus. Imam's distinction: in this case, the day is mentioned as a description of the work (the work must happen within the day), which is subsidiary. In the matn's case (baking for a day for a dirham), the day is mentioned as an end in itself (the hire is for the day), creating ambiguity. The passage then cites al-Ghiyāthiyya with analogous cases: if hired to sew a shirt today for a dirham, it is invalid for Imam; if without time, valid; if with 'and finish in the day', valid; if with 'on condition to finish', invalid.

Key Terms
المعقود عليه (al-ma‘qūd ‘alayhi): The object of the contract: what is being exchanged (benefit or work).
المنفعة (al-manfa‘a): The benefit or utility derived from the worker's time or service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa in the baking case, why is the contract fasid?
A) Because the wage is unknown.
B) Because the timeframe is not specified.
C) Because both time and work are mentioned, causing uncertainty about the object.
D) Because baking is not a valid service.

Key Takeaway
In hire contracts, ambiguity between time and work can be resolved differently: Imam requires clarity, while the Sahibayn allow time as a subsidiary detail.

The Distinction Between Shepherd and Baker in Combining Time and Work
Resolving the apparent contradiction between two rulings on combining time and work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that combining time and work corrupts an ijarah contract only if the work is specified enough to be the sole object, and distinguish between valid and corrupt cases.

Core Idea
Combining time and work corrupts the contract only if the work is specified enough to be the sole object.

This lesson resolves a seeming contradiction in Hanafi ijarah rulings: why is a shepherd's hire valid when time and work are combined, but a baker's hire is invalid? The key lies in whether the work is defined in quantity or only described in type. Understanding this distinction helps avoid ambiguity in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The shepherd case (hiring for a month to pasture sheep) is ruled valid, while the baker case (baking for a day) is ruled corrupt, yet both combine time and work. This seems inconsistent if mere combination were the cause.
2
Understand the proposed rule from al-Muhit
An initial interpretation suggests the first-mentioned element (work or time) determines the object. This would lead to a logical inconsistency if applied uniformly.
This initial rule is rejected as a valid basis.
3
Learn the correct principle from al-Asl
The contract is corrupted only if each element (time and work) is mentioned in a way that could be the sole object of the contract. If the work is merely descriptive of type, corruption does not occur.
This is the authoritative Hanafi principle.
4
Apply the principle to the examples
In the shepherd case, the work (pasturing sheep) has no specified quantity, so it cannot be the sole object. In the baker case, baking for a day implies a defined amount, making it potential sole object, causing corruption.
5
Recognize the illa (effective cause)
The effective cause is the specification of the work's quantity. If the work is well-defined, combining it with time creates ambiguity (gharar) and invalidates the contract; otherwise, it is valid.
This is a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت: ورد في باب الراعي إذا جمع المدة والعمل يعتبر الأول. قال في المحيط : لو استأجره شهراً ليرعى غنمه بدرهم أوقع العقد على العمل لما قدم ذكر العمل على الوقت والعلة التي اقتضت فساد العقد في مسألة الجمع بين المدة والعمل فمقتضى النظر أن يفسد في الراعي كما في مسألة الكتاب، ويجوز في مسألة الكتاب كما جاز في مسألة الراعي ترجيحاً للمقدم في الذكر. وما الفارق بينهما؟ أقول : الفارق بينهما قال في الأصل والأصل عند الإمام أنه إذا جمع بين الوقت والعمل إنما يفسد العقد إذا ذكر كل واحد منهما على وجه لا يصلح أن يكون معقوداً عليه لأن ذكر الوقت والعمل على وجه لا يجوز إفراد العقد عليه لا يفسد العقد بيانه: إذا استأجر رجلاً يوماً ليبني له بالجص والآجر جاز بلا خلاف، وإن جمع بين الوقت والعمل فكان ذكر البناء لبيان نوع العمل وهذا العمل في هذه المسألة لا يجوز إفراد العقد عليه حتى لو ذكر العمل على وجه يجوز إفراد العقد عليه فإن بين قدر البناء لا يجوز ذلك عند الإمام اهـ. فعلى مسألة الخبز بين قدر المحل تفسد وفي مسألة الراعي لم يبين قدر الغنم المرعى فلا يفسد والحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وعن محمد إذا استأجره ليحمل له هذا اليوم ومعلوم بين
If you say: It is reported in the chapter of the shepherd that when time and work are combined, the first (mentioned) is considered. He said in al-Muhit: If he hired him for a month to pasture his sheep for a dirham, the contract is made on the work because the mention of work precedes the time. And the effective cause that necessitated the corruption of the contract in the issue of combining time and work would require that it be corrupt in the shepherd case as in the book's issue, and that it be valid in the book's issue as it is valid in the shepherd case, giving precedence to the first in mention. What is the distinction between them? I say: The distinction between them is as stated in al-Asl: The principle with the Imam is that when time and work are combined, the contract is only corrupted if each one is mentioned in a way that does not allow it to be the sole object of the contract. Because mentioning time and work in a way that does not allow the contract to be concluded on each individually does not corrupt the contract. Explanation: If he hired a man for a day to build with plaster and brick, it is valid without disagreement. Even though he combined time and work, mentioning building is to specify the type of work, and this work in this issue does not allow the contract to be concluded on it alone, so if he mentions work in a way that does allow the contract to be concluded on it, such as specifying the amount of building, then it is not valid according to the Imam, end. So in the baking issue, the amount of work is specified, so it is corrupted. In the shepherd issue, the number of sheep to be pastured is not specified, so it is not corrupted. Praise be to Allah who guided us to this. And from Muhammad: if he hired him to carry for him this day and it is known between...
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage addresses a question: why is the shepherd's case (hiring for a month to pasture sheep for a dirham) ruled valid, while the baker's case (baking for a day for a dirham) is ruled invalid by Imam Abu Hanifa, when both combine time and work? The answer from al-Muhīt: the effective cause for corruption is that each element is mentioned in a way that could be the sole object of the contract. In the shepherd case, 'to pasture his sheep' is a general work without specification of quantity, so it cannot be the sole object (since the work is undefined); thus the contract is valid, with the timeframe being the primary object. In the baker case, 'baking' is specified (the amount is implicit), so it could be the sole object, leading to ambiguity and corruption. This is based on a principle from Imam Muhammad's al-Asl: if the work is mentioned in a way that it could standalone as a contract (i.e., clearly defined), then combining it with a time corrupts the contract. If the work is only mentioned to specify the type (not quantity), the contract is valid. The passage ends with a narration from Muhammad about carrying for a day with known quantity, which appears cut off. The key distinction: specification (bayan) of the work's quantity causes corruption; absence of specification preserves validity.

Key Terms
بيان قدر العمل (bayān qadr al-‘amal): Specification of the quantity of work. If the work is defined in amount, it can be the sole object of contract; if not, it is merely descriptive.
المقدم في الذكر (al-muqaddam fī al-dhikr): The element mentioned first in the contract. In some cases, it may determine which object the contract is made upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle in al-Asl, when does combining time and work corrupt a hire contract?
A) Always, whenever both are mentioned.
B) When the work can be the sole object of the contract (i.e., well-defined).
C) When the time is mentioned first.
D) When the worker is not capable of doing the work.

Key Takeaway
Combining time and work only corrupts the ijarah contract if both are specified in a way that each could stand alone as the contract object.

Compensation in an Invalid Ijara with a Share and Yarn Condition
Ruling statement on compensation in an invalid weaver hiring contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a weaver hired on a share basis with a condition to add yarn, and identify the two compensations due.

Core Idea
In a fasid ijara with share and supplied yarn, the worker gets ujrat al-mithl and the yarn is guaranteed.

This lesson examines a specific case from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that illustrates the Hanafi approach to invalid hiring contracts. When a weaver is hired to weave a cloth in exchange for half of it (a share) on condition that he supplies an additional ratl of yarn, the contract is fasid due to uncertainty in the wage. However, the weaver is still entitled to fair compensation for his work and reimbursement for the yarn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract elements
Recognize that the contract combines a share-based wage (uncertain) with a condition to supply a known quantity of yarn.
2
Determine validity
The share creates gharar, rendering the contract fasid (invalid) according to Hanafi fiqh.
Gharar in the wage is a key invalidator.
3
Determine compensation for labor
Since the weaver performed work, he receives ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) for his work, not the agreed share.
This is the standard Hanafi rule for fasid contracts.
4
Determine compensation for supplied yarn
The yarn is a known commodity; the owner must guarantee it (return or pay its value) because it was supplied under the invalid condition.
The guarantee protects the weaver from loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : ولو استأجر حائكاً لينسج هذا الثوب بنصفه على أن يزيد رطلاً . من عند فنسج وزاد فله أجر مثل عمله ويضمن صاحب الثوب للحياك رطلاً من الغزل.
In al-Muhit: If he hired a weaver to weave this cloth for half of it, on condition that he add a ratl from his own [yarn], and he wove and added [the yarn], then he is entitled to the equivalent wage for his work, and the owner of the cloth guarantees to the weaver a ratl of yarn.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit presents a sub-case of the earlier ruling. If a weaver is hired to weave a specific cloth in exchange for half of it, but with an additional condition that he also supply an extra ratl of yarn from his own stock, the contract remains invalid due to the share-based compensation. However, if the weaver performs the work and adds the yarn, he is entitled to an 'ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) for his labor, and the cloth owner must compensate him for the yarn (the ratl) because the weaver supplied it as a condition. This ruling separates the compensation for the work (which is uncertain due to the share) from the guarantee of the specific yarn (which is a known commodity). The Hanafi approach here protects the weaver from loss while upholding the principle that invalid contracts still require fair compensation.

Key Terms
أجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for the work performed, independent of the contractually agreed compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Muhit, when a weaver is hired to weave a cloth for half of it and must add a ratl of his own yarn, after performing the work, what is he entitled to?
A) Half the cloth
B) Equivalent wage for his work and a ratl of yarn from the owner
C) Only his yarn back
D) Nothing because the contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
In an invalid ijara with uncertain wage and supplied materials, the worker receives fair wages and the materials are guaranteed.

Hiring for a Share of the Product: Ruling and Custom Exception
Ruling on share-based hire contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a person or animal for a share of the product and identify when custom (urf) may permit it.

Core Idea
Hiring for a share of the product is fāsid by default, but custom can override the ruling.

This passage presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school on a common transaction: paying a worker with a portion of the product itself. The default rule is that such compensation is uncertain (gharar), rendering the contract invalid (fāsid). However, the text also records that scholars of Balkh permitted it based on local custom, illustrating the Hanafi principle that established custom can influence rulings in mu'amalat (transactions).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Read the passage and identify the acts described: hiring a weaver, ox, donkey, or shop in exchange for a share of the product. Note that the ruling is fāsid (invalid) according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.
The term fāsid means defective but not void; it can be rectified.
2
Understand the reason
Why is it fāsid? Because the wage (the share) is uncertain at the time of contract – the exact amount of the product is unknown, so there is gharar (uncertainty).
Gharar in the wage makes the contract defective.
3
Note the exception
The text mentions that scholars of Balkh gave fatwa of permissibility based on custom (urf). This shows that custom can override the default ruling in some cases.
Custom must be established and not contrary to nass (explicit text).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ربح حائك ثوباً لينسجه بنصفه أو بثلثه أو ربعه فالإجارة فاسدة عند علمائنا وبه أفتى الإمام السرخسي والسيد الإمام الشهيد ومشايخ بلخ يفتون بالجواز لعرف بلادهم. وفي الظهيرية : أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث وشمس الأئمة الحلواني والقاضي أبو علي النسفي اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : لو استأجر ثوراً ليطحن له أردباً ببعض منه أو حماراً ليحمل له أردباً ببعض منه فالإجارة فاسدة ولو استأجر حانوتاً بنصف ما فيه فالإجارة فاسدة.
Profit: If a weaver takes a cloth to weave it for half, one-third, or one-quarter of it, the contract is invalid according to our scholars. Imam al-Sarakhsi and Sayyid Imam al-Shahid gave fatwa accordingly, and the scholars of Balkh give fatwa of permissibility due to the custom of their land. In al-Zahira: The faqih Abu al-Layth, Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani, and Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi adopted [this]. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: If he hired an ox to grind an ardebb of grain for a part of it, or a donkey to carry an ardebb for a part of it, the contract is invalid; and if he hired a shop for half of what is in it, the contract is invalid.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the invalidity of ijarah (hire) when the compensation is a share of the subject matter itself, such as a weaver being paid with a portion of the cloth he weaves. The text states that such a contract is fāsid (invalid) according to the established Hanafi position ('inda 'ulama'ina). However, it notes that some prominent scholars, like Imam al-Sarakhsi and Sayyid Imam al-Shahid, upheld this view, while the scholars of Balkh permitted it based on local custom ('urf). This illustrates an important principle in Hanafi fiqh: custom can affect the ruling on contractual validity, but only within the scope of permissibility. The passage then extends the same ruling to analogous cases: hiring an ox or donkey for grinding or carrying grain in exchange for a portion of the grain, and hiring a shop for a share of its contents. All are deemed invalid. The key reason is the presence of gharar (uncertainty) because the exact amount of compensation is unknown at the time of contract. The Hanafi school generally prohibits such transactions unless there is a valid custom that overrides the default ruling.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A hire contract that is legally defective due to a flaw in the consideration, such as paying with a share of the object.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom or prevalent practice that can influence legal rulings when not contrary to nass.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which scholars permitted hiring for a share of the product due to custom?
A) Imam al-Sarakhsi
B) Scholars of Balkh
C) Imam al-Shahid
D) Imam al-Halwani

Key Takeaway
Hiring for a share of the product is fāsid due to gharar, but custom can permit it in certain regions.

Hiring for Baking for a Day: Combining Time and Work
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining time and work in ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining time and work in ijarah, and distinguish when the contract is fasid versus valid based on the wording.

Core Idea
When both time and work are mentioned in a hire contract, ambiguity voids it only if each can stand alone as the object.

This passage delves into a nuanced issue in Hanafi ijarah: the validity of a contract that mentions both a specific period (like a full day) and a specific work (like baking). Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ on whether such a contract is valid or not. Understanding the underlying principle is crucial for determining the enforceability of many real-world service contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa on the contract of hiring for baking for a day. According to the text, he considers it fasid (invalid) because mentioning both time and work creates ambiguity about the object of contract.
This is the first position in the dispute.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's view
Now state the opposing view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the contract is valid (jā'iz) and the object is the work, with the day merely for expediting.
They analogize to hiring with a deadline, which is valid by consensus.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's evidence
Understand their reasoning: they draw an analogy to a hiring contract that specifies a deadline for completion, which is considered valid. The mention of the day is a condition for expediting, not a separate object.
The analogy is central to their argument.
4
Assess Abu Hanifa's response
According to the text, Abu Hanifa distinguishes the baking case from the deadline analogy. In the deadline case, time is subordinate to the work; in the baking case, time is mentioned independently, causing a conflict that invalidates the contract.
The distinction hinges on whether the time is intended as a quality or as an independent element.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the dispute: if the worker does not finish baking on that day, according to the Sahibayn he must work the next day without extra pay; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the contract is invalid and he receives ujrat al-mithl for work done.
This shows the real-world impact of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثالث وهو ما إذا استأجره ليخبز له طول النهار بدرهم فلأن ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المعقود هو المنفعة، وذكر العمل يوجب كون العمل هو المعقود عليه ولا ترجيح لأحدهما على الآخر، فإن وقع على المنفعة استحق الأجر بمضي الوقت عمل أو لم يعمل، وإن وقع على العمل لا يستحق إلا بالعمل فيفسد العقد وهو قول الإمام. وقالا : العقد جائز ويكون العقد على العلم دون اليوم حتى إذا فرغ منه نصف النهار فله الأجر، وإن لم يعمل في اليوم فعليه أن يعلم في الغد وذكر اليوم للتعجيل فصار كما إذا استأجره للعمل على أن يفرغ منه في هذا اليوم يجوز بالإجماع والفرق للإمام هنا أن اليوم لم يذكر هنا إلا لإثبات صفة في العمل والصفة تابعة للموصوف غير مقصودة بالذات، وفي مسألة الكتاب ذكر اليوم قصاداً. وفي الغياثية : لو استأجره ليخيط له هذا الثوب قميصاً اليوم بدرهم لم يجز عند الإمام. ولو قال ليخيط ولم يذكر الوقت يجوز، ولو قال ليخيطه قميصاً ويفرغ في اليوم جاز، ولو قال بشرط أن يفرغ أو على أن يفرغ في اليوم لم يجز . فإن قلت: ورد في باب الراعي إذا جمع المدة والعمل يعتبر الأول. قال في المحيط : لو استأجره شهراً ليرعى غنمه بدرهم أوقع العقد على العمل لما قدم ذكر العمل على الوقت والعلة التي اقتضت فساد العقد في مسألة الجمع بين المدة والعمل فمقتضى النظر أن يفسد في الراعي كما في مسألة الكتاب، ويجوز في مسألة الكتاب كما جاز في مسألة الراعي ترجيحاً للمقدم في الذكر. وما الفارق بينهما؟ أقول : الفارق بينهما قال في الأصل والأصل عند الإمام أنه إذا جمع بين الوقت والعمل إنما يفسد العقد إذا ذكر كل واحد منهما على وجه لا يصلح أن يكون معقوداً عليه لأن ذكر الوقت والعمل على وجه لا يجوز إفراد العقد عليه لا يفسد العقد بيانه: إذا استأجر رجلاً يوماً ليبني له بالجص والآجر جاز بلا خلاف، وإن جمع بين الوقت والعمل فكان ذكر البناء لبيان نوع العمل وهذا العمل في هذه المسألة لا يجوز إفراد العقد عليه حتى لو ذكر العمل على وجه يجوز إفراد العقد عليه فإن بين قدر البناء لا يجوز ذلك عند الإمام اهـ. فعلى مسألة الخبز بين قدر المحل تفسد وفي مسألة الراعي لم يبين قدر الغنم المرعى فلا يفسد والحمد لله الذي هدانا لهذا وعن محمد إذا استأجره ليحمل له هذا اليوم ومعلوم بين أنه لا يمكن حمله اليوم فهو على المحل دون الوقت اهـ .
As for the third [case], which is when he hires him to bake for him the entire day for a dirham: because mentioning the time necessitates that the object of contract is the benefit (manfa'ah), and mentioning the work necessitates that the work is the object of contract; and there is no preponderance of one over the other. If it occurs on the benefit, he deserves the wage with the passage of time whether he worked or not; if it occurs on the work, he does not deserve [wage] except by working. Thus the contract is invalid, and this is the statement of Imam [Abu Hanifa]. The two [companions] said: The contract is valid, and the contract is on the work (al-'amal) not the day, so that if he finishes half the day, he gets the wage; if he did not work on that day, he must work the next day. The mention of the day is for expediting; thus it becomes like if he hired him for work on condition that he finish it on that day – that is valid by consensus. The distinction for Imam here is that the day is mentioned only to establish a quality in the work, and the quality is subordinate to the described, not intended by itself; while in the case of the book (i.e., the earlier case?), the day is mentioned intentionally. In al-Ghiyathiyya: If he hired him to sew this cloth into a shirt today for a dirham, it is not permissible according to Imam [Abu Hanifa]. If he said 'to sew' without mentioning time, it is permissible. If he said 'to sew it as a shirt and finish today', it is permissible. If he said 'on condition that he finishes' or 'that he finishes today', it is not permissible. If you say: It is narrated in the chapter of the shepherd that when he combines the period and the work, the first [mentioned] is considered. [The text] says in al-Muhit: If he hired him for a month to pasture his sheep for a dirham, the contract is placed on the work because the mention of work precedes the time. The cause that necessitated the invalidity of the contract in the case of combining period and work – logically, it should be invalid in the shepherd case as in the book's case, and permissible in the book's case as in the shepherd case, giving preponderance to what is mentioned first. What is the difference between them? I say: The difference between them is stated in al-Asl: The principle according to Imam is that when he combines time and work, the contract is invalid only if each one is mentioned in a way that it would not be suitable as an object of the contract alone. Because mentioning time and work in a way that the contract could not be made solely on it does not invalidate the contract. Explanation: If he hired a man for a day to build for him with plaster and brick, it is permissible without dispute. Even though he combined time and work, the mention of building is to specify the type of work, and this work in this case is not permissible to make the contract solely on it [i.e., building without time specification is too vague? Actually, building is not a specific work?]. But if he mentioned the work in a way that a contract could be made solely on it, such as specifying the amount of building, then it is not permissible according to Imam. So in the baking case, he specified the place? Actually, 'bain qadr al-mahall'? The text says 'fa-'ala mas'alat al-khubz bain qadr al-mahall tafsadu', meaning the baking case specifies the quantity of the place? Or 'bain qadr al-'amal'? In any case, the baking case specifies the work, so it invalidates. The shepherd case did not specify the number of sheep, so it does not invalidate. And from Muhammad: If he hired him to carry for him today, and it is known that he cannot carry it today, then the contract is on the work not the time.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage addresses a critical issue in Hanafi ijarah: the validity of a contract that mentions both a specific period (like a full day) and a specific work (like baking). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such a contract is fāsid (invalid) because the mention of time and work conflict as to the object of contract: time implies the benefit (manfa'ah) of the worker, while work implies the labor itself. Since there is no simultaneous way to assign both as the primary object, the contract becomes defective. He analogizes it to a hire for sewing with a deadline, which his companions accept as valid by consensus. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the contract is valid and the primary object is the work (al-'amal), and the day is merely for expediting (ta'jil). This leads to practical differences: if the worker does not finish on time, he must work the next day. The text then compares this with the case of a shepherd hired for a month to pasture sheep. In that case, the work is mentioned first, so the contract is on the work, following the principle that precedence in mention determines the object. The discussion clarifies that the invalidity occurs only when both time and work are mentioned in a way that each could stand alone as the object of contract. If one is merely descriptive (e.g., building to specify type), the contract remains valid. The baking case is problematic because the work is specified in a manner that could be contracted alone, whereas the shepherd case is not specified. This illustrates the subtlety of Hanafi jurisprudence in analyzing contractual intent.

Key Terms
معقود عليه (ma'qūd 'alayh): The object of the contract; what the contract is primarily about (the service or benefit).
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A hire contract that is legally defective due to ambiguity in the object or consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is hiring someone to bake for the entire day for a dirham invalid?
A) Because the wage is unspecified
B) Because both time and work are mentioned in a way that each could be the object of contract
C) Because baking is not a valid work
D) Because the day is too long

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, combining time and work in a hire contract leads to dispute: Abu Hanifa invalidates if both can stand alone as object, while Sahibayn validate with work as primary.

Land Lease with Inherent Conditions (Plowing and Farming) is Valid
States that renting land with conditions like plowing and farming is valid because they are inherent to the contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that conditions inherent to the purpose of a land lease are valid and explain the legal principle 'shart yaqtaḍīhi al-aqd'.

Core Idea
Conditions required by the contract itself do not invalidate a lease.

This lesson examines a key principle from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when renting land for farming, it is valid to include conditions like plowing and irrigating because these are inherent to the contract. Understanding this distinction helps avoid invalidating contracts with extraneous conditions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The author rules that renting land with conditions of plowing and farming is valid.
2
Identify the condition
The conditions mentioned are plowing and irrigating — both essential for farming.
3
Apply the legal principle
These conditions are 'shart yaqtaḍīhi al-'aqd' — required by the contract itself, so they are valid.
Hanafi law permits conditions that are harmonious with the contract's purpose.
4
Distinguish from invalid conditions
Conditions that give an extra benefit to one party unrelated to the use of the land would invalidate the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجر أرضاً على أن يكر بها ويزرعها أو يسقيها ويزرعها صح لأنه شرط يقتضيه العقد وهو ملائم له فلا يفسد العقد.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (If he rents a land on condition that he plows it and farms it, or irrigates it and farms it, it is valid because it is a condition required by the contract and it is harmonious with it, so it does not invalidate the contract.)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a clear ruling: when a person rents agricultural land, conditions that are essential for farming—such as plowing (karab), irrigating (saqi), and sowing—do not render the contract invalid. The reason is that these conditions are 'muqtada al-'aqd' (required by the contract) or 'mulā'im' (harmonious) with the purpose of the lease. In Hanafi law, a condition that is naturally implied in the contract (like tilling the land to farm it) is considered part of the essence of the deal and does not introduce gharar or extra benefit to the lessor that would invalidate it. This ruling applies to any condition that is necessary for the utilization of the subject matter in the customary manner.

Key Terms
شرط يقتضيه العقد (sharṭ yaqtaḍīhi al-'aqd): A condition that the contract inherently requires for its proper execution; such conditions are valid and do not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is renting land with a condition to plow and farm it considered valid?
A) Because the condition is explicitly allowed by the Quran
B) Because plowing and farming are inherent to the purpose of the lease
C) Because the landlord's permission is assumed
D) Because it increases the value of the land

Key Takeaway
Renting land with conditions essential for farming (like plowing and irrigating) is valid because such conditions are required by the contract itself.

Invalid Conditions in Land Lease: Lasting Benefit to Lessor
Details invalid conditions in land lease with rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which conditions in a land lease invalidate the contract and explain the underlying 'illa (effective cause) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A condition that leaves lasting benefit for the lessor beyond the lease term invalidates the contract as a hidden extra payment.

In land lease contracts, the lessor may impose conditions on the lessee, such as plowing the land a second time, digging canals, or fertilizing. However, not all conditions are valid. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between conditions that are necessary for the lease to fulfill its purpose and those that provide an unfair advantage to the lessor. This lesson explores the key invalidating conditions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the stipulation
What exactly is the lessor requiring the lessee to do? For example, tathniyah (plowing twice), digging canals, or manuring.
2
Assess the permanence of the benefit
Does the effect of this act remain after the lease ends? If the benefit (e.g., improved soil, irrigation canal) lasts beyond the term, it is likely a problematic condition.
3
Evaluate necessity
Is this condition essential for the land to be farmed as intended? If the land cannot yield without it, the condition is considered harmonious and may be valid.
Necessity is determined by custom and the specific land.
4
Apply the ruling
If the condition provides lasting benefit and is not necessary, the contract is fasid (invalid). If necessary or temporary, the condition is valid.
5
Note any ikhtilaf
There are intra-Hanafi differences on specific conditions, such as digging small channels vs. large canals. Recognize which view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
Al-Kafi holds that stipulating to dig small channels does not invalidate, unlike large canals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن شرط أن يثنيها أو يكري أنهارها أو يسرقنها أو يزرعها بزراعة أرض أخرى لا يعين لا يجوز لأن أثر التثنية وكري الأنهار والسرقنة يبقى بعد مضي عقد الإجارة فيكون عقد فيه نفع لصاحب الأرض وهو شرط لا يقتضيه العقد فيفسد، ولأن مستأجراً منافع الأجر بعد مضي المدة فتصير صفقة في صفقة فلا يجوز حتى لو كانت بحيث لا تبقى بأن كانت المدة طويلة لو كان البيع لا يحصل إلا به لا يفسد اشتراطه لأنه مما يقتضيه العقد. واختلفوا في التثنية قال بعضهم هو أن يردها مكروبة، وقال أن يكربها مرتين. وذكر شيخ الإسلام: إذا اشترط على المستأجر أن يردها مكروبة بعضهم هو بعد الإجارة فالمسألة على وجهين : إن قال صاحب الأرض أجرتك بكذا بأن تردها مكروبة العقد فالعقد جائز، وأما إذا قال أجرتك على أن تكر بها بعد العقد بعد مضي هذا الوجه ففي العقد فاسد. وإن أطلق الكراب ينصرف إلى ما بعد العقد العقد، وأما إذا شرط أن ويصح يكري أنهارها يفسد العقد، ومن المشايخ من فرق بين الجداول والأنهار فقال : اشتراط كري الجداول صحيح. قال في الكافي الصحيح لا يفسد بهذا العقد بخلاف اشتراط كري الأنهار . وأما إذا شرط عليه أن يسرقنها فلا يخلو إما أن يكون السرقين من عند المستأجر فقد شرط عليه عيناً هو مال فإن كان تبقى منفعته إلى العام الثاني لا يفسد؛ كذا في الأصل. ومقتضى النظر أن يفصل فيها بأن يقال: إن كان الأرض لا يظهر ريعها إلا بالسرقين فهو شرط ملائم للعقد فلا يفسد وإن كان يظهر ريعها من غير سرقنة فهو شرط فيه منفعة لأحد المتعاقدين فيفسد، وأما استئجار الأرض بأرض أخرى ليزرعها الآخر يكون بيع الشيء بجنسه نسيئة وهو حرام كما عرف في موضعه
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he stipulates that he will tathniyah (plow a second time) it, or dig its canals, or manure it, or farm it with the cultivation of another land without specification, it is not permissible. Because the effect of tathniyah, digging canals, and manuring remains after the expiry of the hire contract, so it becomes a contract with benefit for the owner of the land, which is a condition not required by the contract, thus it invalidates. Also, because the hirer [benefits from] the use of the land beyond the period? Actually text: 'wa li-anna musta'jiran manafi' al-ajr ba'da madi al-mudda fatasiru safqatan fi safqatin fala yajuz' – because the hirer takes the benefits of the wage after the expiry? The reasoning: it becomes a double transaction. Until if it were such that it does not remain (i.e., the effect disappears) and the period is long, and the lease would not occur except with it, then its stipulation does not invalidate because it is required by the contract. They differed on tathniyah. Some said it is to return it plowed; some said to plow it twice. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned: If he stipulated on the lessee that he return it plowed – some say after the ijarah – so the case has two aspects: If the landowner said 'I lease it to you for such [amount] on condition that you return it plowed' – the contract is valid. But if he said 'I lease it to you on condition that you plow it after the contract after the expiry of this [period]' – then the contract is invalid. If the plowing is absolute, it refers to after the contract. As for if he stipulated that he dig its canals, it invalidates the contract. Some scholars distinguished between small channels (jadawil) and large canals (anhar), saying stipulating digging small channels is valid. Al-Kafi says: The correct view is that it does not invalidate the contract, unlike stipulating digging large canals. As for if he stipulated that he manure it, it is not free from either that the manure is from the lessee – then he has stipulated a specific item that is wealth; if its benefit remains until the second year, it does not invalidate; thus in al-Asl. Logical consideration requires differentiation: if the land does not produce yield except with manure, then it is a condition harmonious with the contract, so it does not invalidate; if it produces yield without manure, then it is a condition with benefit for one of the contracting parties, so it invalidates. As for renting land for another land to farm it, that is selling a thing for its like on credit, which is prohibited as known in its place.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This detailed passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains invalid conditions in a land lease. The core principle: any condition that leaves a lasting benefit for the lessor beyond the lease term is invalid because it effectively adds an extra compensation beyond the rent. Examples include tathniyah (returning the land plowed twice), digging irrigation canals that remain, and manuring the land with lasting effect. However, the text provides nuance: if the condition is necessary for the lease itself (e.g., land cannot be farmed without manure), then it is considered 'harmonious' and does not invalidate. Also, if the improvement is temporary (e.g., plowing that doesn't last long) or the lease period is very long, it may be acceptable. The passage also records scholarly differences: some allow digging small channels but not large canals; some allow manuring if the manure's benefit does not persist beyond one season. This reflects the Hanafi method of analyzing the underlying cause ('illa) to determine validity. The last part mentions that leasing land for another land (like rent paid in land use) is prohibited as it resembles riba (selling a homogeneous good on credit).

Key Terms
تثنية (tathniyah): Plowing the land a second time, often to prepare it for the next season.
سرقنة (sarqinah): Manuring the land with fertilizer.
جداول (jadawil): Small irrigation channels or ditches.
أنهار (anhar): Large canals or rivers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does stipulating that the lessee must dig the land's canals invalidate the lease?
A) Because digging canals is not related to farming
B) Because the canals remain after the lease, benefiting the lessor
C) Because it is too expensive for the lessee
D) Because the lessor should dig them himself

Key Takeaway
In land leases, conditions that leave lasting benefit for the lessor beyond the term invalidate the contract unless they are necessary for the lease to function.

Prohibition of Renting a House for Another House (Sukna bi-Sukna)
Ruling that exchanging dwelling for dwelling is invalid due to analogy to credit sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging dwelling for dwelling (sukna bi-sukna) and explain the qiyas that makes it analogous to bai' al-dayn bi al-dayn.

Core Idea
Exchanging the use of one house for another is prohibited as a credit-for-credit sale.

This lesson examines a specific contract of ijarah where the rent is not cash or kind but the right to dwell in another house. The Hanafi school rules this invalid because both benefits are non-existent at the time of contract and arise gradually, making it akin to the prohibited sale of debt for debt. We will explore the textual basis, the qiyas reasoning, and a scholarly critique that strengthens the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling from the matn
Identify that the matn says 'la yajuz' (not permissible) for ijarah of dwelling for dwelling. This is the explicit ruling.
The matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Understand the analogy to bai' al-dayn bi al-dayn
Imam Muhammad likens the transaction to selling debt for debt. Both involve deferred obligations of the same genus (usufruct of dwelling). Recognize that this analogy is the core proof.
The prohibition of bai' al-dayn bi al-dayn is established by hadith and ijma.
3
Analyze the critique from al-'Inayah
Two objections are raised: (1) nasi'ah requires an explicit deferred term, not present here; (2) nasi'ah involves present vs. deferred, but here both are deferred. Understand these points.
The critique is about the precision of the qiyas.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the critique
The response is that the gradual nature of benefits makes the deferment inherent, making it even more severe than ordinary nasi'ah. Thus the qiyas is sound.
This shows how Hanafi scholars defend their istidlal.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The ruling is that such a contract is invalid (fasid) and prohibited (haram). This is the mufta bihi position based on Imam Muhammad's statement.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (لا) كإجارة السكني بالسكني) يعني لا يجوز إجارة السكني بالسكنى لأن الجنس بانفراده يحرم النسأ وإليه أشار محمد حين كتب له سماعة لم لا يجوز إجارة سكنى دار بسكنى دار أخرى بقوله في جوابه: أطلت الفكرة وأصابتك الحيرة وجالست الحيارى أي فكان منك ذلة وما علمت أن إجارة السكني بالسكنى بالدين كبيع الدين بالدين بنسيئة. قال صاحب العناية : في هذا الاستدلال بحث من وجهين: الأول أن النسأ ما يكون عن اشتراط أجل في العقد وتأخير المنفعة فيما نحن فيه ليس كذلك. والثاني أن النسأ إنما يتصور في مبادلة موجود في الحال بما ليس كذلك. وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك فإن كل واحد منهما ليس بموجود وإنما يحدثان شيئاً فشيئاً. وأجيب الأول بأنه لما أقدما على عقد يتأخر المعقود عليه فيه ويحدث شيئاً فشيئاً كان ذلك أبلغ في عن
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (No, like ijarah of dwelling for dwelling) meaning: ijarah of dwelling for dwelling is not permissible because the genus alone prohibits nasi'ah (credit). Imam Muhammad alluded to this when Sami'ah wrote to him asking why ijarah of dwelling of a house for dwelling of another house is not permissible. He replied: You have prolonged thought, and error has befallen you, and you sat with the confused – thus from you came weakness, and you did not know that ijarah of dwelling for dwelling on credit is like selling debt for debt on credit. The author of al-'Inayah said: In this deduction there is discussion from two aspects: First, that nasi'ah is by stipulating a term in the contract, and delaying the benefit in our case is not like that. Second, that nasi'ah is only conceivably in the exchange of something present for something not present, and our case is not like that because each of them is not present; rather, they come into being gradually. And it was answered to the first: because they entered into a contract where the object is deferred and comes into being gradually, that is more severe in [the prohibition]?
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of exchanging the right to live in one house for the right to live in another (sukna bi-sukna). The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states it is not permissible. The commentary explains that this is analogous to selling debt for debt (bai' al-dayn bi al-dayn), which is prohibited in Islamic law. The reasoning: both benefits (manafi') are non-existent at the time of contract; they arise gradually. Thus, it is a credit transaction that involves jins (same genus) – both are usufruct of dwelling – and the delay makes it like riba al-nasi'ah. Imam Muhammad's response to Sami'ah's query emphasizes the severity of this transaction. The text then presents a critique from the author of al-'Inayah: first, that nasi'ah usually requires a deferred payment term, which is not explicit here; second, that nasi'ah typically involves exchanging a present for a deferred thing, but here both are deferred. However, the response is that the deferred nature of both usufructs makes it even more akin to prohibited credit sales. This shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning in analogizing new contracts to established prohibitions.

Key Terms
إجارة السكنى (ijārat al-suknā): A lease contract for the right to dwell in a property.
بيع الدين بالدين (bai' al-dayn bi al-dayn): Selling a debt (deferred obligation) for another debt, which is prohibited under Islamic law.
نسيئة (nasi'ah): A credit sale where payment is deferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is renting a house in exchange for living in another house (sukna bi-sukna) invalid according to Hanafis?
A) Because the houses might be of different value
B) Because it is like selling debt for debt, which is prohibited
C) Because the rent is unspecified
D) Because the owner must give permission

Key Takeaway
Exchanging the usufruct of a house for the usufruct of another house is invalid in Hanafi fiqh because it is a credit-for-credit transaction of the same genus.

Conditions in Agricultural Land Lease
Commentary on valid and invalid conditions in land lease contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditions in agricultural land leases and apply the principle of muqtada al-'aqd to determine validity.

Core Idea
A condition that gives lasting benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term invalidates unless essential for the land's purpose.

Leases of agricultural land often include conditions about cultivation practices. The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between conditions that are inherent to the contract and those that provide extra benefit. This lesson examines how scholars evaluate such conditions, with detailed rulings on manuring, digging canals, and fertilizing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Determine what exactly is being stipulated (e.g., ploughing, fertilizing, digging). Classify it as an act that may leave a lasting effect.
2
Check if condition is muqtada al-'aqd
Ask whether the condition is inherently necessary for the lease's purpose (cultivation). If yes, it is valid; if no, proceed to next step.
Examples: planting seeds is necessary; installing a permanent irrigation system is not necessarily required.
3
Evaluate benefit duration
If the condition provides a benefit that lasts beyond the lease term (e.g., fertilizer that improves soil for years), it is suspect.
Long lease terms may reduce the issue because the benefit is consumed during the term.
4
Assess necessity for the land
If the land cannot produce a crop without the condition (e.g., requires manuring), then the condition is harmonious and does not invalidate.
This is a key exception to the general rule.
5
Determine ruling
Combine the above: condition that is not muqtada but provides lasting unnecessary benefit → invalidates lease. Otherwise, valid.
Also note intra-Hanafi differences on details like timing of ploughing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استأجر أرضاً على أن يكر بها ويزرعها أو يسقيها ويزرعها صح لأنه شرط يقتضيه العقد وهو ملائم له فلا يفسد العقد. وقال رحمه الله: (وإن شرط أن يثنيها أو يكري أنهارها أو يسرقنها أو يزرعها بزراعة أرض أخرى لا يعين لا يجوز لأن أثر التثنية وكري الأنهار والسرقنة يبقى بعد مضي عقد الإجارة فيكون عقد فيه نفع لصاحب الأرض وهو شرط لا يقتضيه العقد فيفسد، ولأن مستأجراً منافع الأجر بعد مضي المدة فتصير صفقة في صفقة فلا يجوز حتى لو كانت بحيث لا تبقى بأن كانت المدة طويلة لو كان البيع لا يحصل إلا به لا يفسد اشتراطه لأنه مما يقتضيه العقد. واختلفوا في التثنية قال بعضهم هو أن يردها مكروبة، وقال أن يكربها مرتين. وذكر شيخ الإسلام: إذا اشترط على المستأجر أن يردها مكروبة بعضهم هو بعد الإجارة فالمسألة على وجهين : إن قال صاحب الأرض أجرتك بكذا بأن تردها مكروبة العقد فالعقد جائز، وأما إذا قال أجرتك على أن تكر بها بعد العقد بعد مضي هذا الوجه ففي العقد فاسد. وإن أطلق الكراب ينصرف إلى ما بعد العقد [؟] العقد، وأما إذا شرط أن ويصح يكري أنهارها يفسد العقد، ومن المشايخ من فرق بين الجداول والأنهار فقال : اشتراط كري الجداول صحيح. قال في الكافي الصحيح لا يفسد بهذا العقد بخلاف اشتراط كري الأنهار . وأما إذا شرط عليه أن يسرقنها فلا يخلو إما أن يكون السرقين من عند المستأجر فقد شرط عليه عيناً هو مال فإن كان تبقى منفعته إلى العام الثاني لا يفسد؛ كذا في الأصل. ومقتضى النظر أن يفصل فيها بأن يقال: إن كان الأرض لا يظهر ريعها إلا بالسرقين فهو شرط ملائم للعقد فلا يفسد وإن كان يظهر ريعها من غير سرقنة فهو شرط فيه منفعة لأحد المتعاقدين فيفسد، وأما استئجار الأرض بأرض أخرى ليزرعها الآخر يكون بيع الشيء بجنسه نسيئة وهو حرام كما عرف في موضعه.
If one leases land on condition that he ploughs it and plants it or irrigates it and plants it, it is valid because it is a condition necessitated by the contract and is in harmony with it, so it does not spoil the contract. And he (the author) said: If he stipulates that he will manure it, or dig its canals, or fertilize it, or plant it with the cultivation of another land without specification, it is not permissible because the effect of manuring, digging canals, and fertilizing remains after the lease term ends, so it is a contract that contains benefit for the landowner and is a condition not necessitated by the contract, so it spoils it; and because the lessee [takes] the benefits after the term, so it becomes a sale in a sale and is not permissible unless the effect does not remain, such as when the term is long, and if the sale is not achieved except through it, the stipulation does not spoil it because it is necessitated by the contract. They differed on tathniya: some said it is to return it ploughed, some said to plough it twice. Shaykh al-Islam mentioned: If it is stipulated on the lessee to return it ploughed, some say it is after the lease, so the case has two faces: if the landowner says 'I lease to you for such amount on condition that you return it ploughed' the contract is valid, but if he says 'I lease to you on condition that you plough it after the lease' then the contract is invalid. If the ploughing is left absolute, it refers to after the lease. And if he stipulates that he will dig its canals, the contract is invalid. Some mashayikh differentiated between small channels and large rivers, saying stipulation for digging small channels is valid. In al-Kafi: the correct is that it does not spoil the contract, unlike stipulation for digging large rivers. And if he stipulates that he will fertilize it, it depends: if the manure is from the lessee, he has stipulated a tangible asset; if its benefit lasts to the second year, it does not spoil the contract, as in al-Asl. The necessary consideration is to differentiate: if the land does not produce yield except with manure, it is a condition in harmony with the contract and does not spoil; if it produces yield without manure, it is a condition with benefit to one party and spoils. And leasing land for another land to cultivate is selling a thing for its like on credit, which is haram as known in its place.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses conditions in lease contracts for agricultural land. The author first presents a valid condition: stipulating that the lessee will plough, irrigate, and plant the land. This is valid because such acts are inherent to the purpose of the lease—cultivation—so the condition is in harmony with the contract. Then he discusses invalid conditions: stipulating manuring (tathniya), digging canals, or fertilizing (sarqin) because these provide lasting benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term, making it a 'sale within a sale' (صفقة في صفقة). However, if the lease is long enough that the benefit does not remain, or if the condition is necessary for the land's function, it may be valid. The commentator details differences on tathniya: whether it refers to returning the land ploughed once or twice, and whether the stipulation is at the time of contract or after. He notes that some scholars distinguish between small canals (jadal) and large rivers (anhar), ruling the former valid. For fertilizing, the key is whether the land needs it; if it does, the condition is harmonious and valid. Leasing land in exchange for another piece of land to cultivate is analogized to selling wheat for wheat on credit, which is forbidden. The passage thus teaches the Hanafi principle that conditions in leases are evaluated by their compatibility with the contract's purpose.

Key Terms
تثنية (tathniya): Manuring the land by turning over the soil (ploughing) to prepare it for cultivation.
كري الأنهار (kari al-anhar): Digging out or cleaning canals and rivers to remove silt and maintain water flow.
سرقين (sarqin): Manure or fertilizer applied to land to improve fertility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lessee is required to fertilize the land with manure that lasts more than one season, what is the ruling on the lease?
A) The lease is valid because it is a condition necessitated by the contract.
B) The lease is invalid because the condition provides extra benefit to the lessor beyond the term.
C) The lease is invalid only if the manure is provided by the lessor.
D) The lease is valid only if the manure is from the lessee.

Key Takeaway
A condition that provides lasting benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term invalidates the agricultural land lease unless it is necessary for the land's cultivation.
