Prohibition of Leasing a House for a House
Explanation of the prohibition of leasing residence for residence due to being a sale of debt for debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits leasing a house for another house and identify the practical consequence (rental equivalent) when the invalid contract is executed.

Core Idea
Leasing a house for a house is prohibited because it is a delayed exchange of like benefits, akin to riba.

The Hanafi school prohibits the lease of a residence in exchange for the use of another residence. This ruling is based on the principle that exchanging two similar benefits with a delay in delivery constitutes riba al-nasi'ah. In this lesson, we will examine the reasoning behind this prohibition, including the objections raised by scholars and the Hanafi responses, as well as the practical ruling if such an invalid contract is performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited transaction
The transaction is 'ijarat al-sukna bi al-sukna' — leasing a house for another house. Note that both countervalues are benefits of the same type (housing use) and are not delivered immediately in full.
This contract is invalid in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the reason: nasi'ah (delayed exchange)
The prohibition is because the exchange involves a delay (nasi'ah) of similar items, which is analogous to riba. Imam Muhammad compares it to selling debt for debt on credit.
The delay is inherent since the benefits materialize gradually.
3
Analyze the objections and Hanafi responses
Objection from al-Inaya: nasi'ah requires a stipulated term and immediate exchange of one item, which is not present. Responses: (1) Gradual occurrence implies even stronger delay, so it is analogized by precaution. (2) Despite gradual delivery, one benefit is deemed present legally.
The commentator prefers a simpler argument: hire was allowed against analogy due to need, but there is no need for this type of exchange.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement on rental equivalent
If one party actually uses the benefit, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) holds that a rental equivalent (ajr al-mithl) is due. Imam Abu Yusuf narrated no compensation is owed.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that rental equivalent must be paid.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i permits this contract, viewing benefits as exchangeable commodities. The Hanafi school responds that hire was permitted against qiyas only out of necessity, which does not extend to exchanging identical benefits.
The practical difference: Shafi'i rule the contract valid; Hanafi rule it invalid with rental equivalent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (لا) كإجارة السكني بالسكني) يعني لا يجوز إجارة السكني بالسكنى لأن الجنس بانفراده يحرم النسأ وإليه أشار محمد حين كتب له سماعة لم لا يجوز إجارة سكنى دار بسكنى دار أخرى بقوله في جوابه: أطلت الفكرة وأصابتك الحيرة وجالست الحيارى أي فكان منك ذلة وما علمت أن إجارة السكني بالسكنى بالدين كبيع الدين بالدين بنسيئة. قال صاحب العناية : في هذا الاستدلال بحث من وجهين: الأول أن النسأ ما يكون عن اشتراط أجل في العقد وتأخير المنفعة فيما نحن فيه ليس كذلك. والثاني أن النسأ إنما يتصور في مبادلة موجود في الحال بما ليس كذلك. وما نحن فيه ليس كذلك فإن كل واحد منهما ليس بموجود وإنما يحدثان شيئاً فشيئاً. وأجيب الأول بأنه لما أقدما على عقد يتأخر المعقود عليه فيه ويحدث شيئاً فشيئاً كان ذلك أبلغ في وجوب التأخير من المشروط فألحق به دلالة احتياطاً عن شبهة الحرمة. وعن الثاني بأن الذي لم تصحبه الباء تقام فيه العين مقام المنفعة ضرورة تحقق المعقود عليه دون ما تصحبه لفقدانها فيه ولزم وجود أحدهما حكماً وعدم الآخر فيتحقق النسأ. وفي الشارح: والأولى أن يقال: إن الإجارة أجيزت على خلاف القياس للحاجة ولا حاجة إلى استئجار المنفعة بمنفعة من جنسها، ولو استوفى أحدهما المنفعة في المسألة فعليه أجر المثل في ظاهر الرواية. وذكر الكرخي عن يوسف : لا شيء عليه . وجه ظاهر الرواية أنه استوفى المنفعة بعقد فاسد فيجب أجر المثل، وعند الشافعي يجوز هذا العقد .اهـ.
He (the author) said: (No) like leasing a residence for a residence, meaning it is not permissible to lease a residence for a residence because the genus alone prohibits nasi'ah (delayed exchange). Imam Muhammad indicated this when he wrote to Sami'a why it is not permissible to lease one house for another house, saying in answer: 'You thought too long, perplexity befell you, and you sat with the perplexed' meaning a lowliness befell you, and you did not know that leasing a residence for a residence on credit is like selling debt for debt on credit. The author of al-'Inaya said: In this reasoning there is discussion from two aspects: First, nasi'ah is from stipulating a term in the contract and delaying the benefit, but in our case it is not so. Second, nasi'ah is only conceivable in exchanging something present in exchange for something not present, and our case is not so, for each one is not present but rather they come into being gradually. The response to the first is that since they entered into a contract in which the subject matter is delayed and comes into being gradually, that is more severe in establishing delay than the stipulated, so it is analogized to it by indication as a precaution against the semblance of prohibition. The response to the second is that in what is not accompanied by ba', the commodity is substituted for benefit by necessity to realize the subject matter, unlike what is accompanied by ba' due to its absence, and the existence of one is deemed and the other not, so nasi'ah is realized. In al-Sharh: It is better to say that hire was permitted contrary to analogy due to need, and there is no need to hire a benefit for a benefit of its type. If one of them avails the benefit in the issue, he must pay the rental equivalent in the apparent narration. Al-Karakhi narrated from Yusuf that there is nothing upon him. The argument for the apparent narration is that he availed the benefit through an invalid contract, so he must pay the rental equivalent. According to al-Shafi'i, this contract is permissible.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage discusses the prohibition of leasing a house for another house (إجارة السكنى بالسكنى). The author quotes the matn: 'No, like leasing a residence for a residence,' meaning it is invalid. The reason given is that this transaction involves a delayed exchange (nasi'ah) of benefits of the same type, which is akin to riba. Imam Muhammad is reported to have responded to a question with a strong rebuke, comparing it to selling debt for debt on credit. Then a potential objection is raised: nasi'ah typically involves a stipulated delay, but here the benefits are not fully present at the outset. Two responses are given: (1) the gradual occurrence of benefits actually implies an even greater delay, so it is treated as nasi'ah by precaution; (2) the analogy is valid because one benefit is deemed present while the other is absent. The commentator prefers a simpler argument: hire was permitted against qiyas due to need, but there is no need to exchange one benefit for another of the same type, so the original prohibition applies. If one party actually uses the benefit, the Hanafi rule in the apparent narration is that he must pay the rental equivalent, though there is a contrary narration from Abu Yusuf. Imam al-Shafi'i considers such a lease valid. The passage illustrates the Hanafi principle of strictness in avoiding riba and the use of احتياط (precaution) in matters of prohibited transactions.

Key Terms
نسأ (nasi'ah): A delayed exchange or credit transaction, particularly where the payment is postponed.
إجارة السكنى بالسكنى (ijarat al-sukna bi al-sukna): Leasing a residential property in exchange for the right to reside in another property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prohibit leasing a house for another house?
A) Because the houses are not of equal value.
B) Because it involves delayed exchange of similar benefits, akin to riba.
C) Because lease contracts must be for money only.
D) Because houses cannot be made the object of a lease.

Key Takeaway
Leasing a house for another house is prohibited in the Hanafi school because it constitutes riba al-nasi'ah through the delayed exchange of identical benefits; if executed, the party using the benefit must pay the rental equivalent in the relied-upon narration.

Hiring a Partner for Jointly Owned Work
Rulings on hiring a partner to perform work on shared property or for mutual benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a partner to perform work on jointly owned property and distinguish valid from invalid cases based on the nature of the work.

Core Idea
A lease to a partner to perform work on joint property is invalid if the work cannot be physically divided — no wage is due.

The Hanafi school is known for its strict requirement that the subject matter of a lease be deliverable. When the lessor and lessee are co-owners of the property, a unique problem arises: the work to be done is physically inseparable from each partner's share. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and its rationale through several illustrative cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core case and ruling
Read the opening statement: if a partner hires his partner to carry food that belongs to both of them, there is no wage. Note that the ruling is absolute – no named wage nor rental equivalent.
2
Understand the rationale
The contract is invalid because the subject matter (carrying half in common) is physically impossible. A physical act cannot be divided into undivided shares – every part carried involves both partners.
The analogy to prohibited acts with a jointly owned slave girl (intercourse, striking) reinforces the idea that physical acts cannot be apportioned to a share.
3
Compare with analogous valid cases
Contrast the invalid case with valid ones: hiring a jointly owned house to place food (benefit is realized without needing divided delivery), or hiring a jointly owned slave to sew a shirt (the work is a legal entity assignable to the common share).
These show that if the benefit is intangible or can be delivered without dividing the physical act, the lease is valid.
4
Note intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the partner actually uses the property (e.g., occupies the house), rental equivalent is due – but the contract remains invalid. Imam al-Shafi'i permits such leases entirely.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi – no wage unless use, Shafi'i – wage per contract.
5
Apply the ruling to other cases
Study the cases from 'Uyun and al-Nawadir: hiring a jointly owned animal for common transport invalid; hiring a sack or ship for one's own goods valid. The fatwa follows 'Uyun.
The key principle: if the work is for both partners, invalid; if for the hiring partner alone, valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن استأجره لحمل طعام بينهما فلا أجر) يعني لو استأجر أحد الشريكين صاحبه لحمل طعام بينهما لا يستحق المسمى ولا أجر المثل لأن العقد ورد على ما لا يمكن تسليمه لأن المعقود عليه حمل النصف شائعاً وذلك غير لأن الحمل فعل حسي لا يمكن وجوده في الشائع، ولهذا يحرم وطء الجارية المشتركة وضربها، وإذا لم ينعقد لم يجب الأجر أصلاً، ولأنه ما من جزء يحمله إلا وهو شريكه فيه بخلاف ما لو استأجر داراً مشتركة بينه وبين غيره ليضع فيها الطعام حيث يجوز لأن المعقود عليه المنفعة ويستحق بتحقق تسليمها بدون وضع الطعام وبخلاف العبد المشترك حيث يجوز استئجاره ليخيط له قميصاً لكن المعقود عليه إنما هو نصيب الأجر وهو أمر حكمي يمكن إيقاعه في الشائع، وبخلاف إجارة المشاع عند الإمام حيث يجب فيها أجر المثل لأن فساد العقد للعجز عن التسليم وإذا سكن تبين عدمه. وقال الإمام الشافعي : يجوز. وفي العيون والكبرى : كل شيء استأجره أحدهما من صاحبه مما يكون العمل فيه لهما فإنه لا يجوز، فإن عمل فلا أجر له، وذلك مثل الدابة يعني لو استأجر دابة مشتركة لحمل طعام بينهما فلا أجر له. وكل شيء استأجره أحدهما من صاحبه مما لا يكون العلم فيه لهما فهو جائز نحو الجوالق والسفينة والدار قال فخر الدين والفتوى على ما ذكر في العيون. وفي النوادر: استأجر رجلين ليحملا له هذه الحنطة إلى منزله بدرهم فحملها أحدهما فله نصف الدرهم وهو متطوع إذا لم يكونا شريكين قبل العمل وكذا إذا استأجرهما لبناء حائط أو حفر بئر، فلو كانا شريكين في العمل يجب الأجر كله ويكون بينهما. وفي الأصل: استأجر قوماً ليحفروا له سرداباً إجارة صحيحة فعملوا وتعاونوا في العمل؛ إن كان يسيراً قسم الأجر بينهما على عدد الروؤس، وإن كان فاحشاً يقسم على قدر العمل وإن لم يعمل أحدهما لمرض أو عذر سقطت حصته. وفي الغياثية لرجل بيت على نهر فجاء آخر بحجر ومتاعها فوضعهما في البيت واشتركا على أن يطحنا حبوب الناس، فما حصل قسماه نصفين جاز وهو شركة التقبل وليس للبيت والمتاع أجر. قال رحمه الله : كراهن استأجر الرهن من المرتهن يعني لا يجوز استئجار الشريك هنا
He (the author) said: (If he hires him to carry food shared between them, there is no wage.) Meaning if one partner hires his partner to carry food that is between them, he does not deserve the named wage nor the rental equivalent because the contract is based on what cannot be delivered, for the subject matter is carrying half in common, and that is not possible because carrying is a physical act that cannot exist in a common share. For this reason, intercourse with a jointly owned slave girl and striking her are prohibited. If the contract does not conclude, no wage is due at all. Also, there is no part he carries except that he is his partner in it, unlike if he hires a jointly owned house between him and another to place food therein, where it is permissible because the subject matter is the benefit and its delivery is realized without placing food. Unlike a jointly owned slave hired to sew a shirt for him, but the subject matter is the share of work, which is a legal matter that can be placed in the common share. Unlike the lease of an undivided share according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) where rental equivalent is required because the contract is invalid due to inability to deliver, but after occupation it becomes clear that inability does not exist. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible. In al-'Uyun and al-Kubra: Everything that one hires from his partner where the work is for both of them is not permissible, and if he works, there is no wage for him, such as hiring a jointly owned animal to carry food between them, so there is no wage for him. Everything that one hires from his partner where the work is not for both of them is permissible, such as a sack, ship, or house. Fakhr al-Din said: The fatwa is based on what is mentioned in al-'Uyun. In al-Nawadir: He hired two men to carry this wheat to his house for a dirham, and one carried it; he gets half the dirham and is a volunteer if they were not partners before the work. Similarly, if he hires them to build a wall or dig a well, if they were partners in the work, the entire wage is required and divided between them. In al-Asl: He hired a group to dig a cellar for him, a valid lease; they worked and cooperated; if it is small, the wage is divided by heads; if large, by proportion of work; if one did not work due to illness or excuse, his share falls. In al-Ghiyathiyya: A man had a house on a river; another came with a stone and its belongings, placed them in the house, and they partnered to grind people's grain; whatever they earn is divided half and half; this is permissible as a partnership of acceptance, and there is no rent for the house and belongings. He (the author) said: Like a mortgagor hiring the mortgage from the mortgagee, meaning it is not permissible to hire a partner here.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage addresses the invalidity of hiring a partner to carry out work on property that is jointly owned by both. The central case: one partner hires the other to carry food that belongs to both. The lease is invalid because the subject matter (carrying a specific half) is impossible to deliver physically. The act of carrying cannot be divided into shares. Several analogies are compared: hiring a jointly owned house is valid because the benefit (conveyance of space) is realized without needing divided delivery; hiring a jointly owned slave to sew a shirt is valid because the work is a legal entity that can be assigned to the common share. However, Imam Abu Hanifa considers even the lease of an undivided share (مشاع) invalid but requires rental equivalent if used, because the original inability to deliver is disproven by use. Imam al-Shafi'i considers such leases valid. The passage then cites various cases: hiring an animal for common transport is invalid; hiring a sack or ship for one's own goods is valid. Fatwa is according to 'Uyun. Additional cases from Nawadir and Asl discuss division of wages among multiple workers, and a partnership for grinding grain. The final point analogizes hiring a partner to a mortgagor hiring the mortgage from the mortgagee, which is also invalid. The passage shows the Hanafi emphasis on the physical possibility of delivery in lease contracts, especially when the subject matter is a common share.

Key Terms
شائع (sha'i'): Undivided share; common property that is not physically partitioned.
إجارة المشاع (ijarat al-musha'): Lease of an undivided share of property (e.g., a house or animal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one partner hires his partner to carry a bag of grain that belongs to both of them, what is the ruling in the Hanafi school?
A) The lease is valid and the hired partner is entitled to the named wage.
B) The lease is valid but only rental equivalent is due.
C) The lease is invalid and no wage is owed at all.
D) The lease is valid only if the grain is divided before transport.

Key Takeaway
A partner cannot be hired to perform a physical act on jointly owned property if the benefit is shared; the lease is invalid and no wage is owed.

Hiring a Partner to Carry Shared Food – Void Contract
Ruling with proof on void ijarah for carrying shared food

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a partner to carry jointly owned food and explain the reasoning based on the impossibility of delivering an undivided physical act.

Core Idea
A contract to carry an undivided share is void because physical acts cannot be allocated to a specific part; no wage is due.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi contract law: one partner hires the other to carry food they jointly own. The Hanafi school holds this contract void (batil) because the object of the contract—carrying an undivided half—is impossible to deliver. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling, how it distinguishes physical acts from legal benefits, and compare it to the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is one partner hiring the other to carry food that is jointly owned. The Hanafi ruling states the contract is void (batil) and no wage is due, not even market wage (ujrat al-mithl).
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The text gives two proofs: (a) the contract is upon something impossible to deliver (carrying half of an undivided share), and (b) an analogy to the prohibition of intercourse with a jointly owned slave girl – both are physical acts that cannot be confined to a specific share.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) drawing on a general principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the ruling is derived)
The impossibility (adam al-qabd) makes the contract void ab initio. Since the object is undefined and physical, delivery is impossible. No wage is due because a void contract creates no obligations.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Imam al-Shafi'i holds the contract is valid and the named wage is due. Within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa's view is that the contract is void and even market wage is not owed, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad agree on the main ruling but differ on some details regarding market wage for hiring undivided property.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the contract is void and no wage is due, as affirmed by al-Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities.
Authority: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (وإن استأجره لحمل طعام بينهما فلا أجر يعني لو استأجر أحد الشريكين صاحبه لحمل طعام بينهما لا يستحق المسمى ولا أجر المثل لأن العقد ورد على ما لا يمكن تسليمه لأن المعقود عليه حمل النصف شائعاً وذلك غير لأن الحمل فعل حسي لا يمكن وجوده في الشائع، ولهذا يحرم وطء الجارية المشتركة وضربها، وإذا لم ينعقد لم يجب الأجر أصلاً، ولأنه ما من جزء يحمله إلا وهو شريكه فيه بخلاف ما لو استأجر داراً مشتركة بينه وبين غيره ليضع فيها الطعام حيث يجوز لأن المعقود عليه المنفعة ويستحق بتحقق تسليمها بدون وضع الطعام وبخلاف العبد المشترك حيث يجوز استئجاره ليخيط له قميصاً لكن المعقود عليه إنما هو نصيب الأجر وهو أمر حكمي يمكن إيقاعه في الشائع، وبخلاف إجارة المشاع عند الإمام حيث يجب فيها أجر المثل لأن فساد العقد للعجز عن التسليم وإذا سكن تبين عدمه. وقال الإمام الشافعي : يجوز. وفي العيون والكبرى : كل شيء استأجره أحدهما من صاحبه مما يكون العمل فيه لهما فإنه لا يجوز، فإن عمل فلا أجر له، وذلك مثل الدابة يعني لو استأجر دابة مشتركة لحمل طعام بينهما فلا أجر له. وكل شيء استأجره أحدهما من صاحبه مما لا يكون العلم فيه لهما فهو جائز نحو الجوالق والسفينة والدار قال فخر الدين والفتوى على ما ذكر في العيون. وفي النوادر: استأجر رجلين ليحملا له هذه الحنطة إلى منزله بدرهم فحملها أحدهما فله نصف الدرهم وهو متطوع إذا لم يكونا شريكين قبل العمل وكذا إذا استأجرهما لبناء حائط أو حفر بئر، فلو كانا شريكين في العمل يجب الأجر كله ويكون بينهما. وفي الأصل: استأجر قوماً ليحفروا له سرداباً إجارة صحيحة فعملوا وتعاونوا في العمل؛ إن كان يسيراً قسم الأجر بينهما على عدد الروؤس، وإن كان فاحشاً يقسم على قدر العمل وإن لم يعمل أحدهما لمرض أو عذر سقطت حصته. وفي الغياثية لرجل بيت على نهر فجاء آخر بحجر ومتاعها فوضعهما في البيت واشتركا على أن يطحنا حبوب الناس، فما حصل قسماه نصفين جاز وهو شركة التقبل وليس للبيت والمتاع أجر.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he hires him to carry food between them, then there is no wage) meaning if one of the two partners hires his companion to carry food between them, he does not deserve the named wage nor the market wage because the contract came upon what cannot be delivered, because the object of contract is carrying half in an undivided share, and that is impossible because carrying is a physical act that cannot exist in an undivided share; for this reason, sexual intercourse with a jointly owned slave girl and beating her are prohibited. And if it does not contract, no wage is due at all, and because there is no part he carries except that his partner is his partner in it, unlike if he hired a jointly owned house between him and another to place food in it, which is permissible because the object of contract is the benefit and it becomes due by the realization of its delivery without placing food, and unlike a jointly owned slave where hiring him to sew a shirt is permissible, but the object of contract is only the share of the wage, which is a legal matter that can occur in an undivided share, and unlike hiring of undivided property according to the Imam where market wage is obligatory because the corruption of the contract is due to inability to deliver, and if he resides it becomes clear that it is not. Imam al-Shafi'i said: it is permissible. And in al-Uyun and al-Kubra: Everything that one of them hires from his companion where the work is for both of them, then it is not permissible; if he works, then no wage for him; that is like the animal, meaning if he hired a jointly owned animal to carry food between them, then no wage for him. And everything that one of them hires from his companion where the work is not for both of them, then it is permissible, like the sack, the ship, and the house. Fakhr al-Din said: the fatwa is on what is mentioned in al-Uyun. And in al-Nawadir: He hired two men to carry this wheat to his house for a dirham; one of them carried it, so he deserves half a dirham and he is a volunteer if they were not partners before the work; similarly if he hired them to build a wall or dig a well. If they were partners in the work, the entire wage is obligatory and it is between them. And in al-Asl: He hired some people to dig a cellar for him with a valid contract; they worked and cooperated in the work; if it is light, the wage is divided among them according to heads; if it is heavy, it is divided according to the work; and if one of them did not work due to illness or excuse, his share falls. And in al-Ghiyathiyyah: A man had a house on a river; another came with a stone and his goods and placed them in the house and they partnered on condition that they would grind people's grain; what they get they divide equally; it is permissible and it is a partnership of acceptance, and there is no wage for the house and goods.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the chapter on invalid hire (ijarah fasidah). The author explains the matn ruling: if one partner hires the other partner to carry food that is jointly owned, the contract is void and no wage is owed, not even the market wage (ujrat al-mithl). The reason is that the object of contract (the carrying of an undivided share) is impossible to deliver because carrying is a physical act that cannot be allocated to a specific undivided share. The author analogizes this to the prohibition of having intercourse with a jointly owned slave girl or beating her, as those acts cannot be restricted to one's share. The author then distinguishes this from valid scenarios: hiring a jointly owned house to place food (valid because the benefit is delivered regardless), hiring a jointly owned slave to sew a shirt (valid because the object is the wage share, not the physical act), and the case of hiring undivided property where Imam Abu Hanifa requires market wage because the contract's defect (inability to deliver) is removed once possession occurs. The passage also reports al-Shafi'i's opposing view that such a contract is valid. The author then cites supporting texts: al-Uyun and al-Kubra affirm the prohibition for cases where the work benefits both, and allow cases where it does not (like a sack or ship). Al-Nawadir gives an example of hiring two unrelated men to carry wheat; only the carrier gets half the wage. Al-Asl discusses hiring a group to dig a cellar: wages are divided by heads for light work, by effort for heavy work; if one cannot work, his share drops. Al-Ghiyathiyyah discusses a partnership of grinding grain using one party's house and the other's equipment; no rent is due for those assets.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The market rate wage for similar work, owed in cases of invalid contracts where work was performed.
شائع (shā'i‘): An undivided share in jointly owned property; cannot be physically separated.
باطل (bāṭil): Void; a contract that never comes into existence legally because of an essential defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the contract is fāsid and market wage is only for ṣaḥīḥ contracts.
B) Because the object of contract (carrying half of an undivided share) is impossible to deliver, making the contract void.
C) Because the partner is a volunteer and must intend gift.
D) Because the other partner is not liable for his own property.

Key Takeaway
Hiring a partner to carry jointly owned property is void because physical acts cannot be divided; no wage is due.

Mortgagor Hiring Mortgaged Property from Mortgagee
Analogical reasoning: invalidity of mortgagor hiring from mortgagee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mortgagor cannot validly hire mortgaged property from the mortgagee and identify the requirement of ownership for a valid hire contract.

Core Idea
Only the owner can transfer usufruct; a mortgagee in possession cannot let because ownership is essential.

In this passage, the author draws an analogy to illustrate the invalidity of a partner hiring property from another partner. The key is that the person who lets the property must be the owner. The mortgagee is not the owner, so the contract is void. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mortgagor hiring the mortgaged property from the mortgagee. The ruling is that this contract is invalid (batil).
The ruling is explicit: لا يجوز (not permissible).
2
Determine the reason for invalidity
The mortgagee does not own the property; he only holds it as security. Ownership is a prerequisite for transferring usufruct (tamlīk al-manāfi‘) in a hire contract.
تمليك المنافع requires ownership; a non-owner cannot grant it.
3
Apply the consequence to the mortgagor
The mortgagor is the owner; if he benefits from his own property, he cannot be charged rent. Paying rent for one's own property is contradictory.
The mortgagor's own ownership precludes a rent obligation.
4
Understand the analogical reasoning
The author compares this to a partner hiring property from another partner. In both cases, the person letting lacks full ownership of the usufruct, making the contract void.
Analogy (qiyās) is used to extend the same ruling.
5
State the general principle
A hire contract (ijāra) is valid only if the lessor has the right to transfer the usufruct, i.e., ownership or authorized agency. Possession alone is insufficient.
This principle applies across all hire contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : كراهن استأجر الرهن من المرتهن يعني لا يجوز استئجار الشريك هنا كما لا يجوز في مسألة الراهن لأنه ملكه والمرتهن ليس لمالك حتى يؤجره فلا يتأتى منه تمليك المنافع بعوض لأن التمليك من غير المالك محال، والراهن إنما يمكن من الانتفاع من حيث إنه ملكه، ومن انتفع بملك نفسه لا أجرة عليه.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: Like a mortgagor hiring the mortgaged property from the mortgagee, meaning it is not permissible for the partner to hire here, just as it is not permissible in the case of the mortgagor, because (the property) is his property and the mortgagee is not the owner so as to let it out; therefore, transferring ownership of benefits for compensation cannot occur from him because transfer from a non-owner is impossible. The mortgagor can only benefit insofar as it is his property, and one who benefits from his own property owes no rent.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a comparison made in the sharh to illustrate the ruling on hiring by a partner. The author draws an analogy with the case of a mortgagor (rāhin) who cannot validly hire the mortgaged property from the mortgagee (murtahin). The reason is that the mortgagee is not the owner, so he cannot transfer the benefit of the property in exchange for rent. Ownership is a prerequisite for validly letting property. The mortgagor, though he is the owner, cannot be made to pay rent for using his own property. Therefore, the contract is invalid.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): Mortgage; a contract where property is given as security for a debt, with possession transferred to the creditor (mortgagee).
تمليك المنافع (tamlīk al-manāfi‘): Transfer of ownership of benefits (usufruct), which is the essence of a hire contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid for a mortgagor to hire the mortgaged property from the mortgagee?
A) Because the mortgagee does not own the property and cannot transfer its benefits.
B) Because the mortgagor cannot pay rent on his own property.
C) Both A and B.
D) Because the contract must be in writing.

Key Takeaway
A hire contract is invalid if the lessor does not own the property; the mortgagee, being a mere possessor, cannot validly let the mortgaged property.

Hiring an Animal Without Specifying Load: Liability and Validity
Ruling on hiring an animal without specifying the load

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring an animal without specifying the load, explain when the hirer is liable for the animal's death, and identify the conditions under which the contract becomes valid.

Core Idea
A corrupt hire treats the animal as a trust; death without transgression means no liability, and reaching the destination cures the defect.

Imagine you hire a donkey to carry goods to Mecca but forget to specify exactly what you'll load. What happens if the donkey dies on the way? Under Hanafi fiqh, the answer depends on whether you used the animal normally or abused it. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the ruling, emphasizing the concepts of trust (amānah) and transgression (ta‘addī), and shows how the contract can become valid upon successful completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial contract status
The hire contract is initially corrupt (fāsid) because the load is unspecified (jahālah). This defect does not make the contract void; it retains some validity.
In Hanafi law, a fāsid contract is one that is valid in essence but has a defect in description; it can become valid if the defect is removed.
2
Understand the animal's status as trust
Even in a corrupt hire, the animal is considered a trust (amānah) in the hirer's hands. This means the hirer is not liable for accidental death unless he transgresses (ta‘addī).
Transgression includes overloading, mistreatment, or using the animal in a way not customary.
3
Analyze liability conditions
If the animal dies without transgression (e.g., carrying a normal load), the hirer is not liable. If he transgresses, he becomes liable for the animal's value and forfeits the wage.
The phrase 'so he is not liable as long as he does not transgress' is key.
4
Recognize when the contract becomes valid
If the animal reaches Mecca, the contract becomes valid (sahīh) because the load becomes specified by actual carriage, removing the cause of corruption.
This is analogous to land rental where actual use specifies the benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن استأجر حماراً إلى مكة ولم يسم ما يحمل فحمل ما يحمل الناس فنفق لم يضمن لأن العين أمانة في يده وإن كانت الإجارة فاسدة لأن الفاسد يعتبر بالصحيح لكونه مشروعاً من وجه فلا يضمن ما لم يتعدى، فإذا تعدى ضمن ولا أجر عليه. قال رحمه الله : (وإن بلغ مكة فله المسمى لأن الفساد كان لجهالة ما يحمل فإذا حمل عليه شيئاً تعين ذلك فانقلب صحيحاً لزوال الموجب للفساد.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he hires a donkey to Mecca and does not specify what he will carry, then he carries what people carry and it dies, he is not liable because the property is a trust in his hand even if the hire is corrupt, because the corrupt is treated like the valid in being legislated in some respect, so he is not liable as long as he does not transgress. If he transgresses, he is liable and there is no wage for him. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if he reaches Mecca, he gets the named rent because the corruption was due to ignorance of what he would carry; when he carries something, it becomes specified, so it turns valid due to removal of the cause of corruption.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings. First, if a person hires a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load, and the donkey dies while carrying what people normally carry, the hirer is not liable. This is because the animal is held as a trust (amānah) in his hands, and the corrupt contract is still considered legislated in some respects (mashrū‘ min wajh), so no liability arises without transgression (ta‘addī). If the hirer overloads or mistreats the animal, he becomes liable (ḍāmin) and forfeits his wage. Second, if the animal reaches Mecca safely, the hirer owes the named rent. The original corruption was due to ignorance of the load; once actual loading occurs, the load is specified and the ignorance is removed, causing the contract to become valid. This parallels the previous ruling on land rental, where actual use cures the defect.

Key Terms
أمانة (amānah): A trust; the hired animal in a corrupt contract is still considered a trust, so the hirer is not liable for accidental death unless negligent.
تعدي (ta‘addī): Transgression or misuse beyond the terms of the contract, triggering liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of hiring a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load, if the donkey dies on the way while carrying a customary load, what is the ruling?
A) The hirer is liable (ḍāmin) and must pay compensation.
B) The hirer is not liable because the animal is a trust.
C) The hirer must pay the named rent even though the animal died.
D) The contract is void and no liability or wage arises.

Key Takeaway
In a corrupt hire, the animal is an amānah; no liability for normal death, but transgression triggers liability and forfeits the wage, while arrival at the destination validates the contract.

Land Lease Without Specifying Crop: Valid After Planting by Istihsan
Commentary on curing lease defect after planting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a land lease where no crop is specified and explain how istihsan cures the defect after planting.

Core Idea
Land lease without crop specification is invalid initially, but becomes valid by istihsan once the lessee plants.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract requires clarity of the subject matter. Renting land without specifying what crop will be planted creates ignorance (jahala) that renders the contract fasid. However, if the lessee actually plants and the lease term ends, the defect is cured by istihsan. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and the conditions for its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
State the default Hanafi ruling for a land lease where the crop type is not specified. The contract is fasid (invalid) because the subject matter is unknown, leading to potential dispute.
The text says 'لا يجوز العقد حتى يبين ما يزرع' – the contract is not permissible until the crop is specified.
2
Trace the cure by istihsan
When the lessee plants and the term expires, the contract becomes valid by istihsan. Istihsan overrides strict analogy (qiyas) because the jahala is removed before the lease ends, eliminating the cause of dispute.
The key phrase: 'الجاز استحساناً لأن الجهالة ارتفعت قبل تمام العقد'
3
Analyze the objection and response
The text considers an objection: even if ignorance is removed, the possibility of planting a harmful crop remains. The response: contracts should be upheld as much as possible; the prevention (dispute) disappears once the benefits are received.
From al-Nihayah: 'الأصل إجازة العقد عند انتفاء المانع'
4
Determine the wage outcome
If the contract becomes valid, the named wage (al-musamma) is due. But if a judge has already annulled the contract before planting, the fair wage (ajr al-mithl) applies instead.
From Ghayat al-Bayan: 'ويجب المسمى إذا لم يكن ذلك بعد نقض القاضي العقد'
5
Distinguish from repeated rulings
The commentary notes that this ruling appears similar to earlier statements but differs: the earlier discussion was about valid contracts (from Kanz), while this passage deals with invalid contracts that can become valid.
Al-Akmal clarifies the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استأجر أرضاً ولم يذكر أنه يزرعها أو أي شيء يزرعها فزرعها فمضى الأجل فله المسمى لأن الأرض تؤجر للزراعة ولغيرها من البناء والمراح ونصب الخيم، وكذا ما يزرع فيها يختلف كما تقدم فلا يجوز العقد حتى يبين ما يزرع ويبين جنسه. وإذا زرع ومضى الأجل جاز استحساناً لأن الجهالة ارتفعت قبل تمام العقد فينقلب جائزاً. قال صاحب العناية في حل قوله قبل تمام العقد ينقض الحكم أقول لا يخفى على ذي تأمل أن جعل العقد تاماً ينقض الحكم مما لا تقبله الفطرة السليمة فإن العقد ينفسخ من الأصل بنقض الحاكم إياه فكيف يتصور أن تتم به وتمام الشيء من أثر بقائه به؟ والحق أن المراد بقوله قبل تمام «العقد قبل تمام مدة العقد قال في النهاية : فإن قيل إذا ارتفعت الجهالة بمجرد الزراعة لم يرتفع ما هو الموجب للفساد وهو احتمال أن يزرع فيها ما يضر بالأرض، فكيف ينقلب إلى الجواز بتحقق شيء احتماله مفسد للعقد؟ ولأن المعقود عليه إذا كان مجهولاً لا يتعين إلا بتعيينهما صوناً عن الإضرار بالآخر ولا ينفرد به أحدهما؟ قلت : الأصل إجازة العقد عند انتفاء المانع لأن العقود تصح بقدر الإمكان والمانع الذي فسد العقد باعتباره توقع المنازعة بينهما وعند استيفاء المنافع يزول هذا .اهـ. وفي غاية البيان: ويجب المسمى إذا لم يكن ذلك بعد نقض القاضي العقد .اهـ. وفي بعض النسخ قيل: وهذا تحريف من الكاتب يعني إذا كان بعده فله أجر المثل، لا يقال هذه المسألة متكررة مع قوله والأرض للزراعة أن بين ما يزرع لأنا نقول : : الأول باعتبار ما يصح من العقود وذكرها هنا باعتبار ما يفسد من العقود. قال الأكمل : لا يقال هذه المسألة متكررة مع ما ذكره أول الباب لأن ذلك وضع القدوري وهذا وضع الجامع الصغير يشتمل على زيادة قوله فله» يشير إلى أنه انعقد فاسداً وزال الفساد بالزرع على ما فيه .
And whoever rents a land and does not mention that he will cultivate it or what crop he will plant, then he cultivates it, and the term expires, then he gets the named wage because land is rented for cultivation and for other purposes like building, stable, and pitching tents. Similarly, what is planted in it varies as mentioned earlier, so the contract is not valid until he specifies what he will plant and its type. And when he plants and the term expires, it becomes valid by istihsan because the ignorance was removed before the completion of the contract, so it becomes valid. The author of al-`Inayah said in explaining his statement 'before the completion of the contract' it invalidates the ruling. I say: It is not hidden from one who reflects that making the contract complete invalidates the ruling, which sound nature does not accept, because the contract is annulled from its origin by the judge's annulment, so how can it be conceived that it is completed by it? The completion of something is an effect of its remaining? The truth is that what is meant by his statement 'before completion' is before the completion of the term of the contract. He said in al-Nihayah: If it is said: If the ignorance is removed merely by cultivation, what causes the corruption has not been removed, which is the possibility that he might plant something harmful to the land. So how does it turn to validity by something whose probability corrupts the contract? And because the subject matter of the contract, when unknown, is not determined except by the specification of both parties to protect from harming the other, and one party cannot solely determine it? I say: The principle is to permit the contract when there is no prevention, because contracts are valid as much as possible, and the prevention that caused the contract to be corrupt is the anticipation of dispute between them. And when the benefits are received, this disappears. End quote. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: The named wage is obligatory if that is not after the judge's annulment of the contract. End quote. And in some copies it is said: This is a corruption by the scribe, meaning if it is after it, then he gets the fair wage. It is not said that this issue is repeated with his statement: The land is for cultivation? Because we say: The first is with regard to valid contracts, and it is mentioned here with regard to invalid contracts. Al-Akmal said: It is not said that this issue is repeated with what was mentioned at the beginning of the chapter because that is the placement of al-Quduri, and this is the placement of al-Jami` al-Saghir, which includes the addition of his statement 'so he gets it', indicating that it was concluded as corrupt and the corruption was removed by cultivation according to what it contains.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It addresses a lease of land where the lessee does not specify what crop he will plant. Initially, such a lease is invalid (fasid) due to ignorance (jahala) about the subject matter. However, the text explains that if the lessee actually plants and the lease term expires, the contract becomes valid by istihsan. This is because the ignorance is removed once the planting occurs, and the potential for dispute (the reason for declaring the contract invalid) is eliminated. The commentary addresses objections about the timing of this 'completion' and the possibility that the lessee might plant something harmful. The author of al-`Inayah clarifies that 'before completion' refers to before the end of the lease term, not before the contract is annulled by a judge. The text from al-Nihayah argues that the contract should be upheld because the prevention (the possibility of dispute) disappears once the benefits are received. The commentary also notes that the named wage (al-musamma) is due unless the judge has already annulled the contract, in which case the fair wage (ajr al-mithl) is due.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijara fasida): A defective lease contract that lacks a necessary condition, rendering it invalid but potentially rectifiable.
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) to achieve a more equitable outcome.
جهالة (jahala): Ignorance or ambiguity regarding the subject matter of a contract, which renders the contract invalid if it leads to potential dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of the lessee planting a crop and the term expiring in a land lease where the crop was not specified?
A) The contract remains fasid and the named wage is void.
B) The contract becomes valid by istihsan and the named wage is due.
C) The contract becomes valid but only the fair wage is due.
D) The contract becomes batil and no wage is due.

Key Takeaway
A land lease without crop specification is initially fasid, but becomes valid by istihsan once the lessee plants and the term expires, entitling the lessor to the named rent unless the contract was previously annulled by a judge.

Donkey Hire Without Specifying Load: Liability and Wage
Commentary on rulings for a lease of a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability and wage for a defective lease of a donkey when the load is unspecified and then specified by action, and explain the underlying legal reasoning (istihsan).

Core Idea
A defective lease becomes valid once the unknown term is determined, and the lessee is not liable for the animal's death unless he transgresses.

In Hanafi fiqh, a lease contract that lacks a necessary condition (such as specifying the load) is considered defective (fasid). However, this does not mean it is entirely without effect. This lesson examines two scenarios from the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq: one where the donkey dies, and one where it reaches its destination. You will learn how the defective contract is treated like a valid one in terms of trust, and how the defect can be cured by subsequent action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) the donkey dies after being loaded with a typical load, and (2) the donkey safely reaches Mecca. Note the different rulings for each.
The first scenario concerns liability for loss; the second concerns entitlement to the wage.
2
Analyze the ruling on death: no liability
The text rules that the lessee is not liable (la yadman) for the donkey's death. This is because the animal is held as a trust (amanah) in the lessee's hands. Even though the lease is defective, the defective contract is considered like a valid one in terms of the obligation to safeguard the property.
The lessee only becomes liable if he transgresses (ta'addi) by overloading or mistreating the animal.
3
Understand the legal basis for the second ruling: wage is due
If the donkey reaches Mecca, the lessee must pay the named wage (al-musamma). The original defect was ignorance (jahala) of the load. Once the lessee loads a specific load, that ignorance is removed, and the contract becomes valid (sahih) retroactively.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not strict analogy.
4
Recognize the underlying principle of istihsan
The text uses the principle that a defective contract is treated like a valid one insofar as it is legally sanctioned (mashru' min wajh). The removal of the defect by subsequent action makes the contract valid, similar to how ignorance is cured in a land lease analogy.
This istihsan overrides the general rule that a defective contract does not entitle to a wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن استأجر حماراً إلى مكة ولم يسم ما يحمل فحمل ما يحمل الناس فنفق لم يضمن لأن العين أمانة في يده وإن كانت الإجارة فاسدة لأن الفاسد يعتبر بالصحيح لكونه مشروعاً من وجه فلا يضمن ما لم يتعدى، فإذا تعدى ضمن ولا أجر عليه. قال رحمه الله : (وإن بلغ مكة فله المسمى لأن الفساد كان لجهالة ما يحمل فإذا حمل عليه شيئاً تعين ذلك فانقلب صحيحاً لزوال الموجب للفساد.
And if he rents a donkey to Mecca and does not specify what it will carry, then he loads it with what people usually load, and it dies, he does not guarantee because the thing is a trust in his hand even though the lease is defective, because the defective is considered like the valid in that it is legally sanctioned in some respect, so he does not guarantee unless he transgresses. If he transgresses, he guarantees and owes no wage. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And if he reaches Mecca, he gets the named wage because the defect was due to ignorance of what it carries, so when he loads something on it, that becomes determined, and it becomes valid due to the removal of the cause of corruption.)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings regarding a lease of a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load. First, if the donkey dies after being loaded with a typical load, the lessee is not liable (la yadman) because the animal is considered a trust (amanah) in his possession. Even though the lease is defective (fasid), a defective contract is treated like a valid one in terms of the obligation to safeguard the property; the lessee is only liable if he transgresses (ta'addi). Second, if the donkey reaches Mecca, the lessee must pay the named wage (al-musamma) because the defect (ignorance of the load) is removed once he actually loads it, making the contract valid. This follows the same principle as the land lease: the ignorance is cured by action.

Key Terms
أمانة (amanah): A trust; property held by someone who is not liable for its loss unless negligence occurs.
إجارة فاسدة (ijara fasida): A defective lease contract that is legally recognized in terms of entitlement to wages but lacks a necessary condition.
جهالة (jahala): Ignorance or uncertainty about an essential term of the contract, which renders it defective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person rents a donkey to Mecca without specifying the load, and the donkey dies after being loaded with a typical load, what is the ruling?
A) The lessee must pay full compensation.
B) The lessee is not liable because the animal is a trust.
C) The lessee is liable only for the named wage.
D) The lessee is liable if the load was unusual.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a defective lease of a donkey without specifying the load does not impose liability on the lessee for the animal's accidental death, but if the animal reaches the destination, the lessee must pay the agreed wage because the contract becomes valid once the load is determined.

Denial of Lease During Journey: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage liability after denial of lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the effect of denying a lease during a journey and explain the legal reasoning behind each view.

Core Idea
A lessee who denies the lease becomes a usurper — but does that cancel the remaining wage? Two Hanafi giants disagree.

When a lessee denies the lease while still using the animal, does the denial cancel the wage obligation for the remaining journey? Abu Yusuf argues that after denial the lessee is a usurper, so no wage is due; Muhammad holds that the contract remains in effect, so full wage is owed. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the underlying principle that wage and guarantee cannot coexist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Read the passage and identify the scenario: a person rents an animal (or similar) and then denies the existence of the lease while still using it during the journey.
The denial (jahd) is the key act that transforms the legal status.
2
State Abu Yusuf's ruling and reasoning
Abu Yusuf rules that only the wage for the portion before the denial is due. After denial, no wage is due because the lessee becomes a usurper (ghasib), and wage and guarantee (daman) cannot be combined.
The principle 'al-ajr wa al-daman la yajtami'ān' is central.
3
State Muhammad's ruling and reasoning
Muhammad rules that the full wage is due for the entire journey. He views the contract as still in effect until it is formally rescinded, so the usage remains based on the lease.
Muhammad's view emphasises the continuity of the contract.
4
Examine the underlying principle
Both agree that if the lessee becomes a usurper, he is strictly liable. The dispute is whether the denial automatically makes him a usurper for the entire remaining period or only from the moment of denial forward.
Abu Yusuf treats the denial as a transformative event; Muhammad treats it as a breach but not a retroactive nullification.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Yusuf, the lessor claims nothing for the post-denial portion; under Muhammad, the lessor can collect full wage. In Hanafi fatwa practice, the view of Abu Yusuf is often given weight in cases involving usurpation.
The tarjih may depend on the context and the strength of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استأجر دابة وجحد الإجارة في أثناء الطريق وجب عليه أجر ما ركب قبل الإنكار، ولا يجب الأجر لما بعده عند أبي يوسف لأنه بالجحود صار غاصباً والأجر والضمان لا يجتمعان. وقال محمد: يجب الأجر كله .اهـ.
And if he rents an animal and denies the lease during the journey, then upon him is the wage for what he rode before the denial, and the wage for after it is not obligatory according to Abu Yusuf because by the denial he becomes a usurper, and wage and guarantee cannot be combined. And Muhammad said: The full wage is obligatory. End quote.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa). The case is a lessee who denies the existence of the lease while still using the animal during the journey. Abu Yusuf rules that the lessee must pay wages only for the portion before the denial, because after the denial he becomes a usurper (ghasib), and wage and guarantee cannot coexist. Muhammad holds that the lessee must pay the full wage for the entire journey. The text does not indicate which view is preferred, but it ends the quote, leaving the discussion open.

Key Terms
جحد الإجارة (jahd al-ijara): Denial of the lease; the lessee's act of disavowing the lease contract.
غاصب (ghasib): A usurper; one who wrongfully takes or uses property without right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal reason (ta'lil) given by Abu Yusuf for not requiring wage after the denial?
A) The contract was void from the start.
B) The lessee became a usurper (ghasib), and wage and guarantee cannot be combined.
C) The lessee is excused due to hardship of journey.
D) The owner failed to assert his right.

Key Takeaway
The denial of a lease transforms the lessee's possession from trust to usurpation, but the effect on wage liability for the remaining period is disputed among Hanafi jurists.

Annulment of a Defective Lease: Obligation Without Dispute
Ruling and commentary on annulment of defective lease

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on annulling a defective lease and explain why annulment is obligatory even without party dispute.

Core Idea
A defective lease must be annulled regardless of dispute—corruption cannot persist.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario in ijara: a lease that is defective due to ignorance (jahala) of the precise object. The text rules on what happens when the parties dispute before the defect is cured by the lessee's action of planting or loading. While the matn mentions annulment only upon dispute, the commentator Ibn Nujaym expands the ruling, arguing that removal of the defective contract is always obligatory. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level? The passage states that if the parties dispute before cultivation or loading, the lease is annulled (naqd). The hukm is annulment to prevent corruption.
The act is the defective lease (ijara fasida) that is still uncured.
2
Understand the defect and its cure
Why is the lease defective? The defect is ignorance (jahala) of the precise benefit—the lessee does not know exactly which land or animal will be used. The cure is the lessee's action of planting or loading, which specifies the object and removes the ignorance.
Before the cure, the contract remains fasid.
3
Analyze the condition of dispute
The matn restricts annulment to the case of dispute (tashah). But the commentator argues that annulment is obligatory in all cases because the contract is inherently defective. Why did the matn mention dispute? Possibly to highlight a common trigger, but the ruling is broader.
Ibn Nujaym says 'it is not hidden that removing the defective is obligatory whether they dispute or not.'
4
Trace the talil (ratio)
The underlying reason (illa) is the persistence of fasad (corruption). As long as the defect remains, the contract cannot be upheld. Annulment is wajib to remove the ongoing invalid state. This is true even if both parties remain silent.
The ruling is tied to the nature of the contract, not the parties' behavior.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that annulment is wajib in all cases—dispute or not. A mufti should order annulment whenever a fasid lease is brought to him, regardless of whether the parties are arguing.
This aligns with the principle that fasid contracts must be nullified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تشاحا قبل الزرع والحمل نقضت الإجارة دفعاً للفساد إذ الفساد باق قبل أن ترتفع الجهالة بالتعيين بالزرع والحمل. فإذا قلت: حكم الإجارة الفاسدة نقضها قبل تمام المدة ووجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال فكان ينبغي أن يقدم على وجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال قلنا : قدم الأجرة لكثرة وقوعها فتأمل. ولا يخفى أن رفع الفاسد واجب سواء تشاحا أو لم يتشاحا فكان عليه أن لا يقيده بذلك، ولو قال «عليهما أن يرفعا العقد لكان أولى لأن رفعه واجب عليهما تشاحا أو لا. والله تعالى أعلم.
And if they dispute before cultivation and loading, the lease is annulled to prevent corruption, because the corruption remains before the ignorance is removed by the specification through cultivation and loading. If you say: The ruling of a defective lease is to annul it before the end of the term and the obligation of wage after use, so it would be more appropriate to present the annulment before the obligation of wage after use. We say: He presented the wage because of its frequent occurrence, so reflect. And it is not hidden that removing the defective is obligatory whether they dispute or not, so he should not have restricted it with that. And if he said 'they must annul the contract' it would be better because its annulment is obligatory on them whether they dispute or not. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a defective lease when the parties dispute before the defect is cured by the lessee's action (planting or loading). In such a case, the lease must be annulled (naqd) to prevent the continued corruption of the contract. The commentator notes that the matn only mentions annulment in case of dispute, but in reality, annulment is obligatory even without dispute because the contract remains invalid. The commentator suggests that the author of the matn should have stated 'they must annul the contract' without restricting it to the case of dispute. The reason given is that the defect (jahala) persists until the lessee actually performs the action that removes it.

Key Terms
تشاح (tashah): Dispute between two parties, here between lessor and lessee.
نقض الإجارة (naqd al-ijara): Annulment of the lease contract, rendering it void ab initio.
إجارة فاسدة (ijara fasida): A lease contract that is corrupt due to a defect in its essential conditions, such as ignorance of the object or rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling according to the commentary if the parties dispute before the lessee has planted or loaded the animal?
A) The contract is upheld and they must reconcile.
B) The contract is annulled to prevent corruption.
C) The lessee can complete the planting and then pay the named wage.
D) The lessor can cancel unilaterally.

Key Takeaway
A defective lease must be annulled — whether the parties dispute or not — because the corruption of ignorance persists until the contract is nullified.

Defining the Common Worker and the Circularity Critique
Definition of the common worker with logical critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi definition of the common worker (ajir mushtarak) and explain the critique of circularity regarding that definition.

Core Idea
The definition of ajir mushtarak must avoid circularity; knowledge of entitlement precedes knowledge of the term.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah introduces the chapter on liability of hired workers. He distinguishes between the special worker (ajir khas) and the common worker (ajir mushtarak), defining the latter as 'one who works for more than one person.' However, a sharp critique emerges: this definition appears circular because it presupposes knowledge of the term being defined. We will explore the definition, the critique, and the attempted response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the matn's definition of the common worker. The text states: 'the common worker is one who works for more than one person and does not deserve wages until he works.'
The definition combines work for multiple persons and delayed entitlement.
2
Understand the two types of workers
Recognize that the hired worker is divided into ajir khas (special) and ajir mushtarak (common). The special worker works exclusively and becomes entitled to wages merely by making himself available.
This distinction affects liability rules.
3
Grasp the circularity critique
The critique argues that the definition of ajir mushtarak as 'one who works for more than one person' is circular because it uses the term 'common worker' implicitly. To understand the definition, one must already know what an ajir mushtarak is.
The critique is logical, not substantive.
4
Analyze the response and counter-critique
Sahib al-Nihayah offers a response: the definition refers to a previously mentioned context about entitlement. However, this response is criticized for admitting circularity and not resolving it.
The passage ends mid-objection, leaving the debate open.
5
Draw the methodological lesson
This discussion shows that legal definitions must be carefully constructed to avoid logical fallacies. Distinguishing between definition by reference and definition by intrinsic properties is key.
This is a lesson in legal methodology (usul).

باب ضمان الأجير من جملة يصح عنون لما فرغ من ذكر أنواع الإجارة صحيحها وفاسدها شرع في بيان الضمان لأنه العوارض التي تترتب على عقد الإجارة فيحتاج إلى بيانها كذا في غاية البيان. ولا يخفى أن الأجير على ضربين خاص ومشترك ؛ فشرع المؤلف يبين ذلك، ولا يخفى أن معنى ضمان الأجير إثباتاً ونفياً ولو لم يكن معناه ذلك بل معناه إثبات الضمان فقط لزم أن لا الباب على قول الإمام أصلاً لأنه لا ضمان عنده على أحد من الأجير المشترك والخاص. قال رحمه الله : (إلا ضمير المشترك من يعمل لغير واحد) قال الأكمل: والسؤال عن وجه تقديم المشترك على الخاص دوري .اهـ يعني أن السؤال عن توجيه تقديم المشترك يتوجه على تقدير العكس فلا مرجح سوى الاختيار . قال صاحب النهاية : فإن قلت : تعريف المشترك بقوله من يعمل لغير واحد تعريف يدل على عاقبته إلى الدور لأن هذا حكم لا يعرفه إلا من يعرف الأجير المشترك، ولو كان عارفاً بالأجير المشترك لا يحتاج إلى هذا التعريف، ولو لم یکن عارفاً به قبل ذلك لا يحصل له تعريف الأجير المشترك لأنه يحتاج إلى السؤال عمن يستحق الأجر حتى يعلم من هو فلا بد للمعرف أن يقول هو الأجير المشترك وهو عين الدور . قلت : نعم هو كذلك إلا أن هذا تعريف للخفي بما هو أشهر منه في مفهوم المتعلمين أو هو تعريف لما لم يذكر بما قد سبق ذكره لأنه ذكر قبل هذا استحقاق الأجير بالعمل بقوله «أو باستيفاء المعقود عليه في باب الأجرة متى تستحق فصار كأنه قال وما عرفته بأن الأجير يستحق الأجر باستيفاء المعقود عليه فهو الأجير المشترك إلى هنا كلامه. واعترض بأن الجواب فيه خلل من أوجه أما أولاً فلأن قوله في أول الجواب نعم كذلك اعتراف بلزوم الدور، وما يستلزم الدور يتعين فساده ولا يمكن إصلاحه وأما ثانياً فلأن كون الأجير هو الذي لا
Chapter on the liability of the hired worker. From the total it is correct to title: When he finished mentioning the types of lease, valid and invalid, he began to explain liability because it is among the incidental matters that arise from the lease contract and it is necessary to explain them. Similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is not hidden that the hired worker is of two types: special and common; so the author began to explain that. And it is not hidden that the meaning of liability of the hired worker is affirmation and negation. If its meaning were not that but rather only affirmation of liability, then it would necessitate that the chapter would not be according to the Imam's statement at all, because there is no liability according to him for either the common or special worker. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (Except the pronoun of the common worker: one who works for more than one person). Al-Akmal said: The question about the reason for giving precedence to the common over the special is circular. End quote. That is, the question about the direction of giving precedence to the common applies in the opposite case, so there is no preference except choice. The author of al-Nihayah said: If you say: The definition of the common worker with his statement 'one who works for more than one person' is a definition that leads to circularity because this ruling is only known by one who knows the common worker. And if he knew the common worker, he would not need this definition. And if he did not know it before, the definition does not give him knowledge of the common worker because he needs to ask about who deserves wages until he knows who it is. So the definer must say 'he is the common worker', which is exactly the circularity. I say: Yes, it is so, except that this is a definition of the hidden by what is more well-known in the students' understanding, or it is a definition of what has not been mentioned by what has already been mentioned because before this he mentioned the entitlement of the worker by work with his statement 'or by receiving the subject matter in the chapter on when wages are due', so it is as if he said: And what you know as the worker deserving wages by receiving the subject matter, that is the common worker. This is his statement. And it was objected that the answer contains weakness in several aspects: First, because his statement at the beginning of the answer 'yes it is so' is an admission of circularity, and whatever necessitates circularity is definitely invalid and cannot be corrected. Second, because the worker is who does not...
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on the liability of the hired worker (daman al-ajir). The author first explains the purpose of the chapter: to discuss the incidental liability issues that arise from lease contracts. The hired worker is divided into two types: the special worker (ajir khas) and the common worker (ajir mushtarak). The matn defines the common worker as 'one who works for more than one person and does not deserve wages until he works, like the launderer.' The commentary then critiques this definition. Al-Akmal notes that the question of why the common worker is defined before the special worker is circular because any answer would presuppose knowledge of the terms. Then Sahib al-Nihayah offers a more detailed criticism: the definition itself is circular because to understand it, one must already know what an ajir mushtarak is. The response given is that this is a definition of the hidden by what is more familiar to students, or it is a reference to a prior statement about entitlement. However, the text then records an objection that this response is flawed because it admits circularity. The passage ends in the middle of the second objection.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common worker who works for multiple persons and does not become entitled to wages until he actually performs the work.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A special worker who works exclusively for one employer and becomes entitled to wages by being available.
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning; a logical fallacy where a definition presupposes the term being defined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the critique in the passage, why is the definition of the common worker as 'one who works for more than one person' problematic?
A) It is too vague and includes too many workers.
B) It is circular because it presupposes knowledge of the term 'common worker'.
C) It contradicts a previous definition.
D) It only applies to launderers.

Key Takeaway
The definition of the common worker must be carefully crafted to avoid circularity; the Hanafi jurists recognized this logical issue in their legal methodology.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Rescinding a Fasid Ijarah Before Plantation
Ruling on fasid ijarah rescission with commentary refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on rescinding a fasid ijarah before use and explain the commentator's refinement regarding the condition of dispute.

Core Idea
A fasid ijarah must be rescinded to remove corruption, even if parties do not dispute.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario in a fasid (defective) ijarah contract for agricultural land. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that if the parties dispute before planting or carrying, the contract is rescinded. The commentator expands on this, explaining that corruption remains until ambiguity is removed, and then refines the condition of dispute, arguing that rescission is obligatory regardless. We will unpack the ruling and the subtle correction made by the commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
Determine what is being ruled upon: a fasid ijarah (defective lease) for agricultural land before the lessee has planted or carried the crop. Classify the contract as fasid (not batil) in Hanafi fiqh.
Fasid means valid in essence but defective in description; it requires rescission if the defect persists.
2
State the ruling from the matn
The matn says: if the parties dispute (tashāḥā) before planting/carrying, the ijarah is rescinded to prevent corruption. Note the condition of dispute.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that corruption remains because the ambiguity (jahālah) in the subject matter has not been removed by actual planting or carrying. Rescission removes the corruption.
Ambiguity in ijarah can make it fasid; once the lessee plants, the specific land is determined and the ambiguity is resolved.
4
Analyze the hypothetical objection and response
An objection: normally a fasid ijarah is rescinded before the term ends, but wages become due after use (here, planting has occurred). So wages should take precedence. The commentator replies: wages are given precedence due to their frequent occurrence, but in this context, rescission is prioritized.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that obligations arising from actual use (ujrah) often override the general rule of rescission, but the text emphasizes rescission here.
5
Evaluate the commentator's refinement
The commentator notes that removing a fasid contract is obligatory whether or not the parties dispute. The matn's wording 'if they dispute' is unnecessary; it would be better to say 'they both must lift the contract'. This is a minor correction (tashīḥ) of the matn.
This shows the depth of fiqh commentary: the commentator not only explains but also refines the base text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ضمان الأجير
وإن تشاحا قبل الزرع والحمل نقضت الإجارة دفعاً للفساد.
قال رحمه الله : (وإن تشاحا قبل الزرع والحمل نقضت الإجارة دفعاً للفساد) إذ الفساد باق قبل أن ترتفع الجهالة بالتعيين بالزرع والحمل. فإذا قلت: حكم الإجارة الفاسدة نقضها قبل تمام المدة ووجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال فكان ينبغي أن يقدم على وجوب الأجرة بعد الاستعمال قلنا : قدم الأجرة لكثرة وقوعها فتأمل. ولا يخفى أن رفع الفاسد واجب سواء تشاحا أو لم يتشاحا فكان عليه أن لا يقيده بذلك، ولو قال «عليهما أن يرفعا العقد لكان أولى لأن رفعه واجب عليهما تشاحا أو لا. والله تعالى أعلم.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter: Guarantee of the Employee. And if they dispute before planting and carrying, the ijarah is rescinded to prevent corruption. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if they dispute before planting and carrying, the ijarah is rescinded to prevent corruption) because the corruption remains before the ambiguity is removed by specifying through planting and carrying. If you say: The ruling of a fasid ijarah is to rescind it before the end of the term and that wages become obligatory after use, so it should be given precedence over the obligation of wages after use. We said: Wages are given precedence due to their frequent occurrence, so reflect. And it is not hidden that removing the corrupted contract is obligatory whether they dispute or not, so he should not have restricted it to that. And if he had said 'they both must lift the contract' it would have been better, because lifting it is obligatory on both, whether they dispute or not. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a fasid (defective) ijarah contract related to agricultural land. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that if the parties dispute before the crop is planted or carried (i.e., before the ambiguity of the subject matter is resolved by actual cultivation), the contract is rescinded to prevent further corruption. The commentator (possibly Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) explains that the corrupt element remains until the ambiguity is removed by actual planting. A potential objection is raised: a fasid contract is normally rescinded before the term ends, but wages become due after use (here, the lessee has used the land by planting), so one might think wages should take precedence. The response is that wages are given precedence because the need for wages arises frequently. The commentator then notes that removing a fasid contract is obligatory regardless of a dispute, so the matn's condition 'if they dispute' is not necessary; it would have been better to say 'they both must lift the contract'.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A lease contract that lacks a condition necessary for its validity (e.g., ambiguity in the subject matter) but is not inherently prohibited.
تشاحا (tashāḥā): Both parties disputing or contending over the contract.
نقض الإجارة (naqḍ al-ijārah): Rescinding or annulling the lease contract before it is fully performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why should the matn not restrict the rescission of fasid ijarah to situations of dispute?
A) Because disputes are rare in such contracts.
B) Because removing a fasid contract is obligatory for both parties regardless of dispute.
C) Because the contract becomes valid after planting even without rescission.
D) Because the lessor alone has the right to rescind.

Key Takeaway
A fasid ijarah must be rescinded by both parties to remove corruption, without needing a dispute between them.
